<p>i)alkaloids: Taste bitter and are poorly absorbed in water but become soluble if dissolved in acids examples of drugs derived from alkaloids includes; atropine, caffeine, cocaine, quinine, codeine and morphine.</p>
<p>Conti.</p>
<p>ii)Glycosides: these are digitalis products e.g. digoxin, digitoxin which are gotten from digitalis purpureal or foxglove plants.</p>
<p>iii)Gums: these are polysaccharides exudates that can be used for bulk laxatives and dental adhesives.</p>
<p>iii)Resins: the most common resins is benzoin which is used as an antiseptic.</p>
<p>iv)Oils: These can be volatile oils like peppermint, spearmint, menthol, cinnamon, lemon camphor. They have pleasant fragrance and evaporate easily. The other types of oils is fixed oils which include castor oil used as a laxative, olive oil for cooking, emollients used in cosmetics and solvents for injections.</p>
<p>Conti.</p>
<p>b) Animal sources: these are used to replace human chemicals that are not produced adequately due to disease or genetic problems e.g. insulin from pancreases of pigs and cows. Thyroid drugs and growth hormone preparations from animals hypothalamus. Despite these animal sources most of these products are being currently produced synthetically which provides purer and safer products than animal sources.</p>
<p>c)Inorganic sources: salts of various elements have therapeutic effect in the human body e.g., aluminum ( used as antacids),fluoride( used to prevent dental cavities and osteoporosis), gold( used for rheumatoid arthritis), iron( used for anemia) and potassium (used in potassium K+ supplements.)</p>
<p>Conti.</p>
<p>d)Synthetic sources: Many drugs are developed synthetically after chemicals in plants ,animals or other environment have been screened for signs of therapeutic activity. This eliminates side effects and increases drug potency. Drugs have genetic engineering are used to produce chemicals that have therapeutic effects.</p>
<p>e)Microbiological sources: example penicillins,tetracycline</p>
<p>f)recombinant DNA technology</p>
<p>uses of drugs</p>
<ol>
<li>curative: this is the primary therapy e.g. in treating infections or auxiliary therapy e.g. application of anaesthetic medication.</li>
<li>suppress signs and symptoms, hence improve quality of life without attaining cure e.g. anti diabetics.</li>
<li>prevent/prophylaxis- this could be primary e.g. use of vaccines to prevent one from getting a disease or secondary to stop progression of an existing disease.</li>
<li>diagnosis- for instance the use of tuberculin test to diagnose PTB</li>
</ol>
<p>drug nomenclature</p>
<p>Nomenclature is the systematic naming of drugs especially pharmaceutical drug Drugs in majority of circumstances have three types of names.</p>
<ol>
<li>i)Chemical/molecular/ scientific name: this is the chemical/molecular structure of a drug. It states the structure in terms of atoms and molecules accompanied by a diagram of the chemical structure. Most useful to a few technically trained personnel e.g. chemist or research pharmacist the names are unsuitable for general use since they are long. e.g. acetyl-p-amino-phenol is for paracetamol or acetaminophen</li>
<li>ii)generic/non-proprietary/approved name; this is the abbreviated and approved name. it is the official medical name assigned by the producer in collaboration with the food and drugs board and nomenclature committee. The generic name can be used by any interested party and it removes confusion of giving several names to the same drug regardless of who manufactures them once they have the same chemical structure. A generic name is not capitalized e.g. acetylsalicylic acid commonly known as aspirin,</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="conti">Conti.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#conti" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>iii)Trade name/proprietary/brand name: name given to the drug by the manufacturing and marketing company. One drug may have so many trade name e.g. acetaminophen has about 30 names some are paramol, Tylenol, Panadol etc. they are usually capitalized.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="example-of-drugs-chemical-name-generic-name-and-trade-name">example of drugs chemical name, generic name and trade name.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#example-of-drugs-chemical-name-generic-name-and-trade-name" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>Chemical name</th><th>Generic name</th><th>Trade names</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>2-(4-isobutylphenyl)propanoic acid</td><td>ibrufen</td><td>Brufen, advil, nurofen</td></tr><tr><td>N-acetyl-para-aminophenol</td><td>Paracetamol, acetaminophen</td><td>Calpol, Panadol, tylenol</td></tr><tr><td>2-(2-methl-5-nitro-1h-imidazol1-</td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>y)ethyl benzoate.</td><td>metronidazole</td><td>Flagyl ,metrogyl</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>two major methods of dispensing drugs</p>
<ul>
<li>Over the counter drugs (OTC):they do not need a prescription and can be purchased at the chemical shops; examples pain relief, blood tonics, vitamin preparation, ORS, antacids, antimalarial.</li>
<li>Prescription drugs: They need a prescription and must be controlled from abuse and dependence; e.g. antibiotics, anti-hypertensives, sedatives, diabetics drugs etc.</li>
</ul>
<p>Patients education -about OTC drugs</p>
<ul>
<li>You need to give your attention to all the drugs the patient is taking whether prescription or OTC.</li>
<li>Caution patient not to treat themselves with OTC drugs.</li>
<li>Inform them that most of the OTC medication contain more than one active ingredient.</li>
<li>Tell he patient that interactions can occur when takes more than one OTC medication at a time or takes one with a prescription drugs.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="patients-education-about-drugs-prescription-drugs">patients education about drugs - prescription drugs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#patients-education-about-drugs-prescription-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Inform patient about special consideration and drug safety precaution.</li>
<li>Encourage: complete medication list complete adverse reaction list.</li>
<li>Patients compliance.</li>
</ul>
<p>pharmacokinetics</p>
<ul>
<li>Pharmacokinetics is the process by which the body, sick or well, handles and affects the drug.</li>
<li>It is characterized by four processes</li>
</ul>
<p>i) absorption ;This is the process by which a drug is transferred from the site of administration into the circulating fluids of the body e.g. Blood and lymph.</p>
<ul>
<li>The rate of absorption is vital because it determines when the drug is available to exert its action.</li>
<li>Bioavailability: This is the fraction extent to which a dose of drug reaches its site of action .for example;1. hepatic metabolism and biliary excretion may occur before a drug taken orally reaches systemic circulation.(first pass effect)</li>
</ul>
<ol start="2">
<li>Drug given intravenously its bioavailability is 100%thus bioavailability must be considered when calculating none intravenous routes of administration.</li>
</ol>
<p>factors affecting absorption</p>
<ul>
<li>Route of drug administration.</li>
<li>Dose.</li>
<li>Dosage formulation.</li>
<li>Food and fluids administered with the drugs.</li>
<li>Status of the absorptive surface.</li>
<li>Rate of blood flow to the small intestines.</li>
<li>acidity of the stomach</li>
<li>Status of GI motility.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Factors influencing drug administration</p>
<p>â€¢ The nature of the absorbing surface.</p>
<p>â€¢ Blood flow to the site of administration; increase in blood flow facilitates abortion ; and e.g. sublingual route and pulmonary epithelium.</p>
<p>â€¢ The health status of the person taking the drug. This affects the rate of absorption and transportation.</p>
<p>â€¢ The lipid solubility of drugs the higher the solubility the more a drug is absorbed especially in the GIT.</p>
<p>â€¢ The PH of the drug.</p>
<p>â€¢ Drug concentration and critical concentration.</p>
<p>routes of drug administration</p>
<p>A drugs route of administration affects the rate and extend of absorption.</p>
<p>â€¢ Enteral route : drugs given along any portion of the GIT.it is most common, safe, convenient. and economical. but it is the slowest, it can be orally, sublingually, and rectally.</p>
<p>â€¢ Parenteral route: intradermally, subcutaneous, intramuscular, intrathecal intravenous.</p>
<p>â€¢ Pulmonary route: administered by in halation.</p>
<p>â€¢ topical: applied on the skin, mucus membrane of eyes, ears, nasal mucosa, bladder, vagina and the penis.</p>
<p>Factors to consider when choosing the route of drug administration</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>The time at which the effect of the drug is required.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The method most suitable for the drug required.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The site of drug action.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Patients status whether conscious or unconscious.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Desire off the patient.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Conti.</p>
<ul>
<li>When prescribing drugs the dose may vary with certain factors ; age, route, assimilation.</li>
</ul>
<p>ii)distribution: this is the transport of a drug in body fluids to various tissues of the body and ultimately site of action.</p>
<p>The rate of distribution depends on;</p>
<ul>
<li>The permeability of the capillary to the drug.</li>
<li>Lipid solubility and ionization of the drug. lipid soluble drugs are more rapidly absorbed and distributed than their lipid insoluble drugs</li>
<li>Cardiac function e.g. cardiac out put and regional blood, drug are fast distributed to areas with rich blood flow(Heart, kidneys, brain) later to areas of low blood flow (muscle, fat tissue).</li>
</ul>
<p>Conti.</p>
<ul>
<li>Drugs are widely distributed in body water (free fraction of drug)and partly as bound to plasma proteins and or tissues.</li>
<li>Plasma protein and tissue binding of drug reservoirs that sustain pharmacological action of a drug. The bound fraction and the free fraction are usually in a state of equilibrium</li>
<li>other proteins involved in drug binding include; lipoproteins, glycoprotein and globulins.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Biological membranes which limit the distribution of drugs</p>
<ul>
<li>Blood brain barrier: allows distribution of only lipid soluble drugs e.g. general anesthetics, barbiturates into the brain and spinal cord.</li>
<li>Placenta barrier: lipid soluble and some lipid insoluble can diffuse through hence some drug meant for the mother may pass through and harm the baby e.g. steroids ,narcotis and anaesthetics.</li>
<li>Blood-testes barrier: this may limit some chemotherapeutic agents used for treating testicular neoplasms.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>metabolism</p>
<p>iii)metabolism/biotransformation:</p>
<p>the biological transformation of a drug into an inactive metabolite, a more soluble compound ,or a more potent metabolite.</p>
<p>The Liver is the main organ of metabolism.</p>
<p>The Kidneys, gut mucosa, lungs and the skin are also involved in drug metabolism.</p>
<p>NB: Delayed drug metabolism results in accumulation of drug in the body and prolonged effect of the drug</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="factors-influencing-metabolism">Factors influencing metabolism<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#factors-influencing-metabolism" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Physiological factors like starvation, liver diseases, cardiovascular problems, these depress microsomal enzyme systems.</li>
<li>Age people with extreme ages have decreased metabolism</li>
<li>Genetic predisposition genetic differences in the rate of metabolism of some drugs exist.</li>
<li>Prior administration of the particular drugs or other drugs e.g. repeated administration of a particular drug may cause induction or inhibition</li>
</ul>
<p>Enzyme induction or inhibition</p>
<ul>
<li>enzyme induction this is a situation whereby the re is an increase in amount and activity of the liver microsomal enzymes usually due to exposure to certain substances such as drugs and endogenous substances.</li>
<li>A drug may induce its own metabolism</li>
</ul>
<p>pharmacological Importance of enzyme induction</p>
<ol>
<li>Drug interaction may occur.</li>
<li>Disease may result .</li>
<li>Tolerance (metabolic) to the drug.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>conti.</p>
<ul>
<li>Enzyme inhibition this refers to decrease synthesis and activity of liver microsomal enzymes.it results in reduced metabolism of other drugs/inhibiting drug and endogenous substance.</li>
<li>General enzyme inhibition(beyond liver enzymes )has a greater pharmacological importance utility than enzyme induction.</li>
<li>Examples of drugs that inhibit enzymes include chloramphenicol and cimetidine.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>excretion</p>
<p>iv) Excretion: this the process by which drugs and pharmacologically active or inactive metabolites are eliminated from he body primarily through the Kidneys.</p>
<p>Net renal excretion of a drug is as a result of 3 processes</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>filtration (passive glomerular filtration)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>re-absorption,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>active tubular secretion.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>other routes through which drugs are eliminated include</p>
<p>intestines or biliary excretion e.g. neomycin</p>
<p>Pulmonary elimination e.g. volatile liquids (general anaesthetics)</p>
<p>Sweat and saliva elimination e.g. thiazides.</p>
<p>Breast milk elimination e.g. narcotics.</p>
<p>Pharmacodynamics/mechanism of action</p>
<p>The study of how drugs act on the body. It is the chemical changes or effects that a drug has on body cell and tissues.</p>
<p>â€¢ Drug action: the cellular process involved in the drug and cell interaction.</p>
<p>â€¢ Drug effects: the physiology reaction of the body to the drug.</p>
<p>The common drug molecules (targets) on which drugs bind to produce therapeutic effects include enzymes, carrier molecules, ion channels, and receptors.</p>
<p>â€¢ The receptor : these are proteins that are found within or on the surface of cells</p>
<p>Two terms related to receptors are affinity and efficacy.</p>
<p>â€¢ Efficacy the tendency of a drug to activate the receptor once bound.</p>
<p>â€¢ Affinity the tendency of a drug to bind to the receptor.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="drug-interactions">Drug interactions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#drug-interactions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="harmful-interactions">Harmful interactions-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#harmful-interactions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>-Oral contraceptives and anti TB drugs - contraceptive failure.
-Tetracycline and antacids - cimetidine renders tetracycline ineffective.
-Anticoagulants warfarin and aspirin - may result to bleeding.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="beneficial-drug-interactions">Beneficial drug interactions-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#beneficial-drug-interactions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>-Amino glycoside &amp; penicillin's achieve synergic antimicrobial effects
-probenecid plus penicillin prolong action of penicillin..
-Morphine poisoning-naloxone is used as an antidote.</p>
<p>Conti.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="synergism">Synergism<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#synergism" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This can either be</p>
<p>summation- this occurs when the effect of two drugs having the same action are additive e.g. beta blockers plus thiazide diuretics have an additive anti hypertensive effects.</p>
<p>Potentiating- this means to make more powerful, occurs when the action of one drug increases the action of another. e.g trimethoprim plus sulfamethoxazole.</p>
<p>antagonism</p>
<ul>
<li>Agonist- drug binds to a receptor there is a response.</li>
<li>Antagonist-drug binds to a receptor-no response, prevents binding of agonist(alpha and beta blockers)</li>
<li>Partial agonist-a drug that is able to both stimulate and block at receptor.</li>
<li>Antagonism- occurs when two or more drugs oppose the action of one another producing opposite pharmacodynamic effects e.g.</li>
</ul>
<p>Antacids and tetracycline form a complex which is excreted in feaces chemical antagonism.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="administration-of-medication">Administration of medication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#administration-of-medication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Administration of medication involves all the activities related to safe drug use which are the nursing responsibilities.</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Assessing the risk to a client of a new drug order.</li>
<li>Delivering the drug dose to the proper body tissues.</li>
<li>Assessing the client's response to drug therapy.</li>
<li>Treatment of adverse reactions to drugs.</li>
<li>Consulting with the doctor about adjusting the prescribed regime.</li>
<li>Educating the client about proper use of drugs substances.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="principles-of-drug-administration">Principles of drug administration<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#principles-of-drug-administration" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>For a Nurse administration of medication is an important responsibility.to avoid errors a nurse must adhere to the principles of drug administration.</li>
<li>To provide safe administration of drugs a nurse should practice the rights of drug administration. they are</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Right patient.</li>
<li>Right drug.</li>
<li>Right dose.</li>
<li>Right time.</li>
<li>Right route.</li>
</ol>
<p>conti.</p>
<p>Five additional right are essential in professional nursing practice. they are</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>The right assessment e.g. patients ability to swallow, allergies, contraindication, new signs and symptoms that may indicate adverse effects of administration, heart, liver or kidney disorders.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The right documentation.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The clients right to information of name, purpose, action and potential side effects.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The right evaluation.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The clients right to refuse medication regardless of the consequences.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Conti.</p>
<ul>
<li>Right client/patient:</li>
</ul>
<p>-You should make sure that the right client receives the right drug.</p>
<p>-You should only give drugs to the person for whom they are prescribed or recommended for.</p>
<p>-If the patient is wearing an identification bracelet, check the clients name on the identification bracelet with the name, hospital number on the medication card in your hand.</p>
<p>-Alternatively if the patient is conscious and sane simply call out the patients name.</p>
<p>Conti.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="right-drug">Right drug<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#right-drug" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>â€¢ You must check and double check the package label , the cardex and the medication card or sheet.</p>
<p>â€¢ The right drug label should be read at list three times;</p>
<p>-before removing the drug from the cupboard.</p>
<p>-Before preparing or measuring the actual prescribed does.</p>
<p>-Before replacing the drug on the shelf just before administering the drug to the client.</p>
<p>â€¢ You must prepare the medication you give yourself and DO NOT giver drugs prepared by someone else.</p>
<p>â€¢ You should recheck the order, label and the medication card if a client questions the medication.</p>
<p>A Mentally alert person will notice a change in medication or mention problems that have arisen from the medication.</p>
<p>ensure that you take the following precaution when administering medicine.</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>All doses are best prepared from the original container.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Medicines should not be prepared in the dark</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>You should caution clients about the use of non-labelled pillboxes</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Do not mix supplies of several tablets or capsules in a single container</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>make sure you check medication label before removing from the shelf before pouring or measuring and when returning to the shelf.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>right dose:</p>
<p>-to obtain the right dose you must carefully measure the medicine.</p>
<p>-when pouring solid drugs such as capsules and tablets use proper technique to avoid contaminating the drugs. you should pour the medication in the container cap, and transfer the number of units required from the cap to the medication cup</p>
<p>-if a half a tablet is required a scored tablet may be cut into two pieces with a knife-edge or folded in a clean paper and broken with the fingers. this procedure is easiest with large tablets.</p>
<p>-for small tablets which provide little leverage for fingers ,should be cut with a knife.</p>
<p>-DO NOT ATTEMPT to split NON-SCORED tablets or to divide a dose of a single capsule.</p>
<p>-when you split tablets, give the two halves in successive doses so that any deviation from the prescribed dose due to uneven breakage is levelled out as quickly as possible.</p>
<p>-DO NOT break all the tablets available and mix the halves.</p>
<p>Liquids should be measured with a scale that provides a mark for the required dose e.g. plastic glasses or spoons.</p>
<p>Dosage calculation use the (WIG) calculation; what you want multiply by what's in and divide by what you got equal to amount to give.</p>
<p>Right route:</p>
<p>â€¢ The right route must be used for drug delivery.</p>
<p>â€¢ Most drugs are given orally or by topical application .</p>
<p>â€¢ Ensure the patient understands how the drug is to be taken.</p>
<p>â€¢ sub lingual or chewable tablets should NOT BE swallowed whole.</p>
<p>â€¢ Crush oral drugs if swallowing is difficult or if they are to be taken in liquid form.</p>
<p>â€¢ Demonstrate to the patient the procedures for application of topical drugs.</p>
<p>â€¢ Always check the doctors orders ,the cardex and the treatment sheet to verify the medication route.</p>
<p>Alert the doctor if the route is not in accord with which is recommended for the drug preparation.</p>
<p>Right time:</p>
<ul>
<li>Under normal circumstances the right time for drug administration Is not indicated by the doctor. The doctor only indicates the number of times a drug is to be given.</li>
<li>For example;</li>
</ul>
<p>The hourly interval between doses</p>
<p>The relationship of dose to the clients activity ,such as before or after meals, on rising or retiring, every 4hours, hour, 12 hours.</p>
<p>Patients with poor time orientation, short term memory defects or distracting activity schedule need some systems for guiding them in self medication.</p>
<ul>
<li>Most hospitals have set up routines for intervals and times for medication</li>
<li>Nonetheless you must be familiar with times for medications and the appropriate times for administering them.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>medication in children</p>
<p>Take great care when administering drugs in children;</p>
<p>â€¢ There is high risk of errors due to changes in weight and age.</p>
<p>â€¢ Most drugs have not been tested in children.</p>
<p>â€¢ Many drugs are marked in dosage forms and concentration suitable for adults. Therefore this requires dilution, calculation preparation and administration of very small doses.</p>
<p>â€¢ Children have limited sites for IV (intravenous)administration ,several drugs may be given through the same site.</p>
<p>â€¢ This increases the need for small volumes of fluid and flushing between sites.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="medication-errors">medication errors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#medication-errors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Wrong client</li>
<li>Wrong route</li>
<li>Wrong medication or IV fluids</li>
<li>Wrong dose or IV rate</li>
<li>Omission of dose</li>
<li>Incorrect discontinuation of treatment.</li>
</ul>
<p>drug records</p>
<p>â€¢ Every health institution has its own records for drug accountability,</p>
<p>these are;</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>patients drug order card/treatment sheet</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Antibiotic register oral and injectables this has, stock at hand, drugs received from pharmacy, drug issued to patients, date and time issued, signature of the dispensing nurse. this book is balanced at he end of each page.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Handing over register for the purpose of handing over drug during each shift.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Requisition register for ordering drugs from pharmacy should always be accompanied by the drug register.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>drug storage</p>
<ul>
<li>Many factors can change your medication including heat, .air , light, and moisture. This will infective or even harmful.</li>
<li>Drugs require careful storage and handling to maintain their safety and potency.</li>
<li>Every medication has its owner recommended storage condition from room temperature, refrigeration and freezing thus check the specific storage condition.</li>
<li>They must be kept in special spaces secured from access by unauthorized persons.</li>
<li>Storage areas should be kept clean, cool, and dry with no direct sun light.</li>
<li>Drugs should not be placed on the floor.</li>
<li>Sterile substances should be protected from contamination.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Drugs are best kept in their original containers. original containers protect their content.</p>
<ul>
<li>Do not transfer sterile substances from container to container as it increases the probability of contamination. Protect the label from soiling to ensure it remains legible.</li>
<li>Drugs should only be labeled in pharmacy.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Stock control;</p>
<p>This is done by use of a medication stock sheet for each drug .</p>
<p>Content of the sheet is the</p>
<p>-name of the drug</p>
<p>-date and time</p>
<p>-quantity stock</p>
<p>-quantity received</p>
<p>-quantity used</p>
<p>-quantity discarded</p>
<p>-Expiary date.</p>
<p>Use FEFO (first expiry first out) when arranging and issuing drugs , for drugs with the same expiry date use FIFO (first in first out)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="classification-of-drugs">Classification of drugs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification-of-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Classification systems enable us to readily identify the similarities and differences among a large number of medications within or outside a classification.
Drugs can be classified according to;</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Body systems as follows;
-Respiratory medications
-Cardiovascular system medications
-Nervous system medications
-GIT medications</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Their functions or use e.g.
-antidepressant
-diuretics
-analgesics
-antibiotics
3.Their chemical make up
-estrogens
-opioids</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="antibiotics-anti-infective-agents">antibiotics/anti- infective agents<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#antibiotics-anti-infective-agents" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Antibiotics are among the most commonly used and misused of all drugs.</li>
<li>The inevitable consequence of their widespread use has been the emergence of antibiotic-resistance pathogens.</li>
<li>There different groups of antibacterial agents based on molecular structure and members of each group have a comparable pharmacokinetic and pharmacodynamics.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="classification-of-antibiotics">Classification of antibiotics<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification-of-antibiotics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Beta- lactam antibiotics</li>
<li>tetracycline</li>
<li>Aminoglycoside</li>
<li>Macrolides</li>
<li>Quinolones</li>
<li>Azoles</li>
<li>Antimycobacterial</li>
<li>Sulphonemides</li>
<li>lincosamides</li>
<li>Unclassified antibiotics like chloramphenicol, spectinomycin and vancomycin</li>
</ul>
<p>Beta â€“lactam antibiotics</p>
<p>All beta â€“lactam compounds ,so named because of their unique four membered lactam ring as a basic chemical structure.</p>
<p>They are sub divided in to</p>
<p>â€¢ Penicillin</p>
<p>â€¢ Cephalosporins</p>
<p>â€¢ Others e.g. carbapenems and monobactams</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="penicillins">penicillins<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#penicillins" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="classification-of-penicillins">Classification of penicillins<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification-of-penicillins" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Narrow spectrum e.g. benzyl penicillin, phenoxy methyl penicillin, penethicillin.</li>
<li>Antistaphylococcal penicillin also called beta-lactamase resistant penicillin, or penicillinase resistant penicillin's e.g. nafcillin, cloxacillin, flucloxacillin, methicillin.</li>
<li>Broad spectrum penicillin e.g. ampicillin, amoxicillin, bacampicillin</li>
<li>Antipseudomonal (extended spectrum penicillin) e.g. carbecillin, carfecillin, ticarcillin, temocillin.</li>
</ul>
<p>Mechanism of action</p>
<ul>
<li>All beta lactam anti biotics inhibit bacteria cell wall synthesis.</li>
<li>By inactivating enzymes located in the bacteria cell membrane .</li>
<li>They are bactericidal agents acting against multiplying bacteria (diving cells) as resting bacteria do not make new cell walls.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Mechanism of bacterial resistance</p>
<p>general mechanism of bacteria resistance to antibiotics including beta â€“lactams are;</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Decreased penetration to the target cells</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Alteration of the target site</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Inactivation of the antibiotics by a bacterial enzyme e.g. beta â€“lactamase.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>pharmacokinetics</p>
<ul>
<li>Benzylpenicillin is destroyed by gastric acid hence it is parenterally administered.</li>
<li>Phenoxymethylpenicillin can be orally given.</li>
<li>Metabolism is in the liver.</li>
<li>Half life less than 2hours.</li>
<li>poor lipid solubility hence they donâ€™t cross the BBB.</li>
<li>distribution in body fluids and tissues with a few exception. they are polar hence extracellular concentrations exceed he intracellular.</li>
<li>Elimination in the kidneys by glomerular filtration and tubular secretion.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="benzyl-penicillin-g">Benzyl penicillin G<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#benzyl-penicillin-g" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Penicillin G is gastric acid unstable is used where high plasma concentration era required.</li>
<li>Maximum plasma concentration is reached after 15 minute of administration</li>
<li>Half life 0.5 hours hence reasonably spaced doses have to be large to maintain a therapeutic concentration high doses can be maintained by use of probenecid.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="indication-for-penicillin-g">Indication for penicillin G<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#indication-for-penicillin-g" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>It is generally active against gram positive and gram negative cocci, hence indicated for treatment of conditions such as;</p>
<ul>
<li>Otitis media</li>
<li>Gonococcus infection</li>
<li>Throat infections</li>
<li>Streptococcal endocarditis</li>
<li>Meningococcal meningitis</li>
<li>Pneumonia meningitis</li>
<li>actinomycosis</li>
</ul>
<p>cloxacillin</p>
<ul>
<li>half live is 30 minutes</li>
</ul>
<p>indication for infections due to penicillinase (enzyme against penicillin) producing staphylococci especially skin infections and soft tissue infections e.g. cellulitis, otitis externa, impetigo</p>
<p>Dosage; Adults by oral 500mg every 6 hours at least 30 minutes before meals because food decreases absorption.</p>
<p>IM 250mg every 4-6 hours.</p>
<p>IV injection or infusion 500mg every 4-6 hours .</p>
<p>The dose may be increased in severe infections.</p>
<ul>
<li>A child less than 2 years should get <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>1</mn><mi mathvariant="normal">/</mi><mn>4</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">1 / 4</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mord">1/4</span></span></span></span></span> of adult dose.</li>
<li>Children 2-10 years should receive <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>1</mn><mi mathvariant="normal">/</mi><mn>2</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">1 / 2</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mord">1/2</span></span></span></span></span> of adult dose.</li>
</ul>
<p>Ampicillin</p>
<ul>
<li>Is gastric stable, it is moderately 50 % absorbed orally as food interferes with absorption..</li>
<li>The drug is concentrated in the bile and it under goes enteral hepatic recycling.</li>
<li>Excretion is through the kidneys 1/3 of the administered drug appears unchanged in urine.</li>
<li>Almost all staphylococcus aureus ,50% of E.coli, and 50% of haemophilus influenza are now resistant .</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="indications">Indications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#indications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Urinary tract infections.</li>
<li>Sinusitis .</li>
<li>Chronic bronchitis.</li>
<li>Invasive salmonellosis gonorrhea</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="side-effects">Side effects<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#side-effects" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Diarrhea is quiet common, nausea
Macular rashes resembling measles/rubella - discontinue treatment</p>
<p>Dosage</p>
<p>â€¢ Adults oral 0.25 to 1g 6 hourly at least 30 minutes before food.</p>
<p>â€¢ Different dose are used in treating different condition.</p>
<p>â€¢ Gonorrhea 2-3g is administered as a single dose with probenecid.</p>
<p>â€¢ UTI :500mg every 8 hours IM/IV/infusion.</p>
<p>â€¢ Children under age 10 years give half the adult dose.</p>
<p>amoxicillin</p>
<ul>
<li>This is a broad spectrum penicillin.</li>
<li>A derivative of ampicillin and differs by only one hydroxyl (OH) group.</li>
<li>Have similar anti bacteria spectrum as ampicillin.</li>
<li>when given orally absorption is better than ampicillin.</li>
<li>Absorption is not affected by food in the stomach.</li>
<li>Half life is 1 hourâ€™</li>
</ul>
<p>Indication</p>
<ul>
<li>UTI, otitis media, sinusitis, chronic bronchitis, inversive salmonellosis and gonorrhea.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>dosage</p>
<ul>
<li>Adult dose orally 250mgs 8 hourly which can be doubled in severe infections.</li>
<li>Children up to 10 years of age get 125mg 8 hourly this is doubled in severe infections.</li>
<li>IM/IV adults 500 mg 8 hourly.</li>
<li>IM/IV children get 50-100mg /kg daily in divided doses.</li>
</ul>
<p>Side effects</p>
<p>Diarrhea is less frequent with the use of amoxicillin than ampicillin</p>
<p>co- amoxiclav</p>
<ul>
<li>Amoxicillin ( 250mg or 500mg )can be combined with clavulanic acid (125mg) to make co- amoxiclav.</li>
<li>clavulanic acid itself has no significant anti bacteria activity but binds to beta-lactamase and there by competitively inhibits its activity hence protecting the penicillin. This potentiate the action of penicillin.</li>
</ul>
<p>Indication</p>
<p>Active against beta-lactamase producing bacteria that are resistant to amoxicillin which include; staphylococcus aureus, 50% of E-coli, 15% of H. influenzae strains and klebsiella spp,</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="adverse-effect-of-penicillin-s">adverse effect of penicillin's<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#adverse-effect-of-penicillin-s" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>1gE -mediated allergic reactions.</li>
<li>serum sickness.</li>
<li>Dermatological reactions e.g. eryema multiforme ,steven johsons syndrome and exfoliative dermatitis.</li>
<li>Neurologic reactions.</li>
<li>Gastrointestinal reactions.</li>
<li>Hepatobiliary reaction.</li>
<li>Renal reactions.</li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Nursing Administration</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Instruct clients that penicillin V, amoxicillin, and amoxicillin-clavulanate may be taken with meals. All others should be taken with a full glass of water 1 hours before meals or 2 hours after.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Instruct clients to report any signs of an allergic response such as skin rash, itching, and/or hives.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>IM injection should be done cautiously to avoid injection into a nerve or an artery.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Advise clients to complete the entire course of therapy regardless of presence of absence of symptoms.</p>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<p>cephalosporins are the most frequently prescribed class of antibiotics.</p>
<ul>
<li>They are structurally and pharmacologically related to the penicillins. they have a wider spectrum of activity than penicillins hence they are more expensive.</li>
</ul>
<p>mechanisms of action</p>
<ul>
<li>They are bactericidal, interfere with the bacterial cell wall synthesis.</li>
</ul>
<p>Classification of cephalosporins</p>
<ul>
<li>They are grouped in â€œgenerationsâ€ based on their spectrum of antimicrobial activity.</li>
<li>The first cephalosporins were designated first generation while later, more extended generation cephalosporins.</li>
<li>Each newer generation of cephalosporins has a significantly greater gram negative antimicrobial properties than the preceding generation, in most cases with decreased activity against gram positive organism.</li>
<li>The newer agents have a much longer half life resulting in the decreased of dosing frequency.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>first generation cephalosporins</p>
<ul>
<li>These are generally active against gram positive bacteria. They have moderate activity against gram negative bacterial.</li>
<li>They include;</li>
<li>cephalexin.</li>
<li>Cephaloridine</li>
<li>Cephalothin</li>
<li>Cephapirin</li>
<li>Cefazolin</li>
<li>Cephradine</li>
<li>Cefadroxil.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>second generation cephalosporin</p>
<ul>
<li>They have a greater gram-negative spectrum eg H.influenza n. gonorrhea, E.coli, shigella.</li>
<li>Also some gram-positive organism e.g. clostridium, staphylococcus, streptococcus and pneumococcus.</li>
<li>they are more resistant to beta lactamase.</li>
</ul>
<p>Indication</p>
<ul>
<li>Upper and lower respiratory tract infection</li>
<li>Sinusitis</li>
<li>Otitis media</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Third generation cephalosporins</p>
<ul>
<li>They are especially better than SECOND AND FIRST generation cephalosporin against gram negative bacteria.</li>
<li>These are;</li>
<li>Cefriaxone</li>
<li>Cefperazone</li>
<li>Cefotaxime</li>
<li>Ceftazidine</li>
<li>Cefodizime</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Fourth generation cephalosporin</p>
<ul>
<li>These drugs are very good against both gram positive and gram negative bacteria</li>
<li>Examples ;</li>
<li>Cefepime</li>
<li>Cefditoren and loracarbef.</li>
</ul>
<p>Pharmacokinetic of cephalosporins</p>
<p>Usually given parenterally, though few may be given orally e.g.</p>
<p>cephalexin</p>
<p>cephradine</p>
<p>cefadroxil</p>
<p>Distribution- Wide distribution because of lipid solubility.</p>
<p>Metabolism- in the liver with half life of 1-4 hours.</p>
<p>Excretion- excreted unchanged in urine especially tubular secretion.</p>
<p>â€¢ Dosage should be reduced for patients with renal impairment.</p>
<p>â€¢ Active excretion in the kidneys can be blocked by probenecid.</p>
<p>Indication; Septicemia, Pneumonia, Meningitis, Biliary tract infection, Peritonitis, Urinary tract infection, sinusitis</p>
<p>Unwanted effects of cephalosporins</p>
<ul>
<li>Hypersensitivity is the most common</li>
</ul>
<p>10% of the patients sensitive to penicillin are sensitive to cephalosporin.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Hemorrhage due to interference with blood clotting factors.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Use of cephalosporin for more than two weeks causes thrombocytopenia, neutropenia, interstitial nephritis and abnormal liver function tests.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Drug interactions</p>
<ul>
<li>Cephalosporin with alcohol- disulfiram like effects.</li>
</ul>
<p>Patient should avoid alcohol when taking the drug.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Cephalosporin with high frusemide and torsemide are likely to cause nephrotoxicity.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Cephalosporin with aminoglycoside â€“ nephrotoxicity.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Cephalosporin with oral anticoagulant like warfarin may cause bleed because both interfere with clotting factors.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Ceftriaxone (Rocephin)</p>
<ul>
<li>Half life 4hours hence requires to be administered once a daily.</li>
</ul>
<p>Indication; Septicemia, Pneumonia, UTI, RTI, soft tissue infections.</p>
<p>Contraindication;</p>
<ul>
<li>penicillin sensitivity</li>
<li>Administer with caution in renal impairment.</li>
<li>Do not administer to infants below 6 weeks.</li>
<li>Cephalosporin hypersensitivity.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Nursing administration</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Instruct clients to complete the prescribed course of therapy, even though symptoms may resolve before the full course of antimicrobial treatment is completed.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Advise clients to take oral cephalosporins with food.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Instruct clients to store oral cephalosporin suspensions in a refrigerator.</p>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="tetracyclines">tetracyclines<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tetracyclines" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>First isolated in 1948, isolated from Streptomyces fungi.</li>
<li>Naturally occurring;
-tetracycline
-chlortetracycline
-oxytetracycline
-demeclocycline
Semi-synthetic
Doxycycline, lymecycline, meclocycline, methacyline, minocycline, rolitetracycline.</li>
</ul>
<p>pharmacokinetics</p>
<ul>
<li>Tetracyclines are partially absorbed in the alimentary tract EXCEPT minocycline and doxycycline which have a good absorption.</li>
<li>Absorption is increased in absence of food</li>
<li>antacids and milk decrease absorption as they contain metals like magnesium, calcium, aluminum ,iron which chelate with them.</li>
<li>Distribution is narrow but they cross the placenta barrier.</li>
<li>Metabolism is in the liver</li>
<li>Excretion in urine via glomerular filtration unchanged.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pharmacodynamics">pharmacodynamics<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pharmacodynamics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Tetracyclines are broad spectrum bacteriostatic.</li>
<li>They inhibit protein synthesis by binding to the 30s sub unit of the bacterial ribosomes.</li>
<li>Indication; psittacosis, pneumonia, brucellosis, shigellosis, rickettsia diseases e.g. Q fever, typhus, cholera, borrelia ( lame disease, relapsing fever)acne ,amoebic dysentery, spirochetes, protozoa, bacillary dysentery and chlamydia infections</li>
</ul>
<p>aminoglycosides</p>
<p>Examples;</p>
<p>Gentamycin, kanamycin, amikacin, tobramycin, streptomycin, neomycin,</p>
<p>They are always used in combination of beta lactam antibiotic because of their synergism effect.</p>
<p>pharmacokinetics; they are water soluble hence hey not absorbed through the gut .</p>
<p>They are given IM/IV route</p>
<p>distribution; narrowly distributed hence do not cross the blood brain barrier.</p>
<p>Pharmacodynamics/mechanism of action</p>
<ul>
<li>they are bactericidal act by binding to the 30s ribosomal sub unit and they inhibit bacterial protein synthesis.</li>
<li>Drug interaction;</li>
<li>-muscle weakness or paralysis when given with neural muscular blocking agent.</li>
<li>Ototoxicity when given with ototoxic agent.</li>
<li>Synergic effect when give with beta lactam antibiotic .</li>
<li>Bone marrow depression when give with bone marrow depressing agents.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Unwanted effects</p>
<ul>
<li>Have serious un wanted effects and that are dose dependent</li>
</ul>
<p>these are; nausea, vomiting, diarrhea , lethargy, hypersensitivity and headache.</p>
<p>Others are ,nephrotoxicity, ,ototoxicity, bone marrow depression, neuromuscular blockade, palpitation, numbness, tingling sensation, depression and disorientation.</p>
<p>Contraindication</p>
<ul>
<li>Patients with hearing deficit because thy damage the 8^{th} cranial nerve(vestibular cochlear/auditory nerve)</li>
<li>Myasthenia gravis since they cause neural muscular blockade.</li>
<li>Patients with severe renal disease as they are nephrotoxic</li>
<li>Hypersensitivity</li>
<li>Neonates, geriantrics, infant, botulism and patients with packinsonism</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Gentamycin</p>
<ul>
<li>This is the most active aminoglycoside.</li>
<li>Half life 2-3 hours and reaches peak plasma concentration within 30 minute.</li>
<li>route of administration IM/IV.</li>
<li>indication gram negative and gram positive; septicemia, meningitis, endocarditis, UTI, neonatal sepsis and acute pyelonephritis among other infections.</li>
</ul>
<p>Contraindications; is like for the other aminoglycoside.</p>
<p>dosage adults GIVE 2-5 MG/kg body weight daily 8hrly for 7 days. Reduce the dose in renal impairment and the elderly.</p>
<p>Children below 2wks 3mgs/kg body weight every 12 hours.</p>
<p>Those aged 2wks-12years 2mg/kg every 8 hourly.</p>
<p>Aminoglycoside can replace penicillin in penicillin sensitive patients</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Gentamycin combine with penicillin have a synergic antibiotic effect expands the spectrum of antibiotics activity and prevent emergence of resistance..</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Neomycin and kanamycin can be used for hepatic coma to reduce normal flora and therefore ammonia gas formation.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Amikacin has broadest antibacterial spectrum because it is stable to 8 of the 9 classified aminoglycoside inactivating enzymes whereas gentamycin is inactivated by five of them.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Amikacin is indicated for serious gram negative infections resistant to gentamycin.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Neomycin and framycetin are too toxic for systemic use hence used topically for treatment of aer, nose and skin infections,</p>
</li>
<li></li>
</ul>
<p>quinolones</p>
<ul>
<li>these are broad spectrum antibiotic though some like nalidixic acid and cinoxacin have a narrow antibacterial spectrum.</li>
</ul>
<p>other newer quinolones include</p>
<p>norfloxacin</p>
<p>Ciprofloxacin</p>
<p>Ofloxacin</p>
<p>Levofloxacin</p>
<p>Acrofloxacin</p>
<p>pefloxacin</p>
<p>Pharmacodynamics</p>
<ul>
<li>They are act by inhibiting bacterial DNA gyrase the enzyme that maintains the Helical twist/structure of the DNA.</li>
<li>They are bactericidal but some are bacteriostatic</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Pharmacokinetics</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Quinolones are absorbed in the gut though aluminum and magnesium antacid interfere with the absorption.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Distribution wide distribution such that they cross the placenta and are distributed in breast milk.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>They are concentrated in the lungs, kidneys, prostate, and phagocytes.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>They donâ€™t cross the BBB except ofloxacin and pefloxacin.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Metabolism they under go hepatic metabolism with a variable half life</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Norfloxacin and ciprofloxacin half life of 2-3 hours, 5 hour ofloxacin, perfloxacin10 hour.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Excretion/elimination via renal and biliary.</p>
</li>
<li></li>
</ul>
<p>Adverse effects</p>
<p>â€¢ GIT effects like nausea, vomiting, and diarrhea</p>
<p>â€¢ CNS effects like dizziness, headache, confusion and convulsions.</p>
<p>â€¢ Allergic reactions in form of skin rashes,</p>
<p>They are reported to cause arthropathy in immature animals hence not recommended for children and adolescence unless the benefit out ways the risk.</p>
<p>â€¢ Photosensitivity</p>
<p>â€¢ Bone marrow suppression.</p>
<p>contraindication</p>
<ul>
<li>History of epilepsy or seizures.</li>
<li>Glucose-7-phosphatedehydrogenase deficiency.</li>
<li>Myasthenia gravis.</li>
<li>Pregnancy and breast feeding.</li>
</ul>
<p>Indication; quinolones are basically indicated for UTI ciprofloxacin has a broader spectrum of antibacterial activity.</p>
<p>These are often caused by gram negative organisms like E.coli, proteus spp. Therefore infections like complicated UTI, inversive otitis externa, salmonella typhi infection, gonorrhea, bacteria prostatitis and cervicitis.</p>
<p>They are also indicated for anthrax which has been used as a biological warfare.</p>
<p>So the soldiers can take quinolones just before they go to war just in case they are at risk of exposure to anthrax.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="drug-interactions">drug interactions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#drug-interactions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>These antibiotics are enzyme (cytochrome p-450) inhibitor hence interact with other drugs at metabolism e.g. theophylline, warfarin, and caffeine.</li>
<li>NSAIDS and quinolones causes an increase in the risk of convulsion.</li>
<li>NSAIDS tends to potentiate the effect.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="ciprofloxacin">ciprofloxacin<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ciprofloxacin" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>half life is 3hours</li>
<li>It is mostly effective against gram negative bacteria e.g. salmonella, shigella, Campylobacter, pseudomonas, enterobacteria.</li>
<li>It is indicated for chlamydia and some mycobacteria</li>
</ul>
<p>Indication UTI and genital urinary tract infections.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="dosage">Dosage<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dosage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Oral 250-750mg bd.</li>
<li>IV infusion (30-60) 200-400mg twice daily.</li>
</ul>
<p>Interactions Medication/Food Interactions Nursing Interventions/Client Education</p>
<ul>
<li>Cationic compounds (aluminum-magnesium antacids, iron salts, sucralfate, milk and dairy products) decrease absorption of ciprofloxacin;</li>
</ul>
<p>Administer cationic compounds 6 hrs. before or 2 hrs after ciprofloxacin</p>
<ul>
<li>Plasma levels of theophylline can be the increased with concurrent use of ciprofloxacin;</li>
</ul>
<p>Monitor levels and adjust dosage accordingly.</p>
<ul>
<li>Plasma levels of warfarin can be increased with concurrent use of ciprofloxacin;</li>
</ul>
<p>Monitor prothrombin time and INR, and adjust the dosage of warfarin accordingly.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="administration">Administration<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#administration" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Ciprofloxacin is available in oral and intravenous forms.</li>
<li>Decrease doses of ciprofloxacin in clients with renal dysfunction.</li>
<li>Intravenous ciprofloxacin should be administered slowly over 60 min.</li>
<li>For inhalation anthrax infection, ciprofloxacin is administered every 12 hrs for 60 days.</li>
<li>Instruct clients to complete the prescribed course of antimicrobial therapy, even though symptoms may resolve before the full course is completed.</li>
</ul>
<p>MACROLIDES</p>
<ul>
<li>These broad spectrum antimicrobials including;</li>
<li>Erythromycin</li>
<li>Azithromycin</li>
<li>Spiramycin</li>
<li>Clarithromycin</li>
</ul>
<p>Pharmacodynamics; they inhibit protein synthesis by irreversibly binding to ribosomal 50s sub unit of the sensitive micro-organism hence they are bacteriostatic.</p>
<p>But sometimes can be bactericidal if the dose is high.</p>
<p>Example azithromycin is bactericidal against streptococcus pyogenes, streptococcus pneumonia and hemophilus influenza</p>
<p>pharmacokinetics</p>
<ul>
<li>They can be administered orally though erythromycin is unstable in acidic environment.</li>
<li>Distribution is good except that the drugs do not cross the BBB</li>
<li>Metabolism is in the liver and have variable half life.</li>
</ul>
<p>E.g. clarithromycin has4.5 hours , azithromycin less than 3.5 hours and erythromycin has1.4 to 2 hours.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<ul>
<li><strong>Therapeutic Uses/indication</strong></li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li>Used to treat infections in <strong>clients with a penicillin allergy</strong>, such as for <strong>prophylaxis against rheumatic fever</strong> and <strong>bacterial endocarditis</strong>.</li>
<li>Used for clients <strong>with Legionnairesâ€™ disease, whooping cough</strong> (pertussis), <strong>and acute diphtheria</strong> (eliminates the carrier state of diphtheria) .</li>
<li>Used for chlamydia infections (<strong>urethritis and cervicitis; pneumonia</strong> caused by Mycoplasma pneumoniae**; respiratory tract infections** caused by <strong>Streptococcus pneumoniae and Neisseria gonorrhea.</strong></li>
</ul>
<p>Complications /Side/Adverse Effects; Nursing Interventions/Client Education</p>
<p>Gastrointestinal discomfort</p>
<p>â€¢ (nausea, vomiting, epigastric pain) Administer erythromycin with meals.</p>
<p>â€¢ Observe for GI symptoms and notify the provider.</p>
<p>Hepatotoxicity (abdominal pain, lethargy, jaundice) . Instruct clients to notify the provider because the medication should be discontinued. Prolonged QT interval causing dysrhythmias and possible sudden cardiac death</p>
<p>â€¢ Use in clients with prolonged QT intervals is not recommended.</p>
<p>â€¢ Avoid concurrent use with medications that affect hepatic drug metabolizing enzymes.</p>
<p>Contraindications/Precautions.</p>
<p>â€¢ pre-existing liver disease</p>
<p>erythromycin</p>
<p>â€¢ Erythromycin is the commonest macrolide in use.</p>
<p>Pharmacokinetic;</p>
<p>Erythromycin is inactivated by gastric enzymes hence it is administered as protected enteric coated tablets.</p>
<p>It is hydrolyzed in the 1^{st} phase metabolism to release the active erythromycin.</p>
<p>It is dissolved and absorbed in the small intestines where it undergoes enetro hepatic recirculation.</p>
<p>â€¢ Distribution is very good as it is well distributed in the spleen, liver, placenta, breast milk and inflamed meninges.</p>
<p>â€¢ Excretion 90% in feaces and small amounts in urine.</p>
<p>Dosage and route of administration</p>
<ul>
<li>Orally adults and children above 8years 250-500mg 6 hourly.</li>
<li>Maximum dose is 4g in severe infections.</li>
<li>Children up to 2years 125mg 6hourly.</li>
<li>IV infusion 25-50/kg body wt. daily as continuous infusion.</li>
</ul>
<p>Drug interaction</p>
<p>Macrolides are enzyme inhibitor and they interfere with the metabolism of drugs like warfarin, carbamazepine, theophylline , corticosteroids, oral contraceptives, digoxin, and cyloserine and sodium valproate</p>
<ul>
<li>food tends to decrease the absorption of macrolide, hence should be given one hour before food or 2-3 hours after meals.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Azithromycin</p>
<ul>
<li>azithromycin is derived from erythromycin by adding a methylated nitrogen into the lactogen ring,</li>
<li>Its specrum of activity and clinical uses are virtually identical to those of clarithromycin.</li>
<li>Azithromycin is active against mycobacteria avium complex and toxoplasma gondii</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="sulphonamide">sulphonamide<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sulphonamide" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>These are among the first antibacterial drugs to be discovered in 1935.</li>
<li>Examples</li>
<li>Sulphfamethoxazole,</li>
<li>sulphadiazine,</li>
<li>sulfisoxazole,</li>
<li>sulphadimidine,</li>
<li>sulfasazine,</li>
<li>sulfametopyrazine,</li>
<li>sulphaloxate</li>
</ul>
<p>pharmacokinetics</p>
<ul>
<li>they have good absorption except a few of them sulpadiazine and which are poorly absorbed in the gut.</li>
<li>Distribution widely distributed in body tissues and fluid including crossing the BBB.</li>
<li>They are metabolized in the liver withhalf life of 10 hours.</li>
<li>Majority are excreted in urine hence dose should be reduced in renal impairment.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Side and adverse effects</p>
<p>â€¢ Hypersensitivity including Stevens-Johnson syndrome</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Do not administer TMP-SMZ to clients with allergies to: Sulfonamides (sulfa), Thiazide diuretics [hydrochlorothiazide (HCTZ)] , Sulfonylurea-type oral hypoglycemics [tolbutamide (Orinase)], Loop diuretics [furosemide (Lasix)]</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Stop TMP-SMZ at the first indication of hypersensitivity, such as rash.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>â€¢ Blood dyscrasias (hemolytic anemia, agranulocytosis, aplastic anemia) â€¢</p>
<p>-Draw the clientâ€™s baseline and periodic CBC levels to detect any hematologic disorders.</p>
<ul>
<li>Observe for any bleeding episodes, sore throat, or pallor. â€¢ If the above symptoms occur, instruct clients to notify the provider.</li>
</ul>
<p>â€¢ Crystalluria</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Maintain adequate oral fluid intake.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Instruct client to drink 2 to 3 L/day.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>â€¢ Kernicterus (jaundice, increased bilirubin levels)</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Avoid administering TMP-SMZ to women who are pregnant near term, breastfeeding mothers, and infants younger than 2 months.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Monitor the clientâ€™s liver function. Photosensitivity</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Avoid prolonged exposure to sunlight, use sunscreen, and wear appropriate</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>cotrimoxazole(sulphonamides 400mg/trimethoprim 80mg) serpin.</p>
<ul>
<li>. This has replaced use of sulphonamide due to resistance.</li>
</ul>
<p>Dosage for children</p>
<ul>
<li>6weeks to 5months 120mg every 12 hours</li>
<li>6months to 5years 240mg 10 hourly</li>
<li>6years to 12 years 480mg 12hourly</li>
</ul>
<p>Indications</p>
<ul>
<li>Pneumocystic carinii pneumonia</li>
<li>Toxoplasmosis</li>
<li>UTI</li>
<li>sometimes chronic bronchitis</li>
<li>Others sulphonamides are used for topical application for prophylaxis of burns, leg ulcers, pressure sores because of their wide anti bacteria spectrum</li>
</ul>
<p>drug Interactions Medication/Food Interactions Nursing Interventions/Client Education</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Sulfonamides can increase the effects of warfarin (Coumadin), phenytoin (Dilantin), sulfonylurea oral hypoglycemic, and tolbutamide (Orinase) by inhibiting hepatic metabolism.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>dosages of these medications may be required during therapy.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Nursing Administration Instruct clients to take the drugs on an empty stomach with a full glass of water. (Plenty of oral fluids)</p>
<ul>
<li>Instruct clients to complete the prescribed course of antimicrobial therapy, even though symptoms may resolve before the full course is completed.</li>
</ul>
<p>Nursing Evaluation of Medication Effectiveness</p>
<ul>
<li>Depending on therapeutic intent, effectiveness may be evidenced by: Improvement of infection symptoms, such as improvement of urinary tract symptoms (decreased frequency, burning, and pain during urination) and negative urine cultures</li>
</ul>
<p>AZOLES</p>
<ul>
<li>This includes several classes of drugs e.g. metronidazole and tinidazole which have both anti bacteria and anti protozoal activity.</li>
<li>others are fluconazole, itraconazole econazole, ketoconazole, and miconazole which are anti fungal drugs .( to be covered under anti fungal drugs)</li>
<li>others are mebendazole, thiabendazole, which are anti helminths (to be covered under ant-helminths)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>metronidazole</p>
<ul>
<li>It is very effective against anaerobic bacterial and protozoa.</li>
</ul>
<p>Pharmacodynamics/MOA</p>
<ul>
<li>metronidazole is converted into an active form and bind to the bacterial DNA and prevents nucleic acid formation which consequently interferes with bacterial replication hence its bacteriostatic.</li>
</ul>
<p>Pharmacokinetics;</p>
<p>well absorbed after oral and rectal administration</p>
<p>Distribution is wide.</p>
<p>Metabolism is in the liver.</p>
<p>It is excreted in urine partly unchanged and partly as metabolite.</p>
<p>Half life is 8 hours.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="indications">indications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#indications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>used for treatment of sepsis caused by orgasms like Bacteroides
and anaerobic cocci.</li>
<li>Intra-abdominal infections</li>
<li>Septicemia, wounds, pelvic infection</li>
<li>Osteomyelitis.</li>
<li>pelvic infections</li>
<li>Infections of the brain and lungs.</li>
