<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="assignment">Assignment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assignment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Find out the standard 1st line and the 2nd line ART regime in children.</p>
<p>ANALGESICS, NON STEROIDAL ANTI INFLAMMATORY DRUGS(NSAIDS)</p>
<ul>
<li>Analgesics may be defined as any member or group of drugs used to achieve analgesia, relief from pain. They relieve pain without causing any loss of consciousness.</li>
<li>Analgesics drug works in various ways on the periphery and the CNS.</li>
<li>NSAIDs are referred to as non narcotic analgesics or non-opioid analgesics.</li>
<li>They differ from opioids in the aspects;
-they are less potent
-fail to produce drowsiness or CNS depression
-non additive in nature
-posses anti inflammatory/antipyretic activities</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nsaids-cont">NSAIDs cont.'<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nsaids-cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>1st generation NSAIDs (COX-1 and COX-2 inhibitors):</li>
<li>Aspirin</li>
<li>Ibuprofen (Motrin, Advil)</li>
<li>Naproxen (Naprosyn)</li>
<li>Indomethacin (Indocin)</li>
<li>Diclofenac (Voltaren)</li>
<li>Ketorolac (Toradol)</li>
<li>Meloxicam (Mobic)</li>
<li>2nd generation NSAIDs (selective COX-2 Inhibitor):</li>
<li>Celecoxib (Celebrex)</li>
</ul>
<p>Mechanism of action</p>
<p>â€¢ Inhibition of prostaglandin synthase, also known as cox â€” Inhibition of COX-1 can result in decreased platelet aggregation and kidney damage.</p>
<p>â€¢ Inhibition of COX-2 results in decreased inflammation, fever, and pain.</p>
<p>Therapeutic Uses /indication ( analgesic , antipyretic, and anti inflammatory)</p>
<p>â€¢ Inflammation suppression.</p>
<p>â€¢ Analgesia for mild to moderate pain, such as with osteoarthritis and rheumatoid arthritis.</p>
<p>â€¢ Fever reduction.</p>
<p>â€¢ Dysmenorrhea.</p>
<p>â€¢ Inhibition of platelet aggregation, which protects against stroke and myocardial infarction. (aspirin)</p>
<p>â€¢ The exception of acetaminophen which is an analgesic and antipyretic.</p>
<p>Side/Adverse Effects Nursing Interventions/Client Education</p>
<ul>
<li>Gastrointestinal discomfort (dyspepsia, abdominal pain, heartburn, nausea)</li>
<li>Damage to gastric mucosa may lead to GI bleeding and perforation, especially with long-term use. â€¢</li>
<li>Advise clients to take medication with food or with a full glass of water or milk.</li>
<li>Advise clients to avoid alcohol.</li>
<li>Observe for signs of bleeding (passage of black or dark-colored stools, severe abdominal pain, nausea, vomiting).</li>
<li>Administer a proton pump inhibitor, such as omeprazole (Prilosec), or an H2 receptor antagonist, such as ranitidine (Zantac) to decrease the risk of ulcer formation. Use prophylaxis agents such as misoprostol (Cytotec).</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>side/adverse effects cont.â€™</p>
<p>Renal dysfunction (decreased urine output, weight gain from fluid retention, increased BUN and creatinine levels)</p>
<p>â€¢ Use cautiously with older adults and clients who have heart failure.</p>
<p>â€¢ Monitor I&amp;O and kidney function (BUN, creatinine).</p>
<p>Increased risk of heart attack and stroke (non aspirin NSAIDs)</p>
<p>â€¢ Use the smallest effective dose for clients with known cardiovascular disease.</p>
<p>â€¢ Salicylism may occur with aspirin. Signs and symptoms include tinnitus, sweating, headache and dizziness, and respiratory alkalosis.</p>
<p>â€¢ Advise clients to notify the provider and to stop taking aspirin if symptoms occur.</p>
<p>â€¢ Reyer syndrome is rare, but serious in childhood.</p>
<p>â€¢ This occurs when aspirin is used for fever reduction in children who have a viral illness, such as chickenpox or influenza</p>
<p>â€¢ Advise clients to avoid giving aspirin when a child has a viral illness, such as chickenpox or influenza.</p>
<p>Complication and adverse effects cont.'</p>
<p>Aspirin toxicity</p>
<p>â€¢ Aspirin toxicity should be managed as a medical emergency in the hospital.</p>
<p>Therapy includes:</p>
<p>â€¢ Cooling with tepid water.</p>
<p>â€¢ Correction of dehydration and electrolyte imbalance with IV fluids.</p>
<p>â€¢ Reversal of acidosis and promotion of salicylate excretion with bicarbonate.</p>
<p>â€¢ Gastric lavage Activated charcoal may also be given to decrease absorption.</p>
<p>â€¢ Hemodialysis may be indicated.</p>
<p>Contraindications for aspirin and other 1st generation NSAIDs include</p>
<ul>
<li>Pregnancy (Pregnancy Risk Category D)</li>
<li>Peptic ulcer disease</li>
<li>Bleeding disorders such as hemophilia, vitamin K deficiency</li>
<li>Hypersensitivity to aspirin and other NSAIDs</li>
<li>Children with chickenpox or influenza (aspirin)</li>
<li>Use NSAIDs cautiously in older adults, clients who smoke cigarettes, and in clients with H. pylori infection, hypovolemia, asthma, chronic urticaria, and/or a history of alcoholism.</li>
<li>Celecoxib is contraindicated in clients with allergy to sulfonamides.</li>
<li>Ketorolac is contraindicated in clients with advanced renal dysfunction</li>
<li>Use should be no longer than five days because of the risk for kidney damage.</li>
<li>2nd generation NSAIDs should be used cautiously in clients who have known cardiovascular disease.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="acetaminophen">acetaminophen<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#acetaminophen" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="mechanism-of-action">Mechanism Of Action;<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mechanism-of-action" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Acetaminophen slows the production of prostaglandins in the central nervous system.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="therapeutic-uses">Therapeutic Uses<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#therapeutic-uses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Analgesic (relief of pain) effect</li>
<li>Antipyretic (reduction of fever) effects</li>
</ul>
<p>complications Side/Adverse Effects Nursing Interventions/Client Education</p>
<p>Acute toxicity that results in liver damage with early symptoms of nausea, vomiting, diarrhea, sweating, and abdominal discomfort progressing to, hepatic failure, coma and death</p>
<p>â€¢ Advise clients to take acetaminophen as prescribed and not to exceed 4 g/day.</p>
<p>â€¢ Administer the antidote, acetylcysteine (Mucomyst).</p>
<p>Contraindications/Precautions</p>
<p>â€¢ Use cautiously in clients who consume three or more alcoholic drinks/day and those taking warfarin (interferes with metabolism).</p>
<p>Medication/Food Interactions Nursing Interventions/Client Education</p>
<p>Alcohol increases the risk of liver damage.</p>
<p>â€¢ Advise clients about the potential risk of liver damage with consumption of alcohol.</p>
<p>Acetaminophen slows metabolism of warfarin (Coumadin) leading to increased levels of warfarin.</p>
<p>â€¢ This places clients at risk for bleeding.</p>
<p>â€¢ Instruct clients to observe for signs of bleeding (bruising, petechiae, hematuria).</p>
<p>â€¢ Monitor prothrombin time and INR levels and adjust dosages of warfarin accordingly</p>
<p>Opioid analgesics/narcotic analgesics</p>
<p>â€¢ Opioids are classified as agonists, agonist-antagonists, and antagonist.</p>
<p>Opioid Agonists</p>
<p>â€¢ morphine sulfate</p>
<p>â€¢ Fentanyl (Sublimaze, Duragesic)</p>
<p>â€¢ Meperidine (Demerol)</p>
<p>â€¢ Methadone (Dolophine)</p>
<p>â€¢ Codeine, oxycodone (OxyContin)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mechanism-of-action">Mechanism of action<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mechanism-of-action" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Opioid agonist produce analgesia by binding to specific proteinscoupled receptors that are located in the brain and the spinal cord regions involved in the transmission and modulation of pain</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="indication-therapeutic-uses">Indication/Therapeutic Uses<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#indication-therapeutic-uses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Relief of moderate to severe pain (postoperative, myocardial infarction, cancer)</li>
<li>Sedation</li>
<li>Reduction of bowel motility</li>
<li>Codeine: cough suppression</li>
</ul>
<p>route of administration</p>
<ul>
<li>Morphine sulfate â€“ Oral, subcutaneous, IM, rectal, IV, epidural, and intrathecal</li>
<li>Fentanyl (Sublimaze, Duragesic) â€“ IV, IM, transmucosal and transdermal</li>
<li>Meperidine (Demerol) â€“ Oral, subcutaneous IM, and IV</li>
<li>Codeine â€“ Oral, subcutaneous IM, and IV</li>
<li>Methadone (Dolophine) â€“ Oral, subcutaneous, and IM</li>
<li>Oxycodone (OxyContin) â€“ Oral, rectal</li>
<li>Hydromorphone (Dilaudid) â€“ Oral, subcutaneous, IM, IV</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Side/Adverse Effects Nursing Interventions/Client Education (morphine sulphate)</p>
<p>Respiratory depression.</p>
<p>â€¢ Monitor the clientâ€™s vital signs.</p>
<p>â€¢ Stop opioids if the clientâ€™s respiratory rate is less than 12/ min, and then notify the provider.</p>
<p>â€¢ Have naloxone (Narcan) and resuscitation equipment available.</p>
<p>â€¢ Avoid the use of opioids with CNS depressant medications (barbiturates, benzodiazepines, and consumption of alcohol).</p>
<p>Constipation</p>
<p>â€¢ Increased fluid intake and physical activity.</p>
<p>â€¢ Administer a stimulant laxative, such as Bisacodyl (Dulcolax), to counteract decreased bowel motility, or a stool softener, such as docusate sodium (Colace), to prevent constipation.</p>
<p>Side/ adverse effects cont.'</p>
<p>Orthostatic hypotension</p>
<ul>
<li>Advise clients to sit or lie down if symptoms of lightheadedness or dizziness occur.</li>
<li>Avoid sudden changes in position by slowly moving clients from a lying to a sitting or standing position.</li>
<li>Provide assistance with ambulation as needed.</li>
</ul>
<p>Urinary retention</p>
<ul>
<li>Advise clients to void every 4 hr.</li>
<li>Monitor I&amp;O.</li>
<li>Assess the clientâ€™s bladder for distention by palpating the lower abdomen area every 4 to 6 hr. side and adverse effects</li>
</ul>
<p>Adverse effects cont.'</p>
<p>Cough suppression</p>
<p>Advise clients to cough at regular intervals to prevent accumulation of secretions in the airway.</p>
<p>Auscultate the clientâ€™s lungs for crackles, and instruct clients to increase intake of fluid to liquefy secretions.</p>
<p>Sedation</p>
<p>Advise clients to avoid hazardous activities such as driving or operating heavy machinery.</p>
<p>Biliary colic</p>
<p>Avoid giving morphine to clients who have a history of biliary colic. Use meperidine as an alternative.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="emesis">Emesis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#emesis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Administer an antiemetic such as promethazine (Phenergan).</li>
</ul>
<p>Opioid overdose triad of coma, respiratory depression, and pinpoint pupils</p>
<ul>
<li>Monitor the client's vital signs.</li>
<li>Provide mechanical ventilation.</li>
<li>Administer opioid antagonists, such as naloxone (Narcan) or nalmefene (Revex)</li>
</ul>
<p>Contraindications/Precautions</p>
<ul>
<li>Morphine is contraindicated after biliary tract surgery.</li>
<li>Morphine is contraindicated for premature infants during and after delivery because of respiratory depressant effects.</li>
<li>Meperidine is contraindicated for clients with renal failure because of the accumulation of normeperidine, which can result in seizures and neurotoxicity.</li>
</ul>
<p>Use cautiously with: Clients who have asthma, emphysema, and/or head injuries; infants, and older adults.</p>
<p>Use cautiously with:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Clients who have asthma, emphysema, and/or head injuries; infants, and older adult clients (risk of respiratory depression).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Clients who are pregnant (risk of physical dependence of the fetus).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Clients in labor (risk of respiratory depression in the newborn and inhibition of labor by decreasing uterine contractions)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Clients who are extremely obese (greater risk for prolonged side effects because of the accumulation of medication that is metabolized at a slower rate)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Clients with inflammatory bowel disease (risk of megacolon or paralytic ileus)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Clients with an enlarged prostate (risk of acute urinary retention)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Clients with hepatic or renal disease</p>
</li>
<li></li>
</ul>
<p>Opioid agonist-antagonist</p>
<ul>
<li>butorphanol (Stadol)</li>
<li>Nalbuphine hydrochloride (Nubain)</li>
<li>Buprenorphine hydrochloride (Buprenex)</li>
</ul>
<p>Expected Pharmacological Action</p>
<ul>
<li>These medications act as antagonists on mu receptors and agonists on kappa receptors.</li>
</ul>
<p>Compared to pure opioid agonists, agonist-antagonists have:</p>
<ul>
<li>A low potential for abuse causing little euphoria.</li>
<li>In fact, high doses can cause adverse effects (anxiety, restlessness, mental confusion).</li>
<li>Less respiratory depression.</li>
<li>Less analgesic effect.</li>
</ul>
<p>opioid agonist- antagonist</p>
<p>cont.â€™ |</p>
<p>Indication</p>
<p>â€¢ Relief of moderate to severe pain</p>
<p>â€¢ Treatment of opioid dependence (buprenorphine)</p>
<p>â€¢ Adjunct to balanced anesthesia</p>
<p>â€¢ Relief of labor pain (butorphanol)</p>
<p>Route of administration:</p>
<p>â€¢ Butorphanol â€“ IV, IM, intranasal</p>
<p>â€¢ Nalbuphine â€“ IV, IM, subcutaneous</p>
<p>â€¢ Buprenorphine â€“ IV, sublingual, epidural</p>
<p>Side effects</p>
<p>Abstinence syndrome (cramping, hypertension, vomiting )</p>
<p>Sedation respiratory depression</p>
<p>Dizziness</p>
<p>Increased intracranial pressure, headache</p>
<p>Contraindications/Precautions</p>
<p>Use cautiously in clients who have a history of myocardial infarction, renal or liver disease, respiratory depression, or head injury, and clients who are physically dependent on opioids.</p>
<p>Interactions medication/Food Interactions Nursing Interventions/Client Education</p>
<p>â€¢ CNS depressants and alcohol may cause additive effects.</p>
<p>â€¢ Use together cautiously.</p>
<p>â€¢ Monitor respirations.</p>
<p>â€¢ Opioid agonists may antagonize and reduce analgesic effects of the opioid. Do not use concurrently.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="opioid-antagonist">Opioid antagonist<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#opioid-antagonist" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Naloxone (Narcan)</li>
<li>Naltrexone (Re Via, Depade ),</li>
<li>nalmefene (Revex )</li>
</ul>
<p>Mechanism of Action Opioid antagonists interfere with the action of opioids by competing for opioid receptors. Opioid antagonists have no effect in the absence of opioids.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="therapeutic-uses">Therapeutic Uses<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#therapeutic-uses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Treatment of opioid overdose Reversal of effects of opioids, such as respiratory depression
Reversal of respiratory depression in an infant</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="route-of-administration">Route of administration:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#route-of-administration" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Naloxone- IM, IV, subcutaneous
nalmefene - IV, IM, subcutaneous
Naltrexone - Oral</p>
<p>Opioid antagonist cont.â€™</p>
<p>Therapeutic Uses</p>
<p>Treatment of opioid overdose Reversal of effects of opioids, such as respiratory depression</p>
<p>Reversal of respiratory depression in an infant</p>
<p>Route of administration:</p>
<p>Naloxone,</p>
<p>nalmefene â€“ IV, IM, subcutaneous</p>
<p>Naltrexone â€“ Oral</p>
<p>Opioid anti-agonist cont.â€™</p>
<p>Side Effects</p>
<p>â€¢ Tachycardia and tachypnea</p>
<p>â€¢ Abstinence syndrome (cramping, hypertension, vomiting)</p>
<p>â€¢ Pulmonary edema</p>
<p>Contraindications/Precautions</p>
<p>â€¢ Opioid antagonists are Pregnancy Risk Category B.</p>
<p>â€¢ These medications are contraindicated in clients with opioid dependency.</p>
<p>Adjuvants medication for pain</p>
<p>â€¢ Tricyclic antidepressants: amitriptyline (Elavil) â€“ oral/IM</p>
<p>â€¢ Anticonvulsants: carbamazepine (Tegretol) â€“ gabapentin (Neurontin) oral</p>
<p>â€¢ CNS stimulants: methylphenidate (Ritalin) â€“ oral</p>
<p>â€¢ Antihistamines: hydroxyzine (Vistaril) â€“ oral/IM</p>
<p>â€¢ Glucocorticoids: dexamethasone (Decadron) â€“ oral, IV, IM</p>
<p>â€¢ Bisphosphonates: etidronate (Didronel) â€“ oral</p>
<p>â€¢ NSAIDs: ibuprofen (Motrin) â€“ oral</p>
<p>â€¢ Other Medication: Tricyclic antidepressants: imipramine (Tofranil) â€“ oral</p>
<p>â€¢ Anticonvulsants: phenytoin (Dilantin) â€“ oral, IV, IM</p>
<p>â€¢ CNS stimulants: dextroamphetamine (Dexedrine) â€“ oral</p>
<p>â€¢ Glucocorticoids: prednisone (Deltasone) â€“ oral</p>
<p>â€¢ Bisphosphonates: pamidronate (Aredia) â€“ IV</p>
<p>â€¢ NSAIDs: ketorolac (Toradol)</p>
<p>Expected Pharmacological Action</p>
<p>â€¢ Adjuvant medications for pain enhance the effects of opioids</p>
<p>Therapeutic Uses</p>
<p>â€¢ These medications are used in combination with opioids and cannot be used as a substitute for opioids.</p>
<p>â€¢ NSAIDs are used to treat inflammation.</p>
<p>â€¢ Tricyclic antidepressants are used to treat depression and neuropathic pain such as cramping, aching, burning, darting, and lancinating pain.</p>
<p>â€¢ Anticonvulsants are used to relieve neuropathic pain.</p>
<p>â€¢ CNS stimulants augment analgesia and decrease sedation.</p>
<p>â€¢ Antihistamines decrease anxiety, prevent insomnia and relieve nausea.</p>
<p>â€¢ Glucocorticoids decrease pain from intracranial pressure and spinal cord compression.</p>
<p>â€¢ Bisphosphonates manage hypercalcemia and bone pain</p>
<p>ANTI HELMINTHIC</p>
<p>â€¢ Benzimidazole (BZAs)</p>
<p>These are broad spectrum anthelmintic agents.</p>
<p>Thiabendazole., Mebendazole and Albendazole have been used extensively for human helminth infections.</p>
<p>â€¢ Other drugs are ;pyrantel pamoate, ivermectin, praziquental, piperazine citrate , benzdiazepines and diethylcarbamazine.</p>
<p>Indication/uses;</p>
<p>Thiabendazole is active against a wide range of nematodes that infect the GI tract but it clinical use has declined due to its toxicity.</p>
<p>Mebendazole is used for the treatment of intestinal roundworm infections.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="anthelminthic-cont">Anthelminthic cont.'<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#anthelminthic-cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Albendazole is used primarily against a variety of intestinal and tissue nematodes but also against Larva forms of certain cestodes (cysticercosis, hydatidosis)</li>
<li>Used with ivermectin or diethylcarbamazine for control of helminthes</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="anthelminthics-action">Anthelminthics action<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#anthelminthics-action" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The BZAs inhibit microtubule polymerization by binding to b-tubulin.</li>
<li>Mebendazole and Albendazole are highly effective in treating the major infections (ascariasis, enterobiasis, trichuriasis, and hookworm)'
-These drugs are active against both larva and adult stages of the nematodes, and they are ovicidal for ascaris and trichuris .
-Immobilization and death of susceptible GI parasites occur slowly and their clearance from the GI tract may not be complete until several days after treatment.
Albendazole is more effective than mebendazole for strongyloidiasis, cystic hydatid disease caused By Echinococcus Granulosus And Neurocysticercosis</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="anthelminthic-cont">Anthelminthic cont.'<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#anthelminthic-cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The choice of drug depends on specific helminths involved</li>
<li>Example cestodes infestations e.g. echinococcus granulosus the drugs used are thiabendazole, Albendazole, piperazine citrate, pyrantel pamoate, ivermectin and diethylcarbamazine (hetrazan).</li>
</ul>
<p>Absorption, fate, and excretion</p>
<ul>
<li>thiabendazole is absorbed rapidly after oal ingestion and reaches peak plasma concentration after 1 hour. Most of the drug is excreted in urine.</li>
<li>Mebendazole is rapidly metabolized resulting to low systemic bioavailability.</li>
<li>Albendazole is variably absorbed after oral administration, a fatty meal enhances absorption. It is well distributed into various tissues including hydatid cysts. It excreted in urine.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="antimalarial">antimalarial<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#antimalarial" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="anti-malaria-cont">anti-malaria cont.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#anti-malaria-cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Other anti-malarial drugs for uncomplicated malaria are;</li>
<li>Amodiaquine plus artesunate</li>
<li>Mefloquine plus artesunate</li>
<li>Halofantrine (halfan) .this drug can cause arrhythmias, and is contraindicated in patients with heart disease.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="quinine">Quinine<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#quinine" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Quinine is an alkaloid derived from cinchona tree.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="indication">Indication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#indication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Reserved for severe and complicated malaria.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pharmacodynamics-mechanism-of-action">Pharmacodynamics/mechanism of action<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pharmacodynamics-mechanism-of-action" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>It binds to plasmodium DNA to prevent protein synthesis but its exact mode of action remains uncertain.</li>
<li>It is used to treat plasmodium falciparum in areas of multiple drug resistant.</li>
</ul>
<p>pharmacokinetics</p>
<ul>
<li>Quinine is well absorbed in the gut but absorption is delayed by antacids. It can be given via slow IV Infusion.</li>
<li>Metabolism occurs in the liver, the excretion is in the kidneys.</li>
<li>It is used for the treat of chloroquine resistant P . falciparum often With Combination Of Pyrimethamine/ Sulfadoxine</li>
</ul>
<p>unwanted effects</p>
<ul>
<li>has a low therapeutic widow and it produces effects in the skeletal muscles and can cause; GI irritation, renal damage, hemolytic anemia (rarely)associated with â€œblack water feverâ€ in previously sensitized patients.</li>
<li>black water fever has a fatality rate of 25% due to intravascular coagulation and renal failure.</li>
</ul>
<p>unwanted effects cont.â€™</p>
<p>â€¢ Hypotension</p>
<p>â€¢ Hypoglycemia</p>
<p>â€¢ Cinchonism</p>
<p>Dosage;</p>
<p>Loading dose IV Quinine 20mg/kg body wt. in 500mls of 5% or 10% dextrose (MAX 1200MG) for 4 hours then 10mg/kg body wt. as intravenous infusion in 500mls of 5% or 10% dextrose to run for 4hrs every 8 hourly ( maximum 600mgs)</p>
<p>After 3 IV doses of quinine, one should try to change into oral treatment and treatment should continue for 7 days.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="quinine-cont">quinine cont.'<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#quinine-cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>for children loading dose is <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>20</mn><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">g</mi></mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">/</mi><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">k</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">g</mi></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">20 \mathrm{mg} / \mathrm{kg}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em;
