<ul>
<li>Potassium-sparing diuretics are combined with other diuretics for potassium-sparing effects.</li>
<li>Potassium-sparing diuretics are used for heart failure.</li>
<li>In primary hyperaldosteronism, potassium-sparing diuretics block actions of aldosterone.</li>
<li>Route of administration: Oral</li>
</ul>
<p>Side/Adverse Effects;</p>
<ul>
<li>Hyperkalemia (K+ greater than 5.0 mEq/L)</li>
<li>Endocrine effects (impotence in male clients; irregularities of menstrual cycle in female clients)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Contraindications/Precaution</p>
<ul>
<li>Do not administer to clients who have hyperkalemia.</li>
<li>Potassium-sparing diuretics are contraindicated in clients who have severe renal failure and anuria.</li>
</ul>
<p>Medication/Food Interaction</p>
<ul>
<li>Concurrent use of ACE inhibitors increases the risk of hyperkalemia</li>
<li>Concurrent use of potassium supplements increases the risk of hyperkalemia</li>
</ul>
<p>Nursing Administration</p>
<ul>
<li>Obtain the clientâ€™s baseline data.</li>
<li>Monitor the clientâ€™s potassium levels regularly.</li>
<li>Can only be given orally.</li>
<li>Teach clients to avoid salt substitutes that contain potassium.</li>
<li>Teach clients to self-monitor blood pressure.</li>
<li>Instruct clients to keep a log of blood pressure and weight.</li>
<li>Warn clients that triamterene may turn urine a bluish color.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="d-osmotic-diuretics">d)Osmotic Diuretics<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#d-osmotic-diuretics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>mannitol (Osmitrol)</li>
<li>Expected Pharmacological Action</li>
<li>Osmotic diuretics reduce intracranial pressure and intraocular pressure by raising serum osmolality and drawing fluid back into the vascular and extravascular space.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="therapeutic-uses">Therapeutic Uses<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#therapeutic-uses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Osmotic diuretics prevent renal failure in specific situations, such as hypovolemic shock and severe hypotension.</li>
<li>These medications decrease intracranial pressure (ICP) caused by cerebral edema.</li>
<li>These medications decrease intraocular pressure (IOP).</li>
<li>Osmotic diuretics promote sodium retention and water excretion in clients with hyponatremia and fluid volume excess</li>
</ul>
<p>Side/Adverse Effects</p>
<ul>
<li>Renal failure</li>
<li>Heart failure, pulmonary edema</li>
<li>Fluid and electrolyte imbalances</li>
</ul>
<p>Contraindications/Precautions</p>
<ul>
<li>Use extreme caution in clients with heart failure.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Interactions</p>
<ul>
<li>Furosemide contributes to therapeutic effect by promoting renal excretion of fluid drawn into vasculature by osmotic diuretics.</li>
</ul>
<p>Nursing Administration</p>
<p>Administer mannitol by continuous IV infusion.</p>
<p>To prevent administering microscopic crystals, use a filter needle when drawing from the vial and a filter in the IV tubing.</p>
<p>Monitor daily weight, I &amp; 0, and serum electrolytes.</p>
<p>Monitor for signs of dehydration, acute renal failure, and edema.</p>
<p>Use of furosemide may help prevent rebound fluid retention; this contributes to therapeutic effect.</p>
<p>Carbonic anhydrase inhibitors</p>
<ul>
<li>Blockade of carbonic anhydrase activity induces a sodium bicarbonate diuresis, which reduces body bicarbonate levels.</li>
<li>These drugs include;</li>
<li>Acetazolamide (DIAMOX)</li>
<li>Dichlorphenamide (DARANIDE)</li>
<li>Methazolamide (GLAUCTABS)</li>
</ul>
<p>Acetazolamide administration causes a reduction in aqueous humour and CSF fluid production</p>
<p>acetazolamide cont.â€™</p>
<ul>
<li>the proximal tubule is the major site of action of carbonic anhydrase inhibitors.</li>
<li>the collecting duct is the secondary site of action .</li>
</ul>
<p>Clinical application</p>
<p>Glaucoma; because acetazolamide decreases the rate of aqueous humor production, a decline in IOP occurs.</p>
<p>The major indication of carbonate anhydrase inhibitor is open angle glaucoma.</p>
<p>It may also be given in secondary glaucoma</p>
<p>Preoperatively in acute angle glaucoma.</p>
<p>Treatment of epilepsy.</p>
<p>Altitude sickness familial periodic paralysis</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="toxicity">toxicity<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#toxicity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Hyper chloremic acidosis.</li>
<li>Renal potassium loss.</li>
</ul>
<p>Contraindication
Hepatic cirrhosis.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="antihypertensive">antihypertensive<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#antihypertensive" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cardiovascular-pharmacology">Cardiovascular pharmacology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cardiovascular-pharmacology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Antihypertensive drugs potential drug targets;</li>
<li>CNS: decrease sympathetic tone</li>
<li>Heart: decrease cardiac out put</li>
<li>Veins: dilate; decrease preload</li>
<li>arterioles: dilate; decrease preload</li>
<li>Kidneys: increase diuresis; inhibit renin angiotensin aldosterone</li>
</ul>
<p>Classification of anti hypertensives</p>
<ul>
<li>diuretics:</li>
</ul>
<p>âœ“Thiazide and related agents (hydrochlorothiazide, chlorthalidone)</p>
<p>âœ“Loop diuretics (furosemide, bumetanide,, torsemide, ethacrynic)</p>
<p>âœ“Potassium sparing diuretics (amiloride, triamterene, spironolactone)</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Angiotensin-converting enzyme (ACE) inhibitors ( captopril, enalapril, lisinopril, quinapril, Ramipril, benazepril)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Angiotensin II receptor blockers (ARBS)</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>(losartan, candesartan, Irbesartan, valsartan, telmisartan, eprosartan)</p>
<ul>
<li>Calcium channel blockers (CCB)</li>
</ul>
<p>(verapamil, diltiazem, nifedipine, felodipine, nicardipine, isradipine, amlodipine)</p>
<p>Classification of antihypertensive</p>
<p>Vasodilators
âœ“ Arterial ( hydralazine, minoxidil, diazoxide fenoldopam)
âœ“ Arterial and venous (nitroprusside)
Sympatholytic drugs
Alpha adrenergic blockers; (prazosin, terazosin, doxazosin, phentolamine, phenoxybenzamine)
Beta adrenergic blockers; (metoprolol, atenolol, etc )
Mixed adrenergic; ( labetalol, carvedilol)
Centrally acting alpha2 agonists (methyldopa, clonidine, guanabenz)
Adrenergic neuron blocking agents;( guanethidine, reserpine)</p>
<p>: Angiotensin-Converting Enzyme (ACE) Inhibitors</p>
<p>captopril (Capoten)</p>
<p>â€¢ Other Medications: Enalapril (Vasotec), Enalaprilat (Vasotec IV), Fosinopril (Monopril), Lisinopril (Prinivil), Ramipril (Altace)</p>
<p>Mechanism of action</p>
<p>ACEIs prevents conversion of angiotensin I to angiotensin II which is a potent vasoconstrictor. this causes vasodilation, reduces peripheral resistance, and decreases secretion of aldosterone (thereby resulting in decrease sodium and water retention and extracellular volume)</p>
<p>Merits of ACEIs</p>
<ul>
<li>Safe for asthmatics, diabetics</li>
<li>Absence of rebound hypertension upon abrupt withdrawal.</li>
<li>Total absence of postural hypotension.</li>
<li>maintains renal blood flow.</li>
<li>devoid of electrolyte imbalance.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li>Therapeutic Uses</li>
<li>Hypertension</li>
<li>Heart failure</li>
<li>Myocardial infarction (To decrease mortality and to decrease risk of heart failure and left ventricular dysfunction)</li>
<li>Diabetic and nondiabetic nephropathy</li>
<li>For clients at high risk for a cardiovascular event, Ramipril can be used to prevent MI, stroke, or death.</li>
</ul>
<p>Side/Adverse Effects</p>
<ul>
<li>Cough related to inhibition of kinase II (alternative name for ACE) which results in increase in bradykinin</li>
<li>First-dose orthostatic hypotension.</li>
<li>Hyperkalemia</li>
</ul>
<p>Rash and dysgeusia (altered taste), primarily with captopril</p>
<ul>
<li>Angioedema.</li>
<li>Neutropenia (rare but serious complication of captopril)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Contraindications/Precautions</p>
<ul>
<li>These medications are Pregnancy Risk Category D during the second and third trimester, related to fetal injury.</li>
<li>renal stenosis when present bilaterally or in a single remaining kidney.</li>
<li>history of angioedema following use of ACE inhibitor.</li>
<li>Use cautiously in clients with renal impairment and</li>
<li>collagen vascular disease because they are at greater risk for developing neutropenia. Closely monitor these clients for signs of infection.</li>
<li>hypotension</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="medication-food-interactions">Medication/Food Interactions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#medication-food-interactions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Diuretics can contribute to first-dose hypotension</li>
<li>Antihypertensive medications may have an additive hypotensive effect.</li>
<li>Potassium supplements and potassium-sparing diuretics increase the risk of hyperkalemia.</li>
<li>ACE inhibitors can increase levels of lithium carbonate (Eskalith)</li>
<li>Use of NSAIDs may decrease the antihypertensive effect of ACE inhibitors.</li>
</ul>
<p>Nursing Administration</p>
<ul>
<li>Administer ACE inhibitors orally except enalapril, which is the only ACE inhibitor for IV use.</li>
<li>Advise clients that the medication may be prescribed as a single formulation or in combination with hydrochlorothiazide.</li>
<li>Advise clients that blood pressure has to be monitored after the first dose for at least 2 hr. to detect hypotension.</li>
<li>Instruct clients that captopril should be taken at least 1 hr. before meals. All other ACE inhibitors can be taken with or without food.</li>
<li>Advise clients to notify the provider if cough, rash, dysgeusia (lack of taste), and/or signs of infection occur</li>
</ul>
<p>Angiotensin II Receptor Blockers (ARBs)</p>
<p>â€¢ losartan (Cozaar)</p>
<p>â€¢ Other Medications: Valsartan (Diovan) , Irbesartan (Avapro) , Candesartan (Atacand) , Olmesartan (Benicar)</p>
<p>Expected Pharmacological Action</p>
<p>These medications block the action of angiotensin II in the body.</p>
<p>This results in:</p>
<p>â€¢ Vasodilation (mostly arteriole)</p>
<p>â€¢ Excretion of sodium and water, and retention of potassium (through effects on the kidney)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="therapeutic-uses">Therapeutic Uses :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#therapeutic-uses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Hypertension,</li>
<li>Heart failure and prevention of mortality following MI,</li>
<li>Stroke prevention ,</li>
<li>Delay progression of diabetic nephropathy</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="complications">Complications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The major difference between ARBs and ACE inhibitors is that cough and hyperkalemia are not side effects of ARBs</p>
<p>Side/Adverse Effects</p>
<p>â€¢ Angioedema</p>
<p>contraindication</p>
<p>â€¢ Hypersensitivity</p>
<p>â€¢ Pregnancy</p>
<p>â€¢ renal stenosis when present bilaterally or in a single remaining kidney</p>
<p>considerations</p>
<p>monitor BP, HR, Weight, Edema, Blood Urea Nitrogen, Serum Creatinine.</p>
<p>can be used in patients intolerant to aceis (due to cough)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="calcium-channel-blockers">CALCIUM CHANNEL BLOCKERS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#calcium-channel-blockers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Nifedipine (Adalat, Procardia)</li>
<li>Verapamil (Calan)</li>
<li>Amlodipine (Norvasc)</li>
</ul>
<p>Other Medications:</p>
<ul>
<li>Amlodipine (Norvasc)</li>
<li>Felodipine (Plendil)</li>
<li>Nicardipine (Cardene, Cleviprex)</li>
<li>Diltiazem (Cardizem)</li>
</ul>
<p>Mechanism of action of CCB</p>
<p>Mechanism of action of</p>
<p>â€¢ inhibits calcium influx in the smooth muscles and the myocardium.</p>
<p>â€¢ Blocking of calcium channels in blood vessels leads to vasodilation of peripheral arterioles and arteries/arterioles of the heart, slows down heart conduction and reduction of blood pressure.</p>
<p>NIFEDIPINE (ADALAT)</p>
<p>â€¢ give rise to coronary vasodilation.</p>
<p>â€¢ Enhances coronary blood flow.</p>
<p>â€¢ Reduces total periphery resistance, reduces systolic and diastolic pressure</p>
<p>Therapeutic use</p>
<ul>
<li>Chronic angina</li>
<li>Congestive heart failure</li>
<li>Acute myocardial infarction</li>
<li>Peripheral vascular disorders</li>
</ul>
<p>Adverse drug reaction</p>
<p>Palpitation, nausea, vomiting, flushing, headache, edema.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="amlodipine">amlodipine<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#amlodipine" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Serves as a long acting calcium channel blocker.</li>
</ul>
<p>Therapeutic use</p>
<ul>
<li>Treatment of essential hypertension.</li>
<li>Angina pectoris</li>
</ul>
<p>Adverse drug reaction
Palpitation,epixtasis,cough,nocturia,musclecramps,breathless,importen ce, conjunctivitis</p>
<p>verapamil</p>
<ul>
<li>Enhances coronary blood flow rate,vasodilation.</li>
<li>Exerts anti arrhythmic action.</li>
<li>Reduces peripheral resistance.</li>
</ul>
<p>Therapeutic uses</p>
<ul>
<li>Supraventricular tachycardia.</li>
<li>Acute coronary spasms</li>
<li>Angina pectoris</li>
<li>Hypertension with myocardial infarction</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Adverse reaction</p>
<ul>
<li>Dizziness, vertigo, constipation, hypotension, nausea, pedal edema</li>
</ul>
<p>Advantages of calcium channel blockers</p>
<ul>
<li>Exhibits rapid onset and longer duration of action hence administered once a day.</li>
<li>Do not exhibit cardiac depression.</li>
<li>Do not cause adverse effects on the fetus.</li>
<li>Cause no sedation.</li>
<li>Recommended for patients having angina and asthma.</li>
<li>Do not cause male impotence.</li>
<li>Mostly indicated for the elderly, pregnant and asthmatic.</li>
<li>safe with history of renal impairment.</li>
<li>Do not exhibit action on electrolyte balance.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>considerations</p>
<ul>
<li>Monitor BP, HR, rhythm,</li>
<li>Control calcium supplement.</li>
<li>Inform patient not to stop drug abruptly.</li>
<li>Patient to report signs of adverse effects such as irregular heart beat, shortness of breath, oedema in the hands and feet, dizziness, constipation, nausea and hypotension.</li>
<li>Discontinue in breast feeding because they are excreted in breast milk and have potential for adverse effects in neonates.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="direct-acting-vasodilators">DIRECT ACTING VASODILATORS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#direct-acting-vasodilators" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="hydralazine">HYDRALAZINE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hydralazine" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Hydralazine (APRESOLINE) causes direct relaxation of the arterio smooth muscle secondary to a fall in the intracellular calcium. this is associated with powerful stimulation of the sympathetic nervous system, due to baroreceptor mediated reflexes</p>
<p>Toxicity and precaution</p>
<ul>
<li>These includes; headache, nausea, flushing, hypotension, palpitation, tachycardia, dizziness and angina pectoris.</li>
<li>Myocardial ischemia (increased oxygen demand)</li>
<li>Immunological reactions, drug induced lupus syndrome. this occurs after six months of treatment with hydralazine.</li>
<li>symptoms include, arthralgia, arthritis and fever.</li>
<li>The treatment can result in an illness that resembles serum sickness, hemolytic anaemia, vasculitis, and glomerulonephritis.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Therapeutic uses</p>
<ul>
<li>Due to adverse effect profile, hydralazine is no longer a first line drug in the treatment of hypertension.</li>
<li>Used in patients with CCF(in combination with nitrates for patients who cannot tolerate ACE inhibitors.</li>
<li>Treatment of hypertension emergencies in pregnancy.</li>
</ul>
<p>(especially preeclampsia).</p>
<p>The usual dose is twenty five to 100mgs twice a day</p>
<p>He maximum recommended dose of hydralazine is 200mg/day.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="contraindication">Contraindication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#contraindication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Parenteral administration in coronary artery disease.</li>
<li>Elderly patients</li>
</ul>
<p>ALPHA ADRENERGIC BLOCKERS (SYMPATHOLYTICS)</p>
<ul>
<li>Medication: prazosin (Minipress)</li>
<li>doxazosin mesylate (Cardura)</li>
</ul>
<p>Expected Pharmacological Action</p>
<ul>
<li>It inhibits Alpha adrenergic receptor causing Venous and arterial dilation leading to reduction in total peripheral vascular resistance.</li>
<li>Smooth muscle relaxation of the prostatic capsule and bladder neck</li>
</ul>
<p>Therapeutic uses</p>
<ul>
<li>Primary hypertension.</li>
<li>Doxazosin mesylate (Cardura) may be used to decrease symptoms of benign prostatic hypertrophy (BPH), which include urgency, frequency, and dysuria.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Side/Adverse Effects</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>First-dose orthostatic hypotension</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Start treatment with low dosage of medication.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>First dose may be given at night.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Monitor blood pressure for 2 hr. after the initiation of treatment.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Instruct clients to avoid activities requiring mental alertness for the first 12 to 24 hr.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Instruct clients to change positions slowly and to lie down if feeling dizzy, lightheaded, or faint</p>
</li>
<li></li>
</ul>
<p>Contraindications/Precautions</p>
<p>â€¢ Pregnancy</p>
<p>â€¢ clients with hypersensitivity to medication</p>
<p>â€¢ Medication/Food Interactions Nursing Interventions/Client Education</p>
<p>â€¢ Antihypertensive medications may have an additive hypotensive effect</p>
<p>Instruct clients to observe for signs of hypotension (dizziness, lightheadedness, faintness).</p>
<p>Instruct clients to lie down if these symptoms occur, and to change positions slowly.</p>
<p>â€¢ NSAIDs and clonidine may decrease the antihypertensive effects of prazosin.</p>
<p>Advise clients to avoid OTC NSAIDs.</p>
<p>Nursing Administration</p>
<ul>
<li>Obtain baseline blood pressure and heart rate.</li>
<li>Instruct clients that the medication can be taken with food.</li>
<li>Recommend that clients take the initial dose at bedtime to decrease â€œfirst-doseâ€ hypotensive effect.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>CENTRALLY ACTING ALPHA2 AGONISTS</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clonidine-catapres">clonidine (Catapres)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clonidine-catapres" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>guanfacine HCl (Tenex),</li>
<li>methyldopa (Aldomet)</li>
</ul>
<p>Expected Pharmacological Action</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>These medications act within the CNS to decrease sympathetic outflow resulting in decreased stimulation of the adrenergic receptors (both alpha and beta receptors) of the heart and peripheral vascular system.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Decrease in sympathetic outflow to the myocardium results in bradycardia and decreased cardiac output (CO).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Decrease in sympathetic outflow to the peripheral vasculature results in vasodilation, which leads to decreased blood pressure.</p>
</li>
<li></li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="therapeutic-uses">Therapeutic Uses<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#therapeutic-uses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Primary hypertension (administered alone, with a diuretic, or with another antihypertensive agent)</li>
<li>Severe cancer pain (administered parenterally by epidural infusion)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="investigational-use">Investigational use<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#investigational-use" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Migraine headache</li>
<li>Flushing from menopause</li>
<li>Management of ADHD and Tourette's syndrome</li>
<li>Management of withdrawal symptoms from alcohol, tobacco, and opioids</li>
</ul>
<p>Side/Adverse Effects</p>
<ul>
<li>Drowsiness and sedation</li>
<li>Dry mouth</li>
<li>Rebound hypertension</li>
</ul>
<p>contraindication</p>
<ul>
<li>Clonidine is Pregnancy Risk Category C.</li>
<li>Avoid use during lactation.</li>
<li>This medication is contraindicated for clients taking anticoagulant medications</li>
<li>Avoid use of transdermal patch on affected skin in scleroderma and systemic lupus erythematosus (SLE).</li>
<li>Use cautiously in clients with cerebrovascular disease, recent MI, diabetes mellitus, major depressive disorder, or chronic renal failure</li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Antihypertensive medications may have an additive hypotensive effect.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Concurrent use of prazosin (Minipress), MAOI s, and tricyclic antidepressants can counteract the antihypertensive effect of clonidine.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Additive CNS depression can occur with concurrent use of other CNS depressants, such as alcohol.</p>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-administration">Nursing Administration<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-administration" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Administer medication by oral, epidural, and transdermal routes.</li>
<li>Medication is usually administered twice a day in divided doses. Take larger dose at bedtime to decrease the occurrence of daytime sleepiness.</li>
<li>Transdermal patches are applied every seven days. Advise clients to apply patch on hairless, intact skin on torso or upper arm.</li>
</ul>
<p>Methyldopa (ALDOMET)</p>
<ul>
<li>Acts through its metabolites (amethylnorepinephrine)which stimulates central alpha adrenergic receptors, thus increasing total peripheral resistance.</li>
<li>It does not affect glomerular filtration, cardiac output or heart rate.</li>
</ul>
<p>Therapeutic effects</p>
<p>moderate to severe hypertension</p>
<p>Adverse effects:</p>
<p>GIT upsets, sedation, depression, nasal stuffiness, myocarditis edema, orthostatic hypotension, diarrhea, dry mouth, erectile dysfunction, eosinophilia, hemolytic anemia, fever.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>contraindication</p>
<ul>
<li>Hypersensitivity, activity liver disease, those who developed liver cirrhosis with previous treatment of methyldopa.</li>
</ul>
<p>Caution;</p>
<ul>
<li>Patients taking diuretics and antihypertensive.</li>
<li>Those taking levodopa because of potential for additive antihypertensive effects.</li>
</ul>
<p>Consideration</p>
<ul>
<li>patient to avoid hazardous task.</li>
<li>Lower dose in impaired renal disease.</li>
<li>Monitor liver functions.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Caution cont.'</p>
<ul>
<li>Monitor HB, RBCs for signs of anemia.</li>
<li>Monitor weight, fluid input and out put.</li>
<li>Signs of drug induced depression,</li>
<li>Take BP in different patients position during dose adjustments, warn of signs and symptoms of adverse effects and toxicity</li>
<li>Tolerance may develop 2to 3 weeks after start of treatment.</li>
<li>Urine may darken on exposure to air(as drug is broken down to its metabolites)</li>
<li>Dose increase should be made with the evening dose to minimize the effects of drowsiness.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>BETA ADRENERGIC BLOCKERS (SYMPATHOLYTICS)</p>
<p>Cardioselective: Beta1</p>
<p>â€¢ Metoprolol (Lopressor)</p>
<p>â€¢ Atenolol (Tenormin)</p>
<p>â€¢ Metoprolol succinate (Toprol XL)</p>
<p>â€¢ Esmolol HCL (Brevibloc)</p>
<p>Nonselective: (Beta1 and Beta2)</p>
<p>â€¢ Propranolol (Inderal)</p>
<p>â€¢ Nadolol (Corgard)</p>
<p>â€¢ Labetalol (Normodyne)</p>
<p>Expected Pharmacological Action</p>
<p>They block beta- adrenergic receptors in the myocardium and in the electrical conduction system of the heart.</p>
<p>â€¢ Decreased heart rate</p>
<p>â€¢ Decreased myocardial contractility</p>
<p>â€¢ Decreased rate of conduction through the AV node</p>
<p>Therapeutic Uses</p>
<p>hypertension , Angina, arrhythmias, heart failure and myocardial infarction.</p>
<p>Other uses may include: Treatment of hyperthyroidism, migraine headache, pheochromocytoma, and glaucoma</p>
<p>adverse effects</p>
<ul>
<li>Bradycardia, fatigue, dizziness, nightmares, depression, memory loss, hallucination, impotence, cold extremities, elevated serum cholesterol.</li>
</ul>
<p>Contraindication</p>
<p>severe hypotension, bradycardia, congestive heart failure, asthma, diabetics, critically abnormal lipid profile</p>
<p>Consideration</p>
<ul>
<li>Explain the rationale of therapy and importance of taking drugs as prescribed.</li>
<li>Patient should not discontinue drugs abruptly because it can cause MI or angina</li>
</ul>
<p>Consideration cont.'</p>
<ul>
<li>Advise clients to avoid sudden changes in position to prevent occurrence of orthostatic hypotension</li>
<li>Administer medications orally, usually once or twice a day.</li>
<li>Administer the following medications by IV route: atenolol, metoprolol, labetalol, propranolol.</li>
<li>Teach clients to self monitor heart rate and blood pressure at home on a daily basis.</li>
<li>Monitor weight &amp; signs of hypovolemic shock especially in diabetic patients.</li>
<li>Glucagon is prescribed to reverse signs of overdose.</li>
<li>Dose are lowered in geriatrics due to delayed metabolism and enhanced side effects.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Medications for Hypertensive Crisis</p>
<p>nitroprusside sodium (Nitropress)</p>
<p>Other Medications:</p>
<p>Nitroglycerin (Nitrostat IV)</p>
<p>Nicardipine (Cardene)</p>
<p>Clevidipine (Cleviprex)</p>
<p>Enalaprilat (Vasotec IV)</p>
<p>Esmolol HCL (Brevibloc)</p>
<p>mechanism of Action Direct vasodilation of arteries and veins resulting in rapid reduction of blood pressure (decreased preload and afterload) â— Therapeutic Uses Hypertensive emergencies</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="side-effects">Side effects<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#side-effects" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Excessive hypotension</p>
<ul>
<li>Administer medication slowly because rapid administration will cause blood pressure to go down rapidly. - Monitor the client's blood pressure and ECG.</li>
</ul>
<p>interactions</p>
<p>Nitroprusside should not be administered in the same infusion as any other medication.</p>
<p>Nursing Administration</p>
<p>â€¢ Prepare medication by adding to diluent for IV infusion.</p>
<p>â€¢ Note color of solution. Solution may be light brown in color. Discard solution of any other color.</p>
<p>â€¢ Protect IV container and tubing from light.</p>
<p>â€¢ Discard medication after 24 hr.</p>
<p>â€¢ Monitor vital signs and ECG continuously</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cardiac-glycoside">CARDIAC GLYCOSIDE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cardiac-glycoside" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>two main types</p>
<ul>
<li>cardenolides (digitalis, convallaria, oleandra)</li>
<li>Bufadienolides (Helleborus, Poison Arrow Frog)</li>
</ul>
<p>Mechanism of action
Cardiac glycoside slows down the heart rate and increase the force of contraction</p>
<p>Pharmacological action</p>
<ul>
<li>Enhances myocardial contractility and is used in congestive cardiac failure.</li>
<li>Enhances cardiac output, minimizes dilated cardiac size, blood volume and venous pressure.</li>
<li>They modulate autonomic nervous system activity, and this contributes to their efficacy in management of heart failure.</li>
<li>Diuretic effect, reduce oedema.</li>
<li>It is usually given only when diuretics and ACEIs have failed.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="indication">indication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#indication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Congestive heart failure, heart failure with atrial fibrillation, or pts who remain symptomatic despite therapy with ACE inhibitors and b Adrenergic receptor antagonists</li>
<li>Left ventricular failure.</li>
<li>Atrial fibrillation.</li>
</ul>
<p>digoxin</p>
<ul>
<li>It is the most commonly used digitalis</li>
</ul>
<p>forms</p>
<p>Tablets (Lanoxin)</p>
<p>Capsules (lanoxicaps)</p>
<p>Parenteral digoxin is available for intravenous administration and maintenance doses can be given intravenously when oral dosin is impractical.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="digoxin-cont">Digoxin cont.'<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#digoxin-cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="expected-pharmacological-action">Expected Pharmacological Action<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#expected-pharmacological-action" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="positive-inotropic-effect">Positive inotropic effect<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#positive-inotropic-effect" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">âœ“</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">âœ“</span></span></span></span></span> increased force of myocardial contraction Increased force and efficiency of myocardial contraction improves the heart's effectiveness as a pump,
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">âœ“</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">âœ“</span></span></span></span></span> improving stroke volume and cardiac output.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">âœ“</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">âœ“</span></span></span></span></span> Increase perfusion of the kidneys which facilitates excretion of fluid by the kidneys</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="negative-chronotropic-effect">Negative chronotropic effect<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#negative-chronotropic-effect" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">âœ“</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">âœ“</span></span></span></span></span> decreased heart rate ,
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">âœ“</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">âœ“</span></span></span></span></span> At therapeutic levels, digoxin slows the rate of SA node depolarization and the rate of impulses through the conduction system of the heart.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">âœ“</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">âœ“</span></span></span></span></span> A decreased heart rate gives the ventricles more time to fill with blood coming from the atria, which leads to increased SV and increased CO.</p>
<p>Digoxin cont.â€™</p>
<p>Therapeutic Uses</p>
<p>â€¢ Treatment of heart failure</p>
<p>â€¢ Dysrhythmias (atrial fibrillation)</p>
<p>side/adverse effects</p>
<p>â€¢ Dysrhythmias (caused by interfering with the electrical conduction in the myocardium)</p>
<p>â€¢ Cardiotoxicity leading to bradycardia.</p>
<p>â€¢ GI effects include anorexia (usually the first sign), nausea, vomiting, and abdominal pain.</p>
<p>â€¢ Teach clients to monitor for these effects and report to the provider if they occur.</p>
<p>â€¢ CNS effects include fatigue, weakness, vision changes (diplopia, blurred vision, yellow-green or white halos around objects).</p>
<p>Digoxin cont.â€™</p>
<p>Contraindications/Precautions</p>
<p>â€¢ In Pregnancy</p>
<p>â€¢ clients with disturbances in ventricular rhythm, including ventricular fibrillation, ventricular tachycardia, and second- and third-degree heart block.</p>
<p>â€¢ Use cautiously in clients who have hypokalemia, partial AV block, advanced heart failure, and renal insufficiency.</p>
<p>Medication interaction</p>
<ul>
<li>Thiazide diuretics, such as hydrochlorothiazide (HCTZ), and loop diuretics, such as furosemide (Lasix), may lead to hypokalemia, which increases the risk of developing dysrhythmias</li>
<li>ACE inhibitors and ARBs increase the risk of hyperkalemia, which can lead to decreased therapeutic effects of digoxin.</li>
<li>Sympathomimetic medications such as dopamine (Intropin) complement the inotropic action of digoxin and increase the rate and force of heart muscle contraction.</li>
<li>Quinidine increases the risk of digoxin toxicity when used concurrently.</li>
<li>Verapamil (Calan) increases plasma levels</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>MEDICATIONS AFFECTING THE RESPIRATORY SYSTEM (bronchodilators)</p>
<p>Over view: Asthma is a chronic inflammatory disorder of the airways. It is an intermittent and reversible airflow obstruction that affects the bronchioles. The obstruction occurs either by inflammation or airway hyper-responsiveness leading to bronchoconstriction.</p>
<p>â€¢ Medication management usually addresses both inflammation and bronchoconstriction</p>
<p>â€¢ These same medications may be used in symptomatic treatment of chronic obstructive pulmonary disease (COPD</p>
<ul>
<li></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li>Advise clients to take the medication as prescribed. If a dose is missed, the next dose should NOT be doubled.</li>
<li>Check pulse rate and rhythm before administration of digoxin and record. Notify the provider if heart rate is less than 60/min in an adult, less than 70/min in children, and less than 90/min in infants. Administer digoxin at the same time daily.</li>
<li>Monitor digoxin levels periodically during treatment and maintain therapeutic levels between 0.5 to 2.0 ng/mL to prevent digoxin toxicity.</li>
<li>Avoid taking OTC medications to prevent adverse and side effects and medication interactions.</li>
<li>Instruct clients to observe symptoms of hypokalemia, such as muscle weakness, and to notify the provider if symptoms occur.</li>
<li>Instruct clients to observe symptoms of digoxin toxicity (anorexia, fatigue, weakness), and to notify the provider if symptoms occur.</li>
</ul>
<p>Management of digoxin toxicity</p>
<ul>
<li>Digoxin and potassium-sparing medication should be stopped immediately.</li>
<li>Monitor K+ levels. For levels less than 3.5 mEq/L, administer potassium intravenously or by mouth. Do not give any further K+ if the level is greater than 5.0 mEq/L.</li>
<li>Treat dysrhythmias with phenytoin (Dilantin) or lidocaine.</li>
<li>Treat bradycardia with atropine.</li>
<li>For excessive overdose, activated charcoal, cholestyramine, or Digibind can be used to bind digoxin and prevent absorption.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Bronchodilators cont.'</p>
<p>Medications include:</p>
<p>Classification of Bronchodilator ;</p>
<ul>
<li>beta2-adrenergic agonists short acting; salbutamol,</li>
<li>beta2-adrenergic agonists long acting; salmeterol and formoterol</li>
<li>Methyl xanthine's e.g. theophylline</li>
<li>inhaled anticholinergics e.g. tiotropium</li>
<li>anti-inflammatory agents such as glucocorticoids, mast cell stabilizers, and leukotriene modifiers.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="beta2-adrenergic-agonists">Beta2-Adrenergic Agonists<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#beta2-adrenergic-agonists" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>albuterol (Proventil, Ventolin)</li>
<li>Formoterol (Foradil Aerolizer)</li>
<li>Salmeterol (Serevent)</li>
<li>Terbutaline (Brethine)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="albuterol-proventil-ventolin">albuterol ( Proventil, Ventolin)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#albuterol-proventil-ventolin" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Mechanism of Action</li>
<li>Beta2-adrenergic agonists act by selectively activating the beta2-receptors in the bronchial smooth muscle, resulting in bronchodilation. As a result of this: Bronchospasm is relieved, Histamine release is inhibited, Ciliary motility is increased.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="therapeutic-uses">Therapeutic uses<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#therapeutic-uses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>Medication</th><th>Route</th><th>Therapeutic uses</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Albuterol (Proventil, Ventolin)</td><td>- Inhaled, short-acting</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Oral, long-acting</td><td>- Prevention of asthma attack (exercise-induced) - Treatment for ongoing asthma attack - Long-term control of asthma</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Formoterol (Foradil Aerolizer) Salmeterol (Serevent)</td><td>- Inhaled, long-acting</td><td>- Long-term control of asthma</td></tr><tr><td>Terbutaline (Brethine)</td><td>Oral, long-acting</td><td>- Long-term control of asthma</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Side effects</p>
<p>â€¢ Inhaled agents (short and long acting) have minimal adverse effects.</p>
<p>â€¢ Oral agents can cause tachycardia and angina because of activation of alpha1 receptors in the heart.</p>
<p>â€¢ Tremors caused by activation of beta2 receptors in skeletal muscle.</p>
<p>Contraindications/Precautions</p>
<p>â€¢ Beta2-adrenergic agonists are Pregnancy Risk Category C.</p>
<p>â€¢ These agents are contraindicated in clients with tachydysrhythmia.</p>
<p>â€¢ Use cautiously in clients who have diabetes, hyperthyroidism, heart disease, hypertension, and angina</p>
<p>Medication and food interaction</p>
<p>â€¢ Use of beta-adrenergic blockers (propranolol) can negate effects of both medications.</p>
<p>â€¢ MAOIs and tricyclic antidepressants can increase the risk of tachycardia and angina.</p>
<p>Nursing Administration</p>
<p>Instruct clients to follow manufacturerâ€™s instructions for use of device: metered-dose inhaler (MDI), dry-powder inhaler(DPI), and nebulizer.</p>
<p>When a client is prescribed an inhaled beta2-agonist and an inhaled glucocorticoid, advise the client to inhale the beta2-agonist before inhaling the glucocorticoid.</p>
<p>The beta2-agonist promotes bronchodilation and enhances absorption of the glucocorticoid.</p>
<p>Advise clients not to exceed prescribed dosages.</p>
<p>Ensure that clients know the appropriate dosage schedule (if the medication is to be taken on a fixed or a when-necessary schedule).</p>
<p>Formoterol and salmeterol are both long-acting beta2-agonist inhalers. These inhalers are used every 12 hr. for long-term control and are not to be used to abort an asthma attack. A short-acting beta2-agonist should be used if clients need to treat an acute attack.</p>
<ul>
<li>Advise clients to observe for signs of an impending asthma attack and to keep a log of the frequency and intensity of attacks.</li>
<li>Instruct clients to notify the provider if there is an increase in the frequency and intensity of asthma attacks.</li>
</ul>
<p>METHYLXANTHINES</p>
<p>theophylline (Theolair, Theo-24)</p>
<p>Expected Pharmacological Action</p>
<p>Theophylline causes relaxation of bronchial smooth muscle, resulting in bronchodilation.</p>
<p>Therapeutic Uses</p>
<p>Oral theophylline is used for long-term control of chronic asthma.</p>
<p>Route of administration: oral or IV (emergency use only)</p>
<p>Side/adverse effects</p>
<p>Mild toxicity reaction may include GI distress and restlessness.</p>
<p>â€¢ More severe reactions can occur with higher therapeutic levels and can include dysrhythmias and seizures.</p>
<p>Contraindications/Precautions</p>
<p>â€¢ in Pregnancy</p>
<p>â€¢ Use cautiously in clients who have heart disease, hypertension, liver and renal dysfunction, and diabetes.</p>
<p>â€¢ Use cautiously in children and older adults.</p>
<p>Nursing Administration</p>
<p>â€¢ Advise clients to take the medication as prescribed. If a dose is missed, the following dose should not be doubled.</p>
<p>â€¢ Instruct clients not to chew or crush sustained-release preparations. These medications should be swallowed whole.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="inhaled-anticholinergics">INHALED ANTICHOLINERGICS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#inhaled-anticholinergics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>ipratropium (Atrovent)</li>
<li>tiotropium (Spiriva)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="expected-pharmacological-action">Expected Pharmacological Action<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#expected-pharmacological-action" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>These medications block muscarinic receptors of the bronchi, resulting in bronchodilation.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="therapeutic-uses">Therapeutic Uses<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#therapeutic-uses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>These medications are used to relieve bronchospasm associated with chronic obstructive pulmonary disease (COPD)</li>
<li>These medications are used for allergen-induced and exercise-induced asthma.
Route of administration: inhalation</li>
</ul>
<p>SIDE/ADVERSE EFFECTS</p>
<p>Local anticholinergic effects (dry mouth, hoarseness)</p>
<p>Advise clients to sip fluids and suck on hard candies to control dry mouth.</p>
<p>Contraindications/Precautions</p>
<p>â€¢ Inhaled anticholinergics are Pregnancy Risk Category B.</p>
<p>â€¢ These agents are contraindicated in clients who have an allergy to peanuts because the medication preparations may contain soy lecithin.</p>
<p>â€¢ Use cautiously in clients who have narrow-angle glaucoma and benign prostatic hypertrophy (due to anticholinergic effects).</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Nursing Administration</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Advise clients to rinse the mouth after inhalation to decrease unpleasant taste.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Usual adult dosage is two puffs. Instruct clients to wait the length of time directed between puffs.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If clients are prescribed two inhaled medications, instruct clients to wait at least 5 min between medications</p>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li>Medication/Food Interactions</li>
<li>Caffeine increases CNS and cardiac adverse effects of theophylline.</li>
<li>Caffeine can also increase theophylline levels.</li>
</ul>
<p>Advise clients to avoid consuming caffeinated beverages (coffee, caffeinated colas).</p>
<ul>
<li>Phenobarbital and phenytoin decrease theophylline levels.</li>
<li>Cimetidine (Tagamet), ciprofloxacin (Cipro), and other fluoroquinolone antibiotics increase theophylline level.</li>
</ul>
<p>GLUCOCORTICOIDS</p>
<p>Inhalation: beclomethasone dipropionate (QVAR)</p>
<p>Oral: prednisone (Deltasone)</p>
<p>Inhalation:</p>
<p>â€¢ Budesonide (Pulmicort Flexhaler)</p>
<p>â€¢ Fluticasone propionate and salmeterol (Advair)</p>
<p>â€¢ Fluticasone propionate (Flovent)</p>
<p>â€¢ Triamcinolone acetonide (Azmacort)</p>
<p>systemic :</p>
<p>â€¢ Oral Prednisolone E 30 to 40mg for initial to 7 days,</p>
<p>â€¢ IV/IM dexamethasone</p>
<p>â€¢ IV Hydrocortisone sodium succinate (Solu-Cortef) (</p>
<p>â€¢ IV Methylprednisolone sodium succinate (Solu-Medrol)</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Expected Pharmacological Action</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>These medications prevent inflammation, suppress airway mucus production, and promote responsiveness of beta2 receptors in the bronchial tree.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The use of glucocorticoids does not provide immediate effects, but rather promotes decreased frequency and severity of exacerbations and acute attacks.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Therapeutic Uses</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Short-term IV agents are used for status asthmaticus.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Inhaled agents are used for long-term prophylaxis of asthma.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Short-term oral therapy is used to treat symptoms following an acute asthma attack.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Long-term oral therapy is used to treat chronic asthma.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Replacement therapy is used for primary adrenocortical insufficiency.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Promote lung maturity and decrease respiratory distress in fetuses at risk for preterm birth</p>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Side/Adverse Effects Nursing Interventions/Client Education</p>
<p>Beclomethasone dipropionate</p>
<p>Difficulty speaking, hoarseness, and candidiasis</p>
<p>â€¢ Advise clients to use a spacer with MDI.</p>
<p>â€¢ Advise clients to rinse mouth or gargle with water or salt water after use.</p>
<p>â€¢ Advise clients to monitor for redness, sores, or white patches and to report to provider if they occur.</p>
<p>â€¢ Candidiasis may be treated with nystatin oral suspension.</p>
<p>prednisolone when used for more than 10 days</p>
<ul>
<li>Suppression of adrenal gland function, such as a decrease in the ability of the adrenal cortex to produce glucocorticoids: Can occur with inhaled agents and oral agents</li>
</ul>
<p>Taper the clientâ€™s dose.</p>
<ul>
<li>Bone loss (can occur with inhaled agents and oral agents)</li>
<li>Myopathy as evidenced by muscle weakness</li>
<li>Hyperglycemia and glycosuria</li>
<li>Myopathy as evidenced by muscle weakness a</li>
<li>Peptic ulcer disease</li>
<li>Infection</li>
<li>Disturbances of fluid and electrolytes (fluid retention as evidenced by weight gain, and edema and hypokalemia as evidenced by muscle weakness)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Contraindications/Precautions</p>
<p>â€¢ Pregnancy risk category C</p>
<p>â€¢ Contraindicated in clients who have received a live virus vaccine</p>
<p>â€¢ Contraindicated in clients with systemic fungal infections</p>
<p>â€¢ Use cautiously in children, and in clients who have diabetes, hypertension, peptic ulcer disease, and/or renal dysfunction.</p>
<p>â€¢ Use cautiously in clients taking NSAIDs.</p>
<p>Medication/Food Interactions</p>
<p>â€¢ Concurrent use of potassium-depleting diuretics increases the risk of hypokalemia.</p>
<p>â€¢ Concurrent use of NSAIDs increases the risk of GI ulceration. Concurrent use of glucocorticoids and hypoglycemic agents (oral and insulin) will counteract the effects</p>
<p>Nursing Administration</p>
<p>â€¢ Instruct clients to use glucocorticoid inhalers on a regular, fixed schedule for long-term therapy of asthma.</p>
<p>â€¢ Glucocorticoids are not to be used to treat an acute attack.</p>
<p>â€¢ Administer using an MDI device, DPI, or nebulizer.</p>
<p>â€¢ When a client is prescribed an inhaled beta2-agonist and an inhaled glucocorticoid, advise the client to inhale the beta2-agonist before inhaling the glucocorticoid. The beta2-agonist promotes bronchodilation and enhances absorption of the glucocorticoid.</p>
<p>â€¢ Oral glucocorticoids are used short-term, 3 to 10 days following an acute asthma attack.</p>
<p>â€¢ If client is on long-term oral therapy, additional dosages of oral glucocorticoids are required in times of stress (infection, trauma).</p>
<p>â€¢ Clients who discontinue oral glucocorticoid medications or switch from oral to inhaled agents require additional doses of glucocorticoids during periods of stress.</p>
<p>MASTCELL STABILIZERS ANTI INFLATORY DRUGS (cromolyn sodium (Intal)</p>
<p>others are: nedocromil sodium (Tilade)</p>
<p>Expected Pharmacological Action</p>
<ul>
<li>Anti-inflammatory action</li>
<li>These medications stabilize mast cells, which inhibits the release of histamine and other inflammatory mediators.</li>
<li>These medications suppress inflammatory cells (eosinophils, macrophages).</li>
</ul>
<p>Complications Safest of all asthma medications, Safe to use for children</p>
<p>therapeutic uses</p>
<ul>
<li>Management of chronic asthma</li>
<li>Prophylaxis of exercise-induced asthma</li>
<li>Prevention of allergen-induced attack</li>
<li>Allergic rhinitis by intranasal route</li>
<li>Route of administration: inhalation</li>
</ul>
<p>Contraindications/Precautions</p>
<ul>
<li>These agents are Pregnancy Risk Category B.</li>
<li>Fluorocarbons in aerosols make this medication contraindicated for clients who have coronary artery disease, dysrhythmias, and status asthmaticus.</li>
<li>Use cautiously in clients with liver and kidney impairment.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Nursing Administration</p>
<p>â€¢ Advise clients to take medication 15 min before exercise or exposure to allergen.</p>
<p>â€¢ Advise clients that long-term prophylaxis may take several weeks for full therapeutic effects to be established.</p>
<p>â€¢ Advise clients that this is not a bronchodilator and is not intended for aborting an asthmatic attack.</p>
<p>â€¢ Instruct clients in the proper use of administration devices (nebulizer, MDI).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="leukotriene-modifiers">LEUKOTRIENE MODIFIERS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#leukotriene-modifiers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>leukotriene receptor antagonist ;</p>
<ul>
<li>Montelukast (Singulair)</li>
<li>Zileuton (Zyflo),</li>
<li>Zafirlukast (Accolate)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="expected-pharmacological-action">Expected Pharmacological Action<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#expected-pharmacological-action" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Leukotriene modifiers prevent the effects of leukotrienes, thereby suppressing inflammation, bronchoconstriction, airway edema, and mucus production.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="therapeutic-uses">Therapeutic Uses<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#therapeutic-uses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Leukotriene modifiers are used for long-term therapy of asthma in adults and children 15 years and older and to prevent exercise-induced bronchospasm.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="route-of-administration-oral">Route of administration: oral<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#route-of-administration-oral" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Contraindications/Precautions</p>
<p>â€¢ Use cautiously in clients with liver dysfunction</p>
<p>Medication/Food Interactions</p>
<p>â€¢ Zileuton and zafirlukast inhibit metabolism of warfarin (Coumadin), leading to increased warfarin levels.</p>
<p>â€¢ Zileuton and Zafirlukast inhibit metabolism of theophylline, leading to increased theophylline levels.</p>
<p>Nursing Administration</p>
<p>â€¢ Advise clients to take zileuton as prescribed. Zileuton can be given with or without food.</p>
<p>â€¢ Advise clients that zafirlukast should not be given with food, and to administer it 1 hr. before or 2 hr. after meals.</p>
<p>â€¢ Advise clients to take Montelukast once daily at bedtime.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="git-drugs-peptic-ulcer-disease">GIT DRUGS ( PEPTIC ULCER DISEASE)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#git-drugs-peptic-ulcer-disease" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="acid-peptic-disease-includes">acid peptic disease includes:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#acid-peptic-disease-includes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>peptic ulcers (gastric ulcer, duodenal ulcer, NSAIDS induced ulcers)</li>
<li>gasro oesophageal reflux disease,</li>
<li>hypersecretory states like Zollinger Ellison Syndrome (ulcerogenic tumour of the islets of Langerhans.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="principles-of-therapy">Principles of therapy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#principles-of-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The aim of therapy is to;</p>
<ul>
<li>relieve symptoms,</li>
<li>induced ulcer healing and cure in the long run</li>
<li>Decreased risk of complications</li>
<li>Stopping reoccurrence .</li>
</ul>
<p>Classification of agents used in treatment of peptic ulcer:</p>
<p>â€¢ Inhibition of acid secretion</p>
<p>âž¢H2 receptor agonist e.g. cimetidine, ranitidine, famotidine roxatidine.</p>
<p>âž¢Proton pump inhibitors e.g. omeprazole, pantoprazole, esomeprazole, lansoprazole.</p>
<p>âž¢Anticholinergics e.g. pirenzepine.</p>
<p>âž¢Prostaglandin analogue e.g. misoprostol.</p>
<p>â€¢ neutralization of gastric acids</p>
<p>âž¢Sodium bicarbonate systemic</p>
<p>âž¢Non systemic: magnesium hydroxide, aluminium hydroxide, magnesium trisilicate.</p>
<p>â€¢ Mucosal protective agents e.g. sucralfate, colloidal bismuth.</p>
<p>â€¢ Anti helicobacter pylori drugs (ANTIBIOTICS) e.g. Clarithromycin, Ampicillin, Metronidazole, Tetracycline, Tinidazole</p>
<p>anti H. pylori drugs</p>
<p>â€¢ Amoxicillin (Amoxil)</p>
<p>â€¢ Bismuth (Pepto-Bismol)</p>
<p>â€¢ Clarithromycin (Biaxin)</p>
<p>â€¢ Metronidazole (Flagyl)</p>
<p>â€¢ Tetracycline</p>
<p>Expected Pharmacological Action</p>
<p>â€¢ Eradication of H. pylori bacteria</p>
<p>â€¢ Therapy should include: Combination of 2 or 3 antibiotics for 14 days</p>
<p>The disease process is only altered by the use of antibiotics. All other medications make an environment that is conducive to healing</p>
<p>Two weeks regimen</p>
<ul>
<li>Tetracycline 500mg QID and metronidazole 200mg BID and Bismuth sub salylicylate.</li>
<li>Amoxicillin 100mg BID and clarithromycin 500mg BID+ Lansoprazole 30mgs BID.</li>
<li>Clarithromycin 500mg TDS +Omeprazole.</li>
</ul>
<p>ONE WEEK REGIMEN</p>
<p>Clarithromycin 250mg BID + Metronidazole 400mgs + Omeprazole 20mgs BID.</p>
<p>Amoxicillin 500mg Bid + Clarithromycin 250mg Bid+ Omeprazole 20mg</p>
<p>Histamine2 -Receptor Antagonists</p>
<ul>
<li>ranitidine hydrochloride (Zantac)</li>
<li>Cimetidine (Tagamet)</li>
<li>Nizatidine (Axid)</li>
<li>Famotidine (Pepcid)</li>
</ul>
<p>Expected Pharmacological Action: Histamine2-receptor antagonists suppress the secretion of gastric acid by selectively blocking H2 receptors in parietal cells lining the stomach</p>
<ul>
<li></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li>Therapeutic Uses</li>
<li>gastric and peptic ulcers,</li>
<li>gastroesophageal reflux disease (GERD),</li>
<li>hypersecretory conditions, such as Zollinger-Ellison syndrome.</li>
<li>Histamine2-receptor antagonists are used in conjunction with antibiotics to treat ulcers caused by H. pylori.</li>
</ul>
<p>Side/Adverse Effects</p>
<ul>
<li>Cimetidine may block androgen receptors, resulting in decreased libido and impotence.</li>
<li>Cimetidine may cause CNS effects (lethargy, depression, confusion)</li>
<li>Ranitidine, nizatidine, and famotidine have few adverse effects and interactions.</li>
</ul>
<p>Contraindications/Precautions</p>
<p>â€¢ These medications are Pregnancy Risk Category B</p>
<p>â€¢ Use in older adults can cause antiadrenergic effects (e.g., impotence) and CNS effects (e.g., confusion).</p>
<p>â€¢ H2-receptor antagonists decrease gastric acidity, which promotes bacterial colonization of the stomach and the respiratory tract. Use cautiously in clients who are at a high risk for pneumonia, such as clients with chronic obstructive pulmonary disease (COPD).</p>
<p>Medication/Food Interactions</p>
<p>â€¢ Cimetidine can inhibit medication metabolizing enzymes and thus increase the levels of warfarin, phenytoin (Dilantin), theophylline, and lidocaine.</p>
<p>â€¢ Concurrent use of antacids can decrease absorption of histamine2 -receptor antagonists.</p>
<p>Nursing Administration</p>
<p>Cimetidine, ranitidine, and famotidine can be administered IV for acute situations.</p>
<p>Advise clients to practice good nutrition. Suggest eating six small meals rather than three large meals a day.</p>
<p>Inform clients that adequate rest and reduction of stress may promote healing.</p>
<p>Clients should avoid smoking, because smoking can delay healing.</p>
<p>Encourage clients to avoid aspirin and other nonsteroidal anti-inflammatory drugs (NSAIDs) unless taking low-dose aspirin therapy for prevention of cardiovascular disease.</p>
<p>If alcohol exacerbates symptoms, advise clients to stop drinking.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Availability of these medications OTC may discourage clients from seeking appropriate health care.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Encourage clients to see the provider if symptoms persist.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The medication regimen can be complex, often requiring clients to take two to three different medications for an extended period of time. Encourage clients to adhere to the medication regimen and provide support.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ranitidine can be taken with or without food</p>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
