<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="tetracyclines">tetracyclines<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tetracyclines" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>First isolated in 1948, isolated from Streptomyces fungi.</li>
<li>Naturally occurring;
-tetracycline
-chlortetracycline
-oxytetracycline
-demeclocycline
Semi-synthetic
Doxycycline, lymecycline, meclocycline, methacyline, minocycline, rolitetracycline.</li>
</ul>
<p>pharmacokinetics</p>
<ul>
<li>Tetracyclines are partially absorbed in the alimentary tract EXCEPT minocycline and doxycycline which have a good absorption.</li>
<li>Absorption is increased in absence of food</li>
<li>antacids and milk decrease absorption as they contain metals like magnesium, calcium, aluminum ,iron which chelate with them.</li>
<li>Distribution is narrow but they cross the placenta barrier.</li>
<li>Metabolism is in the liver</li>
<li>Excretion in urine via glomerular filtration unchanged.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pharmacodynamics">pharmacodynamics<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pharmacodynamics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Tetracyclines are broad spectrum bacteriostatic.</li>
<li>They inhibit protein synthesis by binding to the 30s sub unit of the bacterial ribosomes.</li>
<li>Indication; psittacosis, pneumonia, brucellosis, shigellosis, rickettsia diseases e.g. Q fever, typhus, cholera, borrelia ( lame disease, relapsing fever)acne ,amoebic dysentery, spirochetes, protozoa, bacillary dysentery and chlamydia infections</li>
</ul>
<p>aminoglycosides</p>
<p>Examples;</p>
<p>Gentamycin, kanamycin, amikacin, tobramycin, streptomycin, neomycin,</p>
<p>They are always used in combination of beta lactam antibiotic because of their synergism effect.</p>
<p>pharmacokinetics; they are water soluble hence hey not absorbed through the gut .</p>
<p>They are given IM/IV route</p>
<p>distribution; narrowly distributed hence do not cross the blood brain barrier.</p>
<p>Pharmacodynamics/mechanism of action</p>
<ul>
<li>they are bactericidal act by binding to the 30s ribosomal sub unit and they inhibit bacterial protein synthesis.</li>
<li>Drug interaction;</li>
<li>-muscle weakness or paralysis when given with neural muscular blocking agent.</li>
<li>Ototoxicity when given with ototoxic agent.</li>
<li>Synergic effect when give with beta lactam antibiotic .</li>
<li>Bone marrow depression when give with bone marrow depressing agents.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Unwanted effects</p>
<ul>
<li>Have serious un wanted effects and that are dose dependent</li>
</ul>
<p>these are; nausea, vomiting, diarrhea , lethargy, hypersensitivity and headache.</p>
<p>Others are ,nephrotoxicity, ,ototoxicity, bone marrow depression, neuromuscular blockade, palpitation, numbness, tingling sensation, depression and disorientation.</p>
<p>Contraindication</p>
<ul>
<li>Patients with hearing deficit because thy damage the 8^{th} cranial nerve(vestibular cochlear/auditory nerve)</li>
<li>Myasthenia gravis since they cause neural muscular blockade.</li>
<li>Patients with severe renal disease as they are nephrotoxic</li>
<li>Hypersensitivity</li>
<li>Neonates, geriantrics, infant, botulism and patients with packinsonism</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Gentamycin</p>
<ul>
<li>This is the most active aminoglycoside.</li>
<li>Half life 2-3 hours and reaches peak plasma concentration within 30 minute.</li>
<li>route of administration IM/IV.</li>
<li>indication gram negative and gram positive; septicemia, meningitis, endocarditis, UTI, neonatal sepsis and acute pyelonephritis among other infections.</li>
</ul>
<p>Contraindications; is like for the other aminoglycoside.</p>
<p>dosage adults GIVE 2-5 MG/kg body weight daily 8hrly for 7 days. Reduce the dose in renal impairment and the elderly.</p>
<p>Children below 2wks 3mgs/kg body weight every 12 hours.</p>
<p>Those aged 2wks-12years 2mg/kg every 8 hourly.</p>
<p>Aminoglycoside can replace penicillin in penicillin sensitive patients</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Gentamycin combine with penicillin have a synergic antibiotic effect expands the spectrum of antibiotics activity and prevent emergence of resistance..</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Neomycin and kanamycin can be used for hepatic coma to reduce normal flora and therefore ammonia gas formation.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Amikacin has broadest antibacterial spectrum because it is stable to 8 of the 9 classified aminoglycoside inactivating enzymes whereas gentamycin is inactivated by five of them.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Amikacin is indicated for serious gram negative infections resistant to gentamycin.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Neomycin and framycetin are too toxic for systemic use hence used topically for treatment of aer, nose and skin infections,</p>
</li>
<li></li>
</ul>
<p>quinolones</p>
<ul>
<li>these are broad spectrum antibiotic though some like nalidixic acid and cinoxacin have a narrow antibacterial spectrum.</li>
</ul>
<p>other newer quinolones include</p>
<p>norfloxacin</p>
<p>Ciprofloxacin</p>
<p>Ofloxacin</p>
<p>Levofloxacin</p>
<p>Acrofloxacin</p>
<p>pefloxacin</p>
<p>Pharmacodynamics</p>
<ul>
<li>They are act by inhibiting bacterial DNA gyrase the enzyme that maintains the Helical twist/structure of the DNA.</li>
<li>They are bactericidal but some are bacteriostatic</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Pharmacokinetics</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Quinolones are absorbed in the gut though aluminum and magnesium antacid interfere with the absorption.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Distribution wide distribution such that they cross the placenta and are distributed in breast milk.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>They are concentrated in the lungs, kidneys, prostate, and phagocytes.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>They donâ€™t cross the BBB except ofloxacin and pefloxacin.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Metabolism they under go hepatic metabolism with a variable half life</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Norfloxacin and ciprofloxacin half life of 2-3 hours, 5 hour ofloxacin, perfloxacin10 hour.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Excretion/elimination via renal and biliary.</p>
</li>
<li></li>
</ul>
<p>Adverse effects</p>
<p>â€¢ GIT effects like nausea, vomiting, and diarrhea</p>
<p>â€¢ CNS effects like dizziness, headache, confusion and convulsions.</p>
<p>â€¢ Allergic reactions in form of skin rashes,</p>
<p>They are reported to cause arthropathy in immature animals hence not recommended for children and adolescence unless the benefit out ways the risk.</p>
<p>â€¢ Photosensitivity</p>
<p>â€¢ Bone marrow suppression.</p>
<p>contraindication</p>
<ul>
<li>History of epilepsy or seizures.</li>
<li>Glucose-7-phosphatedehydrogenase deficiency.</li>
<li>Myasthenia gravis.</li>
<li>Pregnancy and breast feeding.</li>
</ul>
<p>Indication; quinolones are basically indicated for UTI ciprofloxacin has a broader spectrum of antibacterial activity.</p>
<p>These are often caused by gram negative organisms like E.coli, proteus spp. Therefore infections like complicated UTI, inversive otitis externa, salmonella typhi infection, gonorrhea, bacteria prostatitis and cervicitis.</p>
<p>They are also indicated for anthrax which has been used as a biological warfare.</p>
<p>So the soldiers can take quinolones just before they go to war just in case they are at risk of exposure to anthrax.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="drug-interactions">drug interactions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#drug-interactions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>These antibiotics are enzyme (cytochrome p-450) inhibitor hence interact with other drugs at metabolism e.g. theophylline, warfarin, and caffeine.</li>
<li>NSAIDS and quinolones causes an increase in the risk of convulsion.</li>
<li>NSAIDS tends to potentiate the effect.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="ciprofloxacin">ciprofloxacin<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ciprofloxacin" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>half life is 3hours</li>
<li>It is mostly effective against gram negative bacteria e.g. salmonella, shigella, Campylobacter, pseudomonas, enterobacteria.</li>
<li>It is indicated for chlamydia and some mycobacteria</li>
</ul>
<p>Indication UTI and genital urinary tract infections.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="dosage">Dosage<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dosage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Oral 250-750mg bd.</li>
<li>IV infusion (30-60) 200-400mg twice daily.</li>
</ul>
<p>Interactions Medication/Food Interactions Nursing Interventions/Client Education</p>
<ul>
<li>Cationic compounds (aluminum-magnesium antacids, iron salts, sucralfate, milk and dairy products) decrease absorption of ciprofloxacin;</li>
</ul>
<p>Administer cationic compounds 6 hrs. before or 2 hrs after ciprofloxacin</p>
<ul>
<li>Plasma levels of theophylline can be the increased with concurrent use of ciprofloxacin;</li>
</ul>
<p>Monitor levels and adjust dosage accordingly.</p>
<ul>
<li>Plasma levels of warfarin can be increased with concurrent use of ciprofloxacin;</li>
</ul>
<p>Monitor prothrombin time and INR, and adjust the dosage of warfarin accordingly.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="administration">Administration<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#administration" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Ciprofloxacin is available in oral and intravenous forms.</li>
<li>Decrease doses of ciprofloxacin in clients with renal dysfunction.</li>
<li>Intravenous ciprofloxacin should be administered slowly over 60 min.</li>
<li>For inhalation anthrax infection, ciprofloxacin is administered every 12 hrs for 60 days.</li>
<li>Instruct clients to complete the prescribed course of antimicrobial therapy, even though symptoms may resolve before the full course is completed.</li>
</ul>
<p>MACROLIDES</p>
<ul>
<li>These broad spectrum antimicrobials including;</li>
<li>Erythromycin</li>
<li>Azithromycin</li>
<li>Spiramycin</li>
<li>Clarithromycin</li>
</ul>
<p>Pharmacodynamics; they inhibit protein synthesis by irreversibly binding to ribosomal 50s sub unit of the sensitive micro-organism hence they are bacteriostatic.</p>
<p>But sometimes can be bactericidal if the dose is high.</p>
<p>Example azithromycin is bactericidal against streptococcus pyogenes, streptococcus pneumonia and hemophilus influenza</p>
<p>pharmacokinetics</p>
<ul>
<li>They can be administered orally though erythromycin is unstable in acidic environment.</li>
<li>Distribution is good except that the drugs do not cross the BBB</li>
<li>Metabolism is in the liver and have variable half life.</li>
</ul>
<p>E.g. clarithromycin has4.5 hours , azithromycin less than 3.5 hours and erythromycin has1.4 to 2 hours.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<ul>
<li><strong>Therapeutic Uses/indication</strong></li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li>Used to treat infections in <strong>clients with a penicillin allergy</strong>, such as for <strong>prophylaxis against rheumatic fever</strong> and <strong>bacterial endocarditis</strong>.</li>
<li>Used for clients <strong>with Legionnairesâ€™ disease, whooping cough</strong> (pertussis), <strong>and acute diphtheria</strong> (eliminates the carrier state of diphtheria) .</li>
<li>Used for chlamydia infections (<strong>urethritis and cervicitis; pneumonia</strong> caused by Mycoplasma pneumoniae**; respiratory tract infections** caused by <strong>Streptococcus pneumoniae and Neisseria gonorrhea.</strong></li>
</ul>
<p>Complications /Side/Adverse Effects; Nursing Interventions/Client Education</p>
<p>Gastrointestinal discomfort</p>
<p>â€¢ (nausea, vomiting, epigastric pain) Administer erythromycin with meals.</p>
<p>â€¢ Observe for GI symptoms and notify the provider.</p>
<p>Hepatotoxicity (abdominal pain, lethargy, jaundice) . Instruct clients to notify the provider because the medication should be discontinued. Prolonged QT interval causing dysrhythmias and possible sudden cardiac death</p>
<p>â€¢ Use in clients with prolonged QT intervals is not recommended.</p>
<p>â€¢ Avoid concurrent use with medications that affect hepatic drug metabolizing enzymes.</p>
<p>Contraindications/Precautions.</p>
<p>â€¢ pre-existing liver disease</p>
<p>erythromycin</p>
<p>â€¢ Erythromycin is the commonest macrolide in use.</p>
<p>Pharmacokinetic;</p>
<p>Erythromycin is inactivated by gastric enzymes hence it is administered as protected enteric coated tablets.</p>
<p>It is hydrolyzed in the 1^{st} phase metabolism to release the active erythromycin.</p>
<p>It is dissolved and absorbed in the small intestines where it undergoes enetro hepatic recirculation.</p>
<p>â€¢ Distribution is very good as it is well distributed in the spleen, liver, placenta, breast milk and inflamed meninges.</p>
<p>â€¢ Excretion 90% in feaces and small amounts in urine.</p>
<p>Dosage and route of administration</p>
<ul>
<li>Orally adults and children above 8years 250-500mg 6 hourly.</li>
<li>Maximum dose is 4g in severe infections.</li>
<li>Children up to 2years 125mg 6hourly.</li>
<li>IV infusion 25-50/kg body wt. daily as continuous infusion.</li>
</ul>
<p>Drug interaction</p>
<p>Macrolides are enzyme inhibitor and they interfere with the metabolism of drugs like warfarin, carbamazepine, theophylline , corticosteroids, oral contraceptives, digoxin, and cyloserine and sodium valproate</p>
<ul>
<li>food tends to decrease the absorption of macrolide, hence should be given one hour before food or 2-3 hours after meals.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Azithromycin</p>
<ul>
<li>azithromycin is derived from erythromycin by adding a methylated nitrogen into the lactogen ring,</li>
<li>Its specrum of activity and clinical uses are virtually identical to those of clarithromycin.</li>
<li>Azithromycin is active against mycobacteria avium complex and toxoplasma gondii</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="sulphonamide">sulphonamide<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sulphonamide" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>These are among the first antibacterial drugs to be discovered in 1935.</li>
<li>Examples</li>
<li>Sulphfamethoxazole,</li>
<li>sulphadiazine,</li>
<li>sulfisoxazole,</li>
<li>sulphadimidine,</li>
<li>sulfasazine,</li>
<li>sulfametopyrazine,</li>
<li>sulphaloxate</li>
</ul>
<p>pharmacokinetics</p>
<ul>
<li>they have good absorption except a few of them sulpadiazine and which are poorly absorbed in the gut.</li>
<li>Distribution widely distributed in body tissues and fluid including crossing the BBB.</li>
<li>They are metabolized in the liver withhalf life of 10 hours.</li>
<li>Majority are excreted in urine hence dose should be reduced in renal impairment.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Side and adverse effects</p>
<p>â€¢ Hypersensitivity including Stevens-Johnson syndrome</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Do not administer TMP-SMZ to clients with allergies to: Sulfonamides (sulfa), Thiazide diuretics [hydrochlorothiazide (HCTZ)] , Sulfonylurea-type oral hypoglycemics [tolbutamide (Orinase)], Loop diuretics [furosemide (Lasix)]</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Stop TMP-SMZ at the first indication of hypersensitivity, such as rash.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>â€¢ Blood dyscrasias (hemolytic anemia, agranulocytosis, aplastic anemia) â€¢</p>
<p>-Draw the clientâ€™s baseline and periodic CBC levels to detect any hematologic disorders.</p>
<ul>
<li>Observe for any bleeding episodes, sore throat, or pallor. â€¢ If the above symptoms occur, instruct clients to notify the provider.</li>
</ul>
<p>â€¢ Crystalluria</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Maintain adequate oral fluid intake.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Instruct client to drink 2 to 3 L/day.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>â€¢ Kernicterus (jaundice, increased bilirubin levels)</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Avoid administering TMP-SMZ to women who are pregnant near term, breastfeeding mothers, and infants younger than 2 months.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Monitor the clientâ€™s liver function. Photosensitivity</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Avoid prolonged exposure to sunlight, use sunscreen, and wear appropriate</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>cotrimoxazole(sulphonamides 400mg/trimethoprim 80mg) serpin.</p>
<ul>
<li>. This has replaced use of sulphonamide due to resistance.</li>
</ul>
<p>Dosage for children</p>
<ul>
<li>6weeks to 5months 120mg every 12 hours</li>
<li>6months to 5years 240mg 10 hourly</li>
<li>6years to 12 years 480mg 12hourly</li>
</ul>
<p>Indications</p>
<ul>
<li>Pneumocystic carinii pneumonia</li>
<li>Toxoplasmosis</li>
<li>UTI</li>
<li>sometimes chronic bronchitis</li>
<li>Others sulphonamides are used for topical application for prophylaxis of burns, leg ulcers, pressure sores because of their wide anti bacteria spectrum</li>
</ul>
<p>drug Interactions Medication/Food Interactions Nursing Interventions/Client Education</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Sulfonamides can increase the effects of warfarin (Coumadin), phenytoin (Dilantin), sulfonylurea oral hypoglycemic, and tolbutamide (Orinase) by inhibiting hepatic metabolism.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>dosages of these medications may be required during therapy.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Nursing Administration Instruct clients to take the drugs on an empty stomach with a full glass of water. (Plenty of oral fluids)</p>
<ul>
<li>Instruct clients to complete the prescribed course of antimicrobial therapy, even though symptoms may resolve before the full course is completed.</li>
</ul>
<p>Nursing Evaluation of Medication Effectiveness</p>
<ul>
<li>Depending on therapeutic intent, effectiveness may be evidenced by: Improvement of infection symptoms, such as improvement of urinary tract symptoms (decreased frequency, burning, and pain during urination) and negative urine cultures</li>
</ul>
<p>AZOLES</p>
<ul>
<li>This includes several classes of drugs e.g. metronidazole and tinidazole which have both anti bacteria and anti protozoal activity.</li>
<li>others are fluconazole, itraconazole econazole, ketoconazole, and miconazole which are anti fungal drugs .( to be covered under anti fungal drugs)</li>
<li>others are mebendazole, thiabendazole, which are anti helminths (to be covered under ant-helminths)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>metronidazole</p>
<ul>
<li>It is very effective against anaerobic bacterial and protozoa.</li>
</ul>
<p>Pharmacodynamics/MOA</p>
<ul>
<li>metronidazole is converted into an active form and bind to the bacterial DNA and prevents nucleic acid formation which consequently interferes with bacterial replication hence its bacteriostatic.</li>
</ul>
<p>Pharmacokinetics;</p>
<p>well absorbed after oral and rectal administration</p>
<p>Distribution is wide.</p>
<p>Metabolism is in the liver.</p>
<p>It is excreted in urine partly unchanged and partly as metabolite.</p>
<p>Half life is 8 hours.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="indications">indications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#indications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>used for treatment of sepsis caused by orgasms like Bacteroides
and anaerobic cocci.</li>
<li>Intra-abdominal infections</li>
<li>Septicemia, wounds, pelvic infection</li>
<li>Osteomyelitis.</li>
<li>pelvic infections</li>
<li>Infections of the brain and lungs.</li>
<li>Used in prevention of post operative infection especially after bowel, antibiotic related colitis, eg pseudomembranous colitis, amoebiasis EH</li>
<li>other indications include giardiasis, acute ulcers, gingivitis, and dental infections. and anaerobic vaginosis</li>
<li>Treatment of protozoal infections (intestinal amoebiasis, giardiasis, trichomoniasis) and obligate anaerobic bacteria (Bacteroides fragilis, antibiotic-induced Clostridium difficile, Gardnerella vaginalis)</li>
<li>Treatment of H. pylori in clients who have peptic ulcer disease in combination with tetracycline and bismuth salicylate.</li>
</ul>
<p>Dosage and route of administration</p>
<p>Established anaerobe are usually treated for 7 days.</p>
<p>â€¢ The dose per oral is then 8oomgs initially for 3 days then 400mg or 500mg 8 hourly, or just 400mg 8 hourly for 7 days.</p>
<p>â€¢ By rectum 1gm every 8 hours for 3 days then1gm 12 hourly.</p>
<p>â€¢ By infusion 500mg 8 hourly.</p>
<p>â€¢ In children 7.5/kg every 8 hours by any route.</p>
<p>for surgical prophylaxis</p>
<p>â€¢ Per oral 400mg 8 hourly started 24 hours before surgery then continued postoperatively by IV infusion until oral administration can be resumed for 2days</p>
<p>Complications Side/Adverse Effects Nursing Interventions/Client Education</p>
<p>Gastrointestinal discomfort (nausea, vomiting, dry mouth, and metallic taste) Advise clients to observe for symptoms and to notify the provider.</p>
<p>Darkening of urine Advise clients that this is a harmless effect of metronidazole.</p>
<p>CNS symptoms (numbness of extremities, ataxia, and seizures)</p>
<p>Advise clients to notify the provider if symptoms occur.</p>
<p>Stop metronidazole.</p>
<p>Contraindications/Precautions</p>
<ul>
<li>Use cautiously in clients with renal dysfunction to prevent accumulation of toxic levels with prolonged use.</li>
<li>Avoid use during the first trimester of pregnancy and use with caution during the rest of pregnancy because metronidazole can pass through the placenta.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Interactions</p>
<p>Medication/Food Interactions Nursing Interventions/Client Education</p>
<p>â€¢ Alcohol causes a disulfiram-like reaction/ Advise clients to avoid alcohol consumption.</p>
<p>Metronidazole inhibits inactivation of warfarin.</p>
<p>â€¢ Monitor prothrombin time and INR, and adjust warfarin dosage accordingly</p>
<p>Nursing Administration</p>
<p>â€¢ Administer by oral or IV route.</p>
<p>â€¢ Instruct clients to complete the prescribed course of antimicrobial therapy, even though symptoms may resolve before the full course is completed.</p>
<p>Nursing Evaluation of Medication Effectiveness</p>
<p>â€¢ Depending on therapeutic intent, effectiveness may be evidenced by: Improvement of symptoms (resolution of bloody mucoid diarrhea, formed stools, negative stool results for ameba and Giardia, , decrease or absence of watery vaginal/ urethral discharge, negative blood cultures for anaerobic organisms in the CNS, blood, bones and joints, and soft tissues)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="chloramphenicol">Chloramphenicol<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chloramphenicol" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>It is soluble in water and poorly soluble in alcohol</li>
<li>Chloramphenicol succinate which is used for parenteral administration is highly water soluble</li>
</ul>
<p>pharmacokinetics</p>
<ul>
<li>The usual dosage of chloramphenicol is 50-100mg/kg/d.</li>
<li>After oral administration crystalline chloramphenicol is rapidly and completely absorbed.</li>
<li>A 1g oral dose produces blood levels between 10and 15mcg/ml</li>
<li>Chloramphenicol palmitate is a pro drug that is hydrolyzed in the intestine to yield free chloramphenicol.</li>
</ul>
<p>Pharmacodynamic chloramphenicol potent inhibitor of microbial protein synthesis.</p>
<p>It binds to the 50s sub unit of the bacteria ribosome</p>
<p>It is bacteriostatic, broad spectrum against both aerobic and anaerobic gram positive and gram negative bacterial.</p>
<p>clinical uses</p>
<ul>
<li>it is rarely used due to it potential toxicity and bacterial resistance.</li>
<li>Used to treat; serious rickettsia infections such as typhus and rocky mountain spotted fever.</li>
<li>Alternative for beta lactam antibiotics for treatment of meningococcal meningitis and pneumococcal meningitis</li>
<li>Topical eye infections</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Adverse reactions</p>
<p>GIT disturbance nausea, vomiting and diarrhea.</p>
<p>-This rare in children.</p>
<p>-Oral and vaginal candidiasis may occur due to alteration of the normal flora.</p>
<p>Born marrow disturbance</p>
<p>-suppression of the born marrow</p>
<p>-Aplastic anemia it is irreversible and fatal</p>
<p>Toxicity for new born infants:</p>
<ul>
<li>new born infants lack glucuronic acid for the conjugation and detoxification of chloramphenicol.</li>
</ul>
<p>-Therefore drugs may accumulate resulting in gray baby syndrome with vomiting flaccidity, hypothermia, gray colour, shock and collapse</p>
<p>ANTI-FUNGAL DRUGS</p>
<ul>
<li>Fungi are saprophytic organism as they lack chlorophyll which is present in plants.</li>
<li>Many fungi are commensals in the bodies of healthy people but pose a problem when immune system is compromised.</li>
<li>Since 1970s incidence of fungal infections has increased due to the following reasons</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Increase use of broad spectrum antibiotics which decrease non pathogenic bacterial that compete with the fungi.</li>
<li>Increases number of people with immunosuppression, use of cancer chemotherapy, and immunosuppressants, diabetes mellitus or have burns.</li>
<li>Inversive procedures may introduce fungi into systemic circulation.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="therapeutic-uses">Therapeutic Uses<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#therapeutic-uses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Antifungals are the treatment of choice for systemic fungal infection (Candidiasis, Aspergillosis, Cryptococcosis, Mucormycosis) and non opportunistic mycoses, (Blastomycosis, Histoplasmosis, Coccidioidomycosis)</li>
<li>Resistant is usually due to a</li>
</ul>
<p>1.decrease in membrane ergosterol content
2.Or a change in membrane structure</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="classification-of-anti-fungal-drugs">Classification of anti fungal drugs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification-of-anti-fungal-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Topical anti-fungal</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Polyenes anti-fungal agents e.g. nystatin</li>
<li>Benzoic acid</li>
</ul>
<ol start="2">
<li>Systemic anti fungal</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Polyenes anti-fungal agents e.g. amphotericin B</li>
<li>Fluorinated pyramids e.g. only flu cytosine</li>
<li>Azoles ;imidazole and triazoles
-Imidazole's include clotrimazole and econazole, sulconazole, fenticonazole, ketoconazole, and miconazole
-triazole include fluconazole, itraconazole and voriconazoles among others</li>
</ul>
<ol start="3">
<li>Miscellaneous; terbinafine and Griseofulvin</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Polyenes anti-fungal agents; nystatin and amphotericin B are the only ones in clinical use.</p>
<ul>
<li>MOA; they act by binding to the ergostel in fungal cell walls forming pores or channels which increase permeability and allow leakage of fungal cellular molecules e.g. potassium and magnesium</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="therapeutic-uses">Therapeutic uses<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#therapeutic-uses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Antifungals are the treatment of choice for systemic fungal infection (Candidiasis, Aspergillosis, Cryptococcosis, Mucormycosis) and nonopportunistic mycoses, (Blastomycosis, Histoplasmosis, Coccidioidomycosis).</li>
<li>Some antifungals treat superficial fungal infections:</li>
<li>dermatophytic infections (tinea Pedis [ringworm of the foot], tinea cruris [ringworm of the groin]); candida infections of the skin and mucous membranes; and fungal infections of the nails (Onychomycosis).</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="amphotericin-b">Amphotericin B<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#amphotericin-b" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Amphotericin B has been available for use since 1950s</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="moa-pharmacodynamics">MOA/PHARMACODYNAMICS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#moa-pharmacodynamics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Amphotericin B deoxycholate is an antifungal agent that acts on fungal cell membranes to cause cell death.</li>
<li>Depending on concentration, these agents can be fungi static (slows growth on the fungus) or fungicidal (destroys the fungus).</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pharmacokinetics">PHARMACOKINETICS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pharmacokinetics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>administered intravenously</li>
<li>wide distribution though poor penetration to the CNS</li>
<li><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>90</mn><mi mathvariant="normal">%</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">90 \%</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8056em; vertical-align: -0.0556em;"></span><span class="mord">90%</span></span></span></span></span> bound to plasma, half life of 24 and 15 days</li>
<li>excretion predominantly via the biliary route(slow excretion over a period of days)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="therapeutic-uses">Therapeutic Uses<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#therapeutic-uses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Antifungals are the treatment of choice for systemic fungal infection (Candidiasis, Aspergillosis, Cryptococcosis, Mucormycosis) and nonopportunistic mycoses, (Blastomycosis, Histoplasmosis, Coccidioidomycosis).</li>
</ul>
<p>side/ adverse reactions</p>
<p>Infusion reactions (fever, chills, rigors, and headache) 1 to 3 hr. after initiation</p>
<p>â€¢ Pretreat with diphenhydramine (Benadryl) and acetaminophen.</p>
<p>â€¢ Meperidine (Demerol), Dantrolene, or hydrocortisone may be given for rigors.</p>
<p>Thrombophlebitis Observe infusion sites for signs of erythema, swelling, and pain.</p>
<p>â€¢ Rotate injection sites.</p>
<p>â€¢ Administer in a large vein and administer heparin before infusing amphotericin B</p>
<p>Nephrotoxicity</p>
<p>â€¢ Obtain baseline kidney function (BUN and creatinine) and do weekly kidney function test, Monitor I&amp;O.</p>
<p>â€¢ Infuse 1 L of saline on the day of amphotericin B infusion.</p>
<p>Hypokalemia</p>
<p>â€¢ Monitor electrolyte levels, especially potassium.</p>
<p>â€¢ Administer potassium supplements accordingly.</p>
<p>Bone marrow suppression â€¢ Obtain baseline CBC and hematocrit, and monitor weekly.</p>
<p>ketoconazole</p>
<p>Hepatotoxicity (anorexia, nausea, vomiting, jaundice, dark urine, and clay-colored stools)</p>
<p>â€¢ Obtain baseline liver function studies and monitor liver function monthly.</p>
<p>â€¢ If symptoms occur, notify provider and discontinue medication.</p>
<p>Effects on sex hormones:</p>
<p>â€¢ In males, gynecomastia (enlargement of breast), decreased libido, erectile dysfunction</p>
<p>â€¢ In females, irregular menstrual flow</p>
<p>Advise clients to observe for these symptoms and to notify the provider.</p>
<p>Contraindications/Precautions</p>
<ul>
<li>Antifungals are contraindicated in clients with renal dysfunction because of the risk for nephrotoxicity.</li>
</ul>
<p>Interactions Medication/Food Interactions Nursing Interventions/Client Education</p>
<ul>
<li>Aminoglycosides (gentamicin, streptomycin, cyclosporine) have additive nephrotoxic risk when used concurrently with antifungal medications.</li>
</ul>
<p>Avoid use of these antimicrobials when clients are taking amphotericin B due to additive nephrotoxicity risk.</p>
<ul>
<li>Antifungal effects of Flucytosine (Ancobon) are potentiated with concurrent use of amphotericin B.</li>
</ul>
<p>Potentiating the effects of flucytosine allows for a reduction in amphotericin B dosages.</p>
<p>Nursing Administration</p>
<ul>
<li>Amphotericin B is highly toxic and should be reserved for severe life-threatening fungal infections</li>
</ul>
<p>Systemic infection for mucocutaneous infections</p>
<p>Griseofulvin</p>
<p>â€¢ Griseofulvin is a very insoluble fungistatic drug derived from a species of penicillium.</p>
<p>â€¢ It is only used in the systemic treatment of dermatophytosis.</p>
<p>â€¢ It is administered in a microcrystalline at a dose of 1g per day.</p>
<p>â€¢ Absorption is improved when it is given with fatty foods.</p>
<p>â€¢ Nail infections may require therapy for months to allow regrowth of the new protected nail and is often followed by relapse.</p>
<p>Topical anti fungal</p>
<p>Nystatin</p>
<p>â€¢ Nystatin is a polyene macrolide much like amphotericin B.</p>
<p>â€¢ it is too toxic for parenteral administration and is only used topically</p>
<p>â€¢ nystatin is currently available in creams, ointments, suppositories and other forms for application to skin and mucous membrane.</p>
<p>â€¢ nystatin is active against most candida species and is most commonly used for suppression of local candida infections.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="anti-mycobacterial-agents-anti-tuberculosis">Anti mycobacterial agents (anti-tuberculosis)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#anti-mycobacterial-agents-anti-tuberculosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The main mycobacterial infection are the tuberculosis and leprosy. The treatment of tuberculosis assumes the principle of combination therapy for two main reasons,
I. To prevent emergency of resistance (tubercle bacilli develops resistant very fast when monotherapy is used).
II. To reduce the rate of spread by reducing bacterial population rapidly.
For this reason the available tablets contain multiple drugs in a fixed dose combination (FDC).</li>
</ul>
<p>anti-TB contiâ€™</p>
<ul>
<li>Anti TB are divided into two first line and second line</li>
</ul>
<p>I. First line; this is not a universal principle but depend on local scientific evidence.</p>
<p>The drugs include isoniazid, ethambutol, pyrazinamide and streptomycin.</p>
<p>ii Second line drugs include capreomycin, cycloserine, clarithromycin and ciprofloxacin</p>
<p>Anti TB cont.â€™</p>
<ul>
<li>First initial phase: takes two months and three drugs are used concomitantly.</li>
<li>These includes Isoniazid (H), Rifampicin (R) Pyrazinamide (Z) plus (Ethambutol or streptomycin) if resistant organism are suspected. This combination reduces bacterial population rapidly.</li>
<li>Continuation phase takes four months and two drugs are used these are isoniazid and rifampicin</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="isoniazid">ISONIAZID<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#isoniazid" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Expected Pharmacological Action</li>
<li>This medication is highly specific for mycobacteria. Isoniazid inhibits growth of mycobacteria by preventing synthesis of mycolic acid in the cell wall.</li>
<li>Therapeutic Uses; Indicated for active and latent tuberculosis</li>
<li>Latent: INH only - 6 to 9 months</li>
<li>Active: Multiple medication therapy including INH, for a minimum of 6 months</li>
<li>The initial phase (induction phase) focuses on eradicating the active tubercle bacilli, which will result in non infectious sputum.</li>
<li>The second phase (continuation phase) works toward eliminating any other pathogens in the body.</li>
</ul>
<p>isoniazid cont.â€™</p>
<ul>
<li>Length of treatment varies and may be as short as 6 months for medication-sensitive tuberculosis (2 months for the initial phase and 4 months for the continuation phase) or as long as 24 months for medication-resistant infections.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Complications Side/Adverse Effects Nursing Interventions/Client Education</p>
<ul>
<li>Allergic skin eruptions are the commonest side effects</li>
<li>Others are fever , GIT disturbance</li>
<li>Peripheral neuropathy (tingling, numbness, burning, and pain resulting from deficiency of pyridoxine, vitamin B6 ).</li>
</ul>
<p>Instruct clients to observe for symptoms and to notify the provider if symptoms occur.</p>
<p>Administer 50 to 200 mg of vitamin B6 daily.</p>
<ul>
<li>Hepatotoxicity (anorexia, malaise, fatigue, nausea, and yellowish discoloration of skin and eyes).</li>
</ul>
<p>Instruct clients to observe for symptoms and notify the provider if symptoms occur.</p>
<p>Monitor liver function tests.</p>
<p>Instruct clients to avoid consumption of alcohol.</p>
<p>Medication may need to be discontinued if liver function test results are elevated.</p>
<p>Contraindications/Precautions</p>
<p>INH is contraindicated for clients with liver disease.</p>
<p>Interactions Medication/Food Interactions Nursing Interventions/Client Education</p>
<p>INH inhibits metabolism of phenytoin, leading to buildup of medication and toxicity.</p>
<p>Ataxia and incoordination may indicate toxicity.</p>
<p>Monitor the clientâ€™s levels of phenytoin.</p>
<p>Dosage of phenytoin may need to be adjusted based on phenytoin levels.</p>
<p>Concurrent use of alcohol, rifampin, and pyrazinamide increases the risk for hepatotoxicity.</p>
<p>Instruct clients to avoid alcohol consumption.</p>
<p>Monitor liver function.</p>
<p>Interactions cont.'</p>
<ul>
<li>Induce liver enzymes ,hence affect the metabolism of warfarin, glucocorticoids, narcotics, oral anti diabetes, dapsone and estrogens and oral contraceptives.</li>
<li>Advice clients on oral contraceptives to change method of family planning or use a back up method.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Nursing Administration</p>
<p>â€¢ Administer by oral route</p>
<p>â€¢ For active tuberculosis, direct observation therapy (DOT) is done to ensure adherence.</p>
<p>â€¢ Advise clients to take INH 1 hours before meals or 2 hours after.</p>
<p>â€¢ If gastric discomfort occurs, the client may take INH with meals.</p>
<p>â€¢ Instruct clients to complete the prescribed course of antimicrobial therapy, even though symptoms may resolve before the full course is completed.</p>
<p>rifampicin</p>
<ul>
<li>This is one of the most active anti TB .it is also active against gram positive and gram negative bacteria.</li>
<li>Mechanism of action: Rifampin is bactericidal as a result of inhibition of protein synthesis.</li>
<li>Indications:</li>
</ul>
<p>Rifampin is a broad-spectrum antibiotic effective for gram-positive and gram-negative bacteria,</p>
<p>M. tuberculosis, and M. Leprae.</p>
<p>pharmacokinetics</p>
<ul>
<li>Given orally</li>
<li>Has a wide distribution</li>
<li>It causes orange tinge coloration to saliva ,sputum, tears, sweat and urine.</li>
<li>It is excreted in urine and under goes enterohepatic recycling.</li>
<li>Metabolism is in the liver and the metabolites has anti bacterial activity but poorly absorbed from the gut.</li>
<li>Half life is one to five hours but reduces during treatment since it induces microsomal enzymes, hence its own metabolism.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Side/adverse effects</p>
<p>i) Discoloration of body fluids.</p>
<p>â€¢ Inform clients of expected orange color of urine, saliva, sweat, and tears.</p>
<p>ii)Hepatotoxicity (jaundice, anorexia, and fatigue)</p>
<p>â€¢ Monitor the clientâ€™s liver function.</p>
<p>â€¢ Inform clients regarding symptoms of anorexia, fatigue, and malaise, and instruct them to notify the provider if symptoms occur.</p>
<p>â€¢ Avoid alcohol.</p>
<p>iii) Mild gastrointestinal discomfort associated (anorexia, nausea, and abdominal discomfort.</p>
<p>â€¢ Abdominal discomfort is mild and usually does not require intervention</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="contraindications-precautions">Contraindications/Precautions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#contraindications-precautions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Use cautiously in clients with liver dysfunction.</li>
</ul>
<p>Interactions Medication/Food Interactions Nursing Interventions/Client Education</p>
<p>Rifampin accelerates metabolism of warfarin (Coumadin), oral contraceptives, protease inhibitors, and NNRTIs (medications for HIV), resulting in diminished effectiveness.</p>
<p>â€¢ Increased dosages of HIV medications may be necessary.</p>
<p>â€¢ Monitor PT (prothrombin time) and INR (international normalized ratio)</p>
<p>â€¢ Clients may need to use alternative form of birth control.</p>
<p>Concurrent use with INH and pyrazinamide increases risk of hepatotoxicity.</p>
<p>â€¢ Instruct clients to avoid alcohol consumption. Monitor liver function.</p>
<p>Nursing Evaluation of Medication Effectiveness</p>
<p>Depending on therapeutic intent, effectiveness may be evidenced by:</p>
<p>â€¢ Improvement of tuberculosis symptoms such as clear breath sounds, no night sweats, increased appetite, no afternoon rises of temperature</p>
<p>â€¢ 3 negative sputum cultures for tuberculosis, usually taking 3 to 6 months to achieve.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="ethambutol">ethambutol<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ethambutol" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Pharmacodynamics;</li>
<li>Mechanism of action through inhibiting inhibition of bacterial growth through suppression of RNA synthesis. Resistance emergence occurs rapidly if used on its own.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pharmacokinetic">Pharmacokinetic<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pharmacokinetic" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>good absorption from GIT.</li>
<li>Metabolism is in the liver.</li>
<li>Excretion in urine.</li>
<li>It can reach therapeutic concentrated with CSF for tuberculosis.</li>
</ul>
<p>Unwanted effects</p>
<p>These are common.</p>
<p>â€¢ Optic neuritis dose related especially if renal function decreases.</p>
<p>this leads to visual disturbances, red/ green color blindness followed by decreased visual acuity.</p>
<p>Monitor color vision in long treatments</p>
<p>Contraindication</p>
<p>â€¢ Patients with known optic neuritis</p>
<p>Patients who are unable to appreciate and report visual side effects or changes in vision e.g.</p>
<p>â€¢ young children and unconscious patients</p>
<p>pyrazinamide</p>
<ul>
<li>It is often inactive in neutral PH.</li>
</ul>
<p>Pharmacodynamics.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>its mechanism of action is unknown but it is tuberculostatic at acidic PH.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>it is very effective against intracellular organism in macrophages since after phagocytosis, in which PH is low.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Pharmacokinetic</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>it has good gut absorption .</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>it is widely distributed in that it crosses the BBB</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>excreted in the kidneys</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>DAPSONE</p>
<ul>
<li>pharmacodynamics</li>
<li>DAPSONE is chemically related to sulphonemides and it acts by inhibiting the enzyme dihydrofolate reluctance hence inhibits folate synthesis.</li>
<li>Its action is antagonized by PABA. resistance to this drug</li>
<li>Has increased, hence it â€˜s combined with other drugs during treatment.</li>
<li>Pharmacokinetic</li>
<li>Good oral absorption.</li>
<li>It under goes enteral hepatic recycling.</li>
<li>It has a half life of 24 to 48 hours</li>
<li>it is excreted in feces</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Unwanted effects</p>
<ul>
<li>Hemolysis of white blood cells .</li>
<li>Anorexia , nausea and vomiting.</li>
<li>Fever and allergic dermatitis,</li>
<li>neuropathy</li>
<li>Leprareation where there is exacerbation of lepromatous lesions can occur and a syndrome resembling infectious mononucleosis which can be fatal.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Antiviral agents</p>
<ul>
<li>Viruses present a more difficulty problem of chemotherapy than do higher organisms, e.g. bacteria, for they are intracellular parasites that use the metabolism of the host cells.</li>
<li>Antiviral agents are most active when virus are replicating.</li>
<li>The earlier the treatment is given the better.</li>
<li>Apart from primary infections ,viral illness is often the consequences of reactivation of latent virus in the body.</li>
<li>Patients whose immune system is compromised may suffer particular severe illness.</li>
<li>Viruses are capable of developing resistance.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="antiviral-and-antiretroviral-cont">Antiviral and antiretroviral cont.'<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#antiviral-and-antiretroviral-cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>Drug</th><th>viruses</th><th>Chemical type</th><th>target</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Non nucleotide reverse</td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>transcriptase inhibitor.</td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>(NNRTIs);Nevirapine,</td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Delavirdine.</td><td>HIV Virus</td><td>Non nucleotide analogue</td><td>Reverse transcriptase</td></tr><tr><td>protease inhibitors;</td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Saquinavir, Ritonavir,</td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Indinavir, Nelfinavir.</td><td>HIV virus</td><td>Peptide analogue</td><td>HIV protease</td></tr><tr><td>Ribavirin</td><td>Broad spectrum: HCV, HSV,</td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Measles, Lasa fever, SARS</td><td>Triazole carboxamide</td><td>RNA mutagen</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Amantadine/Rimantadine</td><td>Influenza A strains</td><td>Tricyclic amine</td><td>Matrix</td></tr><tr><td>protein/hemagglutinin</td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Zanamivir, oseltamivir</td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>phosphate</td><td>Influenza strains A and B</td><td>Neuraminic acid mimetic</td><td>Neuraminidase inhibitor</td></tr><tr><td>Pleconaril</td><td>picornaviruses</td><td>Small cyclic</td><td>Blocks attachment and</td></tr><tr><td>coating</td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Interferons</td><td>Hepatitis B and C virus</td><td>protein</td><td>Cell defense</td></tr></tbody></table>
<table><thead><tr><th>Drug(</th><th>Viruses</th><th>chemical</th><th>Target</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>vidarabine</td><td>herpesvirus</td><td>Nucleoside analogue</td><td>Virus polymerase</td></tr><tr><td>acyclovir</td><td>Herpes simplex (HSV)</td><td>Nucleoside analogue</td><td>Virus polymerase</td></tr><tr><td>Ganciclovir and valganciclovir</td><td>Cytomegalovirus (CMV)</td><td>nucleoside analogue</td><td>Virus polymerase</td></tr><tr><td>Nucleoside reverse transcriptase inhibitor (NRTI) zidovudine( AZT) didanosine (ddI), zalcitabine (ddC), stavudine (D4T), lamivudine (3TC)</td><td>Retroviruses (HIV)</td><td>Nucleoside analogue</td><td>Reverse transcriptase</td></tr><tr><td>Non nucleotide reverse transcriptase inhibitor (NNRTI) nevirapine and delavirdine</td><td>HIV virus</td><td>Non nucleotide analogue</td><td>Reverse transcriptase</td></tr><tr><td>Protease inhibitors saquinavir, Ritonavir, indinavir, nelfinavir</td><td>HIV virus</td><td>Peptide analogue</td><td>HIV protease</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>ACYCLOVIR</p>
<ul>
<li>Expected Pharmacological Action</li>
<li>Acyclovir prevents the reproduction of viral DNA and thus interrupts cell replication.</li>
</ul>
<p>Therapeutic Uses</p>
<ul>
<li>Acyclovir is used to treat herpes simplex and varicella-zoster viruses</li>
</ul>
<p>Ganciclovir is used for treatment and prevention of cytomegalovirus (CMV).</p>
<ul>
<li>Prevention therapy using ganciclovir is given for clients who have HIV/AIDS, organ transplants, and other immunocompromised states.</li>
<li>Interferon alfa-2b and lamivudine are used to treat hepatitis.</li>
<li>Oseltamivir is used to treat influenza A and B.</li>
<li>Ribavirin is used to treat respiratory syncytial virus (RSV) and influenza.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Complications Side/Adverse Effects Nursing Interventions/Client education</p>
<p>Acyclovir Phlebitis and inflammation at the site of infusion</p>
<p>â€¢ Rotate IV injection sites.</p>
<p>â€¢ Monitor IV sites for swelling and redness.</p>
<p>Nephrotoxicity</p>
<p>â€¢ Administer acyclovir infusion slowly over 1 hr.</p>
<p>â€¢ Ensure adequate hydration during infusion and 2 hr. after to minimize nephrotoxicity by administering IV fluids and increasing oral fluid intake as prescribed.</p>
<p>Mild discomfort associated with oral therapy (nausea, headache, diarrhea)</p>
<p>â€¢ Observe for symptoms and notify the provider.</p>
<p>Complications Side/Adverse Effects Nursing Interventions/Client education cont.'</p>
<p>Ganciclovir</p>
<p>Granulocytopenia and thrombocytopenia</p>
<p>â€¢ Obtain baseline CBC and platelet count.</p>
<p>â€¢ Administer granulocyte colony-stimulating factors.</p>
<p>â€¢ Monitor WBC, absolute neutrophil, and platelet counts.</p>
<p>Contraindications/Precautions</p>
<p>â€¢ Acyclovir should be used cautiously in clients with renal impairment or dehydration, and clients taking nephrotoxic medications.</p>
<p>â€¢ Ganciclovir is Pregnancy Risk Category C;</p>
<p>â€¢ contraindicated in clients with a neutrophil count below 500/mm3 or platelet counts less than 25,000/mm3, and should be used cautiously in clients with pre-existing low white and platelet counts.</p>
<p>Interactions Medication/Food Interactions Nursing Interventions/Client Education</p>
<p>Acyclovir</p>
<p>â€¢ Probenecid may decrease elimination of acyclovir.</p>
<p>â€¢ Monitor for medication toxicity.</p>
<p>â€¢ Concurrent use of zidovudine may cause drowsiness.</p>
<p>â€¢ Use with caution</p>
<p>Ganciclovir</p>
<p>â€¢ Cytotoxic medications may cause increased toxicity.</p>
<p>â€¢ Use together with caution.</p>
<p>Nursing Administration</p>
<p>Acyclovir:</p>
<p>For topical administration, advise clients to put on rubber gloves to avoid transfer of virus to other areas of the body.</p>
<p>Administer IV infusion slowly over 1 hr or longer.</p>
<p>Inform clients to expect symptom relief but not cure.</p>
<p>Instruct clients to wash affected area with soap and water 3 to 4 times/day and to keep the lesions dry after washing.</p>
<p>Advise clients to refrain from sexual contact while lesions are present.</p>
<p>Clients with healed herpetic lesions should continue to use condoms to prevent transmission of the virus.</p>
<p>Nursing administration</p>
<p>Ganciclovir</p>
<p>Administer IV infusion slowly, with an infusion pump, over at least 1 hr.</p>
<p>Administer oral medication with food.</p>
<p>Administer intraocular for CMV retinitis.</p>
<p>Instruct clients to complete the prescribed course of antimicrobial therapy, even though symptoms may resolve before the full course is completed.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="antiretroviral-drugs">Antiretroviral drugs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#antiretroviral-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>antiretroviral therapy goal is to delay disease progression and to prolong survival by suppressing the replication of the virus.</li>
<li>Two types of antiretroviral combination are recommended for initial HIV therapy;</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>first line ; 1 NNRTI plus 2NRTI.</li>
<li>second line; 1PI plus 2 NRTI.</li>
<li>protease inhibitors are preserved for second line</li>
</ol>
<p>five goals of ART</p>
<ol>
<li>to reduce amount of HIV virus in the body.</li>
<li>Support and restore the immune system.</li>
<li>Improve the quality of life.</li>
<li>Reduce HIV related illness and deaths.</li>
<li>reduce general risk of transmission.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mechanism-of-action-of-arvs">Mechanism of action of ARVs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mechanism-of-action-of-arvs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Block reverse transcriptase to disrupt copying of HIV genetic cord(NRTIs, NNRTIs).</li>
<li>Block protease enzyme, preventing maturation of new virions.(PIs).</li>
<li>Prevent fusion of HIV with cell membranes (fusion inhibitors).</li>
<li>Block CCR5 co receptor (CCR5 antagonist)</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="hiv-life-cycle-targets-for-antivirals">HIV life cycle: Targets for antivirals<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hiv-life-cycle-targets-for-antivirals" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251214-a5ff7bde.jpeg" alt="img-57.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="zidovudine-retrovir">ZIDOVUDINE (REtrovir)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#zidovudine-retrovir" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Other Medications:</li>
<li>Didanosine (Videx)</li>
<li>Stavudine (Zerit)</li>
<li>Lamivudine (Epivir)</li>
<li>Abacavir (Ziagen)</li>
</ul>
<p>Combination Medications:
Abacavir, lamivudine zidovudine (Trizivir)
Abacavir, lamivudine (Epzicom)
Lamivudine, zidovudine (Combivir)</p>
<p>Expected Pharmacological Action</p>
<ul>
<li>Reduces HIV symptoms by inhibiting DNA synthesis and thus viral replication.</li>
</ul>
<p>Therapeutic Uses</p>
<ul>
<li>Used to treat HIV infection</li>
<li>Route of Administration: Oral, IV</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Side/Adverse Effects Nursing Interventions/Client Education</p>
<p>Suppressed bone marrow resulting in anemia, agranulocytosis (neutropenia) and thrombocytopenia</p>
<p>â€¢ Monitor CBC and platelets.</p>
<p>â€¢ Advise clients that transfusions may be needed.</p>
<p>Lactic acidosis</p>
<p>â€¢ Monitor for symptoms of lactic acidosis, such as hyperventilation, nausea, and abdominal pain.</p>
<p>â€¢ Pregnancy increases the risk of lactic acidosis.</p>
<p>Nausea, vomiting, diarrhea</p>
<p>â€¢ Clients may take the medication with food to reduce gastric irritation. Monitor fluids and electrolytes.</p>
<p>Hepatomegaly/fatty liver</p>
<p>â€¢ Monitor liver enzymes</p>
<p>Medication/Food Interactions Nursing Interventions/Client Education</p>
<p>Probenecid, valproic acid, and methadone may increase zidovudine.</p>
<p>â€¢ Reduce dosage</p>
<p>â€¢ Monitor for medication toxicity.</p>
<p>Ganciclovir or medications that decrease bone marrow production may further suppress bone marrow.</p>
<p>â€¢ Use together with caution.</p>
<p>Rifampin and ritonavir may reduce zidovudine levels.</p>
<p>â€¢ Adjust dosage if needed.</p>
<p>Phenytoin may alter both medication levels.</p>
<p>â€¢ Monitor medication levels.</p>
<p>Nursing Administration</p>
<ul>
<li>Monitor for bone marrow suppression.</li>
<li>Obtain baseline CBC and platelets at the start of therapy and every 4 weeks.</li>
<li>Anemia may be treated with epoetin alfa or transfusions.</li>
<li>Neutropenia may be treated with colony-stimulating factors.</li>
<li>Advise clients to monitor for fever, sore throat, increased bleeding, bruising or fatigue.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="non-nucleoside-reverse-transcriptase-inhibitors-nnrti-s">Non-nucleoside reverse transcriptase inhibitors (NNRTI s)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#non-nucleoside-reverse-transcriptase-inhibitors-nnrti-s" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Select medication: delavirdine (Rescriptor), efavirenz (Sustiva)</li>
<li>Other Medications: nevirapine (Viramune), etravirine (Intelence)</li>
<li>Expected Pharmacological Action</li>
<li>NNRTIs act directly on reverse transcriptase to stop HIV reprication</li>
<li>Therapeutic Uses</li>
<li>Primary HIV-1 infection</li>
<li>Often used in combination with other antiretroviral agents to prevent medication resistance</li>
<li>Route of administration:</li>
<li>Oral</li>
<li>Monitor for rash.</li>
</ul>
<p>Complications Side/Adverse Effects Nursing Interventions/Client Education</p>
<p>Rash, which may become serious and lead to Stevenâ€™s-Johnson syndrome</p>
<p>â€¢ Monitor for rash.</p>
<p>â€¢ Treat with diphenhydramine (Benadryl), if prescribed.</p>
<p>â€¢ Notify the provider for fever or blistering.</p>
<p>Flu-like symptoms, headache, fatigue</p>
<p>â€¢ Monitor for adverse reactions.</p>
<p>â€¢ Encourage rest and adequate oral fluid intake</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="contraindications-precautions">Contraindications/Precautions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#contraindications-precautions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>NNRTIs are Pregnancy Risk Category C.</li>
<li>These medications are contraindicated in clients with medication hypersensitivity.</li>
<li>Use with caution in clients who have liver disease.</li>
</ul>
<p>Medication/Food Interactions Nursing Interventions/Client Education</p>
<p>Antacids may decrease absorption of delavirdine.</p>
<p>â€¢ Allow 1 hr. between medications.</p>
<p>NNRTIs may increase effects of amphetamines, antihistamines, calcium channel blockers, ergot alkaloids, quinidine, warfarin, and others.</p>
<p>â€¢ Monitor for medication toxicity.</p>
<p>Rifampin and phenytoin may cause decrease in levels of delavirdine.</p>
<p>â€¢ Do not use together.</p>
<p>Didanosine may reduce both medicationsâ€™ absorption.</p>
<p>Allow 1 hour between medications.</p>
<p>NNRTIs hypotension and changes in vision.</p>
<p>â€¢ may cause increase in sildenafil level.</p>
<p>â€¢ Monitor for Use together with caution.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="protease-inhibitors">Protease inhibitors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#protease-inhibitors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Members of this group are;
ritonavir (Norvir)
Saquinavir (Invirase)
Indinavir (Crixivan)
Amprenavir (Agenerase)
Nelfinavir (Viracept)
Mechanism Of Action
Protease inhibitors act against HIV-1 and HIV-2 to alter and inactivate the virus by inhibiting enzymes needed for HIV replication.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="indication">Indication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#indication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Used to treat HIV infections
Should be used with another antiretroviral medication to reduce medication resistance
Route of administration: Oral</p>
<p>Side/Adverse Effects Nursing Interventions/Client Education</p>
<p>â€¢ Diabetes mellitus/hyperglycemia ; Monitor serum glucose,</p>
<p>Adjust diet and administer anti-diabetic medications as prescribed. Advise clients to monitor for increased thirst and urine output.</p>
<p>â€¢ hypersensitivity reaction;</p>
<p>Monitor for rash.</p>
<p>Notify the provider if rash develops.</p>
<p>â€¢ Nausea and vomiting; Take medication with food to reduce GI effects and increase absorption.</p>
<p>â€¢ Elevated serum lipids</p>
<p>Monitor for hyperlipidemia.</p>
<p>Adjust diet.</p>
<p>â€¢ Thrombocytopenia, leukopenia</p>
<p>Monitor CBC. Monitor for signs of infection (fever, sore throat). Monitor for bleeding, blood in stool and bruising</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="medication-food-interactions-nursing-interventions-client-education">Medication/Food Interactions Nursing Interventions/Client Education<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#medication-food-interactions-nursing-interventions-client-education" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Ritonavir may cause these medications to accumulate to toxic levels: Bupropion, carbamazepine, diazepam, lidocaine, prednisone clozapine, lovastatin, simvastatin, alprazolam, and ergotamine.
Avoid concurrent use.</li>
<li>Ritonavir may increase medication levels of sildenafil, tadalafil, and vardenafil.
Use with caution. Dosages of these medications may need to be reduced.</li>
<li>Ritonavir decreases levels of ethynyl estradiol in oral contraceptives. Instruct clients to use an alternative form of birth control.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="entry-fusion-inhibitors">Entry/fusion inhibitors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#entry-fusion-inhibitors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Enfuvirtide this is the first antiretroviral to target the host cell attachment.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="mechanism-of-action-pharmacodynamics">Mechanism of action/pharmacodynamics<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mechanism-of-action-pharmacodynamics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>It inhibits fusion of the cellular and viral membranes.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pharmacokinetic">Pharmacokinetic<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pharmacokinetic" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

adverse effects</li>
