<li>Drug tolerance</li>
<li>Withdrawal symptoms</li>
</ul>
<p>Contraindication
Renal damage
Hepatic ailments
Pulmonary insufficient</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="anticonvulsant-ant-seizure-anti-epileptic-medication">anticonvulsant/ant seizure /anti epileptic medication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#anticonvulsant-ant-seizure-anti-epileptic-medication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Barbiturates: Phenobarbital (Luminal), Primidone (Mysoline) amobarbital, metharbital.</li>
<li>Hydantoins: phenytoin (Dilantin)</li>
<li>Benzodiazepines: Diazepam (Valium), Lorazepam (Ativan)</li>
<li>Carboxamide: Carbamazepine (Tegretol, carbatrol), oxcarbazepine (Trileptal)</li>
<li>Phenyltriazine: Lamotrigine (lamictal)</li>
<li>pyrrolidines: levetiracetam (Keppra)</li>
<li>Succinimides: ethosuximide (zorontin)</li>
<li>Miscellaneous: acetazolamide (Diamox), primidone(mysoline), valproic acid(depakene, Depakote), zonisamide (zonegran)</li>
</ul>
<p>Mechanism of action</p>
<ul>
<li>Unfortunately the mechanism of seizure activity is not well understood.</li>
<li>AEDs control seizure disorders by various mechanisms, which include:</li>
</ul>
<p>âœ“ Slowing the entrance of sodium and calcium back into the neuron and, thus extending the time it takes for the nerve to return to its active state.</p>
<p>âœ“ Suppressing neuronal firing, which decreases seizure activity and prevents propagation of seizure activity into other areas of the brain.</p>
<p>âœ“ Decreasing seizure activity by enhancing the inhibitory effects of gamma butyric acid (GABA.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="therapeutic-uses">Therapeutic uses<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#therapeutic-uses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="phenobarbital">Phenobarbital<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#phenobarbital" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Phenobarbital is used for partial seizures and generalized tonic clonic seizures.</li>
<li>This medication is not effective against absence seizures.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="phenytoin">Phenytoin<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#phenytoin" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>phenytoin effective against all major forms of epilepsy except absence seizures.</li>
<li>Use IV route for status epilepticus.</li>
</ul>
<p>Phenytoin is an ant dysrhythmic.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="carbamazepine">Carbamazepine<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#carbamazepine" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Carbamazepine is used for the treatment of partial (simple and complex) seizures, tonic-clonic seizures, bipolar disorder, and trigeminal and glossopharyngeal neuralgias.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="therapeutic-use-cont">Therapeutic use cont.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#therapeutic-use-cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Ethosuximide is only indicated for absence seizures.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="valproic-acid">Valproic acid :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#valproic-acid" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Valproic acid is used for partial, generalized, and absence seizures; bipolar disorder; and migraine headaches.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="gabapentin">Gabapentin:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#gabapentin" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Gabapentin is used as a single agent for control of partial seizures.</li>
<li>This medication is also used for neuropathic pain and the prevention of migraine headaches.
Diazepam : Diazepam is used in status epilepticus.</li>
</ul>
<p>Adverse drug reaction of anti epileptics/ anticonvulsant medication</p>
<p>â€¢ Almost all cause undesired effects</p>
<p>â€¢ All cross the placenta barrier;</p>
<p>âž¢Cleft lip, cardiac malformation; phenobarbitone, phenytoin.</p>
<p>âž¢Spina bifida; folate deficiency induced by sodium valproate, phenytoin, phenobarbital</p>
<p>phenytoin</p>
<p>â€¢ This is the oldest non sedative anti seizure drug introduced in 1938.</p>
<p>Mechanism of action</p>
<p>It blocks sodium channels and inhibit the generation of rapidly repetitive action potentials.</p>
<p>pharmacokinetics; oral ,IM, IV.</p>
<p>Metabolism; is in the liver.</p>
<p>Side /adverse effects and nursing education</p>
<p>CNS effects (nystagmus, sedation, ataxia, double vision, cognitive impairment)</p>
<p>â€¢ Monitor for symptoms and notify the provider if symptoms occur.</p>
<p>Gingival hyperplasia (softening and overgrowth of gum tissue, tenderness, and bleeding gums)</p>
<p>â€¢ Advise clients to maintain good oral hygiene (dental flossing, massaging gums).</p>
<p>â€¢ Skin rash â€¢ Stop medication if rash develops.</p>
<p>â€¢ Teratogenic (cleft palate, heart defects)</p>
<p>â€¢ Avoid use in pregnancy..</p>
<p>Side /adverse effects and nursing education</p>
<p>Cardiovascular effects (dysrhythmias, hypotension)</p>
<p>â€¢ Administer at slow IV rate and in dilute solution to prevent adverse CV effects.</p>
<p>Endocrine and other effects (coarsening of facial features, hirsutism, and interference with vitamin D metabolism)</p>
<p>â€¢ Instruct clients to report changes.</p>
<p>â€¢ Encourage clients to consume adequate amounts of calcium and vitamin D.</p>
<p>PSYCHOTHRAPEUTIC AGENTS</p>
<ul>
<li>These are antipsychotics, antidepressants and mood stabilizers</li>
</ul>
<p>ANTIDEPRESSANTS</p>
<ul>
<li>Depression is a mood (affective) disorder and is a widespread problem, ranking high among causes of disability.</li>
<li>Clients starting antidepressant medication therapy for depression need to be advised that symptom relief can take 1 to 3 weeks and possibly 2 to 3 months for full benefits to be achieved. Encourage continued adherence.</li>
<li>Clients with major depression may require hospitalization with close observation and suicide precautions until the antidepressant medications reach their peak effect.</li>
</ul>
<p>Antidepressants cont.â€™</p>
<p>Antidepressant mediations are classified into four main groups:</p>
<p>âž¢ Tricyclic antidepressants</p>
<p>âž¢ Selective serotonin reuptake inhibitors (SSRIs)</p>
<p>âž¢ Monoamine oxidase inhibitors (MAOIs)</p>
<p>âž¢ Atypical antidepressant</p>
<p>a)Tricyclic antidepressant;</p>
<p>Amitriptyline (Elavil), Imipramine (Tofranil), Doxepin (Sinequan) , Nortriptyline (Aventyl), Amoxapine (Asendin),</p>
<p>Trimipramine (Surmontil)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mechanism-of-action">Mechanism of action<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mechanism-of-action" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Tricyclic antidepressant medications block reuptake of norepinephrine and serotonin in the synaptic space, thereby intensifying the effects of these neurotransmitters.
Therapeutic Uses</li>
<li>Depression</li>
<li>Chronic pain</li>
<li>childhood Enuresis</li>
<li>Obsessive compulsive disorders (clomipramine)</li>
</ul>
<p>Side effects</p>
<ul>
<li>Sedation</li>
<li>Anticholinergic effects
âœ“ Dry mouth
âœ“Blurred vision
âœ“ Photophobia
âœ“ Urinary hesitancy or retention
âœ“ Constipation
âœ“Seizures and impotence</li>
<li>older patients; dizziness, postural hypotension, constipation, delayed micturition, edema, muscle tremors.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Tricyclic overdose</p>
<p>â€¢ Lethal 70 to 80 percent die before reaching the hospital</p>
<p>â€¢ CNS and cardiovascular systems are affected.</p>
<p>â€¢ death results from seizures and dysrhythmias</p>
<p>no specific antidote</p>
<p>âœ“ Decrease drug absorption with activated charcoal</p>
<p>âœ“ Speed elimination by alkalinizing urine</p>
<p>âœ“ Manage seizures and dysrhythmias</p>
<p>âœ“ Basic life support</p>
<p>Drug interactions</p>
<ul>
<li>Antipsychotics and steroids may inhibit TCAs</li>
<li>Aspirin may displace TCAs from binding site</li>
<li>TCAs and alcohol potentiate the effects of each other hence death due to severe respiratory distress.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="b-monoamine-oxidase-inhibitors-maoi-s">b)Monoamine Oxidase Inhibitors (MAOI s)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-monoamine-oxidase-inhibitors-maoi-s" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>phenelzine (Nardil)</li>
<li>Isocarboxazid (Marplan)</li>
<li>Tranylcypromine (Parnate)</li>
<li>Selegiline (Emsam) - transdermal MAOI</li>
</ul>
<p>Mechanism of action;
MAOIs inhibit the MAO enzyme system in the CNS.
Amines ( Norepinephrine, Dopamine And Serotonin) resulting in higher levels in the brain to transmit impulses.</p>
<p>Therapeutic use</p>
<ul>
<li>Highly effective considered second line treatment for depression not responsive to cyclics.</li>
<li>Atypical depression</li>
<li>Bulimia nervosa</li>
<li>Obsessive compulsive disorders (OCD)</li>
</ul>
<p>Side effects</p>
<p>Few side effects most common; orthostatic hypotension.</p>
<p>Tachycardia, dizziness, insomnia, anorexia, blurred vision, palpitation, drowsiness, headache, nausea, impotence</p>
<p>MAOIs overdose</p>
<p>â€¢ Symptoms appear 12 hours after ingestion.</p>
<p>these are; tachycardia, circulatory collapse, seizure, coma.</p>
<p>Treatment;</p>
<p>âž¢gastric lavage</p>
<p>âž¢Urine acidification</p>
<p>âž¢hemodialysis</p>
<p>MAOIs hypertensive crisis and tyramine</p>
<p>â€¢ Ingestion of food/drinks with amino acid tyramine leads to hypertensive crisis, which may lead to cerebral hemorrhage, stroke, coma, or death</p>
<p>â€¢ Avoid foods that contain tyramine;</p>
<p>âž¢aged mature cheese</p>
<p>âž¢Smoked/pickled or aged meat, fish, poultry(herring ,sausages, corned beef, salami, pepperoni).</p>
<p>âž¢Red wine(chianti, sherry, vermouth)</p>
<p>âž¢Italian broad beans (fava).</p>
<p>Contraindications/Precautions</p>
<ul>
<li>MAOIs are Pregnancy Risk Category C.</li>
<li>These medications are contraindicated in clients taking SSRIs and in those with pheochromocytoma, heart failure, cardiovascular and cerebral vascular disease, and severe renal insufficiency.</li>
<li>Use cautiously in clients with diabetes and seizure disorders or those taking TCAs.</li>
<li>Transdermal selegiline is contraindicated for clients taking carbamazepine (Tegretol) or oxcarbazepine (Trileptal), which may increase blood levels of the MAOI.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>c)Selective Serotonin Reuptake Inhibitors (SSRIs)</p>
<p>â€¢ Fluoxetine (Prozac)</p>
<p>â€¢ Citalopram (Celexa)</p>
<p>â€¢ Escitalopram oxalate (Lexapro)</p>
<p>â€¢ Paroxetine (Paxil)</p>
<p>â€¢ Sertraline (Zoloft)</p>
<p>Pharmacodynamics</p>
<p>â€¢ SSRI inhibit the reuptake of only serotonin at the part of the amine pump that is specifically for reuptake of serotonin.</p>
<p>â€¢ This explains why these drugs have lesser unwanted effects compared to TCAs.</p>
<p>â€¢ the drug of choice for Depression.</p>
<p>Therapeutic Uses</p>
<ul>
<li>Major depression</li>
<li>Obsessive compulsive disorders (OCD)</li>
<li>Bulimia nervosa</li>
<li>Premenstrual dysphoric disorders</li>
<li>Panic disorders</li>
<li>Posttraumatic disorder (PTSD)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>pharmacokinetics</p>
<ul>
<li>SSRIs are well absorbed orally</li>
<li>Wide distribution and half life of fifteen to 24 hour but fluoxetine has a half life of 24 to ninety six hours.</li>
<li>They achieve effects within 2 to 4 weeks.</li>
<li>Paroxetine and fluoxetine are not used with TCAs since they inhibit TCA hepatic metabolism</li>
</ul>
<p>Unwanted effects</p>
<p>This include nausea and vomiting, diarrhea, agitation, anorgasmia priapism.</p>
<p>Drug interaction</p>
<ul>
<li>MAOIs, TCAs, and St. Johnâ€™s wort increase the risk of serotonin syndrome.</li>
<li>Fluoxetine can displace warfarin (Coumadin) from bound protein and result in increased warfarin levels.</li>
<li>Fluoxetine can increase the levels of tricyclic antidepressants and lithium.</li>
<li>Fluoxetine suppresses platelet aggregation and thus increases the risk of bleeding when used concurrently with NSAIDs and anticoagulants.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="d-second-generation-antidepressants">d) Second generation antidepressants<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#d-second-generation-antidepressants" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Newer</p>
<ul>
<li>Fewer side effects than tricyclic but not superior in overall efficacy or onset of action.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="examples-are">Examples are<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#examples-are" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Trazodone,
Bupropion
Duloxetine</p>
<p>Mechanism of action</p>
<p>â€¢ selective inhibition of serotonin uptake</p>
<p>â€¢ Advantage over tricyclic and MAOIs little or no effect on cardiovascular system.</p>
<p>Therapeutic uses</p>
<p>Depression, bipolar affective disorders, obesity, eating disorders, obsessive compulsive disorders, panic attacks, myoclonus, treatment for various substance abuse problems (bupropion is used for smoking cessation treatment)</p>
<p>Side effects</p>
<ul>
<li>CNS; headache, dizziness, nervousness, insomnia, fatigue and tremors.</li>
<li>GI; nausea, diarrheal, constipation, dry mouth, sweating, sexual dysfunction .</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>ANTIPSYCHOTIC AGENTS/TRANQUILIZERS/NEUROLEPTICS</p>
<p>â€¢ Classification of neuroleptic is based on chemical structure or severity of resulting unwanted effects.</p>
<p>â€¢ Based on unwanted effect;</p>
<p>Conventional (typical, first generation)</p>
<p>Examples;</p>
<p>chlorpromazine, haloperidol, and fluphenazine</p>
<p>Newer (atypical, second generation)</p>
<p>Example; clozapine, loxapine, asenapine, olanzapine, quetiapine, paliperidone, risperidone, sertindole.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="classification-cont">Classification cont.'<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification-cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The distinction between typical and atypical neuroleptic is not clear but rest on ; receptor profile , incidence of extrapyramidal effects which are less in the atypical group, efficacy in treatment and efficacy in negative symptoms.
Classification according to chemical structures;
Phenothiazines; chlorpromazine 100 to 1500 mg , trifluoperazine, fluphenazine 1 to 10 mg
Butyrophenones; haloperidol 2 to 20 mg
Dibenzodiazepine; clozapine 25 to 900 mg
Thienobenzodiazepines; olanzapine
Thioxanthene's; flupentixol 6 to 18 mg
Benzisoxazole; risperidone 1to 12mg</li>
</ul>
<p>Pharmacodynamics</p>
<ul>
<li>They act by blocking the dopamine receptor.</li>
</ul>
<p>Indication</p>
<ul>
<li>Treatment of acute and chronic psychosis</li>
<li>Schizophrenia</li>
<li>Bipolar disorders (primarily the manic phase)</li>
<li>Touretteâ€™s syndrome</li>
<li>Delusional and schizoaffective disorders</li>
<li>Dementia</li>
<li>Prevention of nausea/vomiting through blocking of dopamine in the chemoreceptor trigger zone of the medulla</li>
<li>hiccups</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Side effects typical antipsychotic</p>
<ul>
<li>Extrapyramidal effects (dystonia, parkinsonism, tardative dyskinesia)</li>
<li>Anticholinergic effects; (dry mouth, blurred vision, urinary retention, constipation and impotence)</li>
<li>Cardiovascular effects; tachycardia, arrhythmias, postural hypotention</li>
<li>Galactorrhea,</li>
<li>gynecomastia</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="side-effect-atypical-antipsychotics">Side effect atypical antipsychotics<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#side-effect-atypical-antipsychotics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Clozopine; weight gain, agranulocytosis</li>
<li>Risperidone; insomnia anxiety, agitation</li>
<li>Olanzapine; weight gain, dizziness, sedation, anticholinergic effect</li>
</ul>
<p>Mood stabilizers</p>
<p>lithium carbonate</p>
<p>Expected Pharmacological Action</p>
<p>Lithium produces neurochemical changes in the brain, including serotonin receptor blockade.</p>
<p>There is evidence that the use of lithium can show a decrease in neuronal atrophy and/or an increase in neuronal growth.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="therapeutic-uses">Therapeutic Uses<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#therapeutic-uses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Lithium is used in the treatment of bipolar disorders. Lithium controls episodes of acute mania, helps prevent the return of mania or depression, and decreases the incidence of suicide.</li>
<li>Other uses:</li>
<li>Alcoholism</li>
<li>Bulimia</li>
<li>Schizophrenia</li>
</ul>
<p>pharmacokinetics</p>
<ul>
<li>Absorption :rate and extent vary with dose form. absorption is complete within hours of oral use.</li>
<li>Distribution :wide distribution in the body, concentration in thyroid gland, bone and brain tissue exceed serum levels.</li>
<li>Metabolism :not metabolized</li>
<li>Excretion : excreted unchanged in urine. Half lif18 hours (adolescence)to 3 hour (elderly).</li>
</ul>
<p>Dosage adults :300mg to six hundred mg up to q.i.d increasing to achieve optimal dosage.</p>
<p>Adverse reaction</p>
<ul>
<li>Gastrointestinal distress (nausea, diarrhea, abdominal pain).</li>
<li>Fine hand tremors that can interfere with purposeful motor skills and can be exacerbated by factors such as stress and caffeine.</li>
<li>Polyuria, mild thirst.</li>
<li>Weight gain</li>
<li>Renal toxicity</li>
</ul>
<p>Goiter and hypothyroidism with long-term treatment Brady dysrhythmia, hypotension, and electrolyte imbalances .</p>
<p>Contraindications/Precautions</p>
<ul>
<li>Lithium is Pregnancy Risk Category D. This medication is teratogenic, especially during the first trimester.</li>
<li>Discourage clients from breastfeeding if lithium therapy is necessary.</li>
<li>Use cautiously in clients with renal dysfunction, heart disease, sodium depletion, and dehydration</li>
</ul>
<p>Medication/Food Interactions</p>
<ul>
<li>Sodium is excreted with the use of diuretics. Reduced serum sodium decreases lithium excretion, which can lead to toxicity.</li>
<li>Concurrent use of NSAIDs (ibuprofen [Motrin] and celecoxib [Celebrex]) will increase renal reabsorption of lithium, leading to toxicity.</li>
</ul>
<p>Avoid use of NSAIDs.</p>
<p>Use aspirin as a mild analgesic.</p>
<ul>
<li>Anticholinergics (antihistamines, tricyclic antidepressants) can induce urinary retention and polyuria, leading to abdominal discomfort</li>
<li>Advise clients to avoid medications with anticholinergic effects. rt.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-administration">Nursing Administration<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-administration" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Monitor plasma lithium levels while undergoing treatment. At initiation of treatment, monitor levels every 2 to 3 days and then every 1 to 3 months. Lithium blood levels should be obtained in the morning, usually 12 hr . after the last dose.</li>
<li>During initial treatment of a manic episode, levels should be between 0.8 to <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>1.4</mn><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">E</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">q</mi></mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">/</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">L</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">1.4 \mathrm{mEq} / \mathrm{L}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mord">1.4</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">mEq</span></span><span class="mord">/</span><span class="mord mathrm">L</span></span></span></span></span>.</li>
<li>Maintenance level range is between 0.4 to <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>1.0</mn><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">E</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">q</mi></mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">/</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">L</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">1.0 \mathrm{mEq} / \mathrm{L}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mord">1.0</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">mEq</span></span><span class="mord">/</span><span class="mord mathrm">L</span></span></span></span></span>.</li>
<li>Plasma levels &gt; <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>1.5</mn><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">E</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">q</mi></mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">/</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">L</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">1.5 \mathrm{mEq} / \mathrm{L}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mord">1.5</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">mEq</span></span><span class="mord">/</span><span class="mord mathrm">L</span></span></span></span></span> can result in toxicity.</li>
<li>Care for clients who have a toxic plasma lithium level in an inpatient setting and provide supportive measures. Hemodialysis may be indicated.</li>
<li>Advise clients that effects begin within 7 to 14 days.</li>
</ul>
<p>Nursing administration cont.â€™</p>
<ul>
<li>Advise clients to take lithium as prescribed. Lithium must be administered in 2 to 3 doses daily due to a short half life. Taking lithium with food will help decrease GI distress.</li>
<li>Encourage clients to adhere to laboratory appointments needed to monitor lithium effectiveness and adverse effects. Emphasize the high risk of toxicity due to the narrow therapeutic range.</li>
<li>Provide nutritional counseling. Stress the importance of adequate fluid and sodium intake.</li>
<li>Instruct clients to monitor for signs of toxicity and when to contact the provider. Clients should stop taking medication and seek medical attention if experiencing diarrhea, vomiting, or excessive sweating.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="other-mood-stabilizing-drugs">Other mood stabilizing drugs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#other-mood-stabilizing-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Carbamazepine (Tegretol)</li>
<li>Valproic acid (Depakote)</li>
<li>Lamotrigine (Lamictal) Purpose</li>
</ul>
<p>Expected Pharmacological Action: AEDs help treat and manage bipolar disorders by various mechanisms, which include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Slowing the entrance of sodium and calcium back into the neuron and, thus extending the time it takes for the nerve to return to its active state.</li>
<li>Potentiating the inhibitory effects of gamma butyric acid (GABA)</li>
<li>Inhibiting glutamic acid (glutamate) which in turn suppresses CNS excitation</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="therapeutic-uses">Therapeutic Uses<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#therapeutic-uses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Treatment of manic and depressive episodes, prevention of relapse of mania and depressive episodes.</li>
<li>Especially useful for clients with mixed mania and rapid cycling bipolar disorders.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cns-stimulants">CNS STIMULANTS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cns-stimulants" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>MEDICATION</th><th>SHORT ACTING</th><th>INTERMEDIATE ACTING</th><th>LONG ACTING</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Methylphenidate</td><td>Ritalin, Methylin</td><td>Ritalin SR, Methylin ER</td><td>ethylin ER Ritalin LA,</td></tr><tr><td>Concerta, Daytrana</td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>(transdermal)</td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Dexmethylphenidate</td><td>Focalin</td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Dextroamphetamine</td><td>Dexedrine</td><td></td><td>Dexedrine Spansule</td></tr><tr><td>Amphetamine mixture</td><td>Adderall</td><td></td><td>Adderall-XR</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cns-stimulants-cont">CNS stimulants cont.'<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cns-stimulants-cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="expected-pharmacological-action">Expected Pharmacological Action :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#expected-pharmacological-action" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>These medications raise the levels of norepinephrine, serotonin, and dopamine into the CNS.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="therapeutic-uses">Therapeutic Uses:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#therapeutic-uses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>ADHD ( Attention Deficit Hyperactivity Disorder)</li>
<li>Conduct disorder</li>
</ul>
<p>Side effects</p>
<ul>
<li>CNS stimulation (insomnia, restlessness)</li>
<li>Weight loss</li>
<li>Cardiovascular effects (dysrhythmias, chest pain, high blood pressure)</li>
<li>These medications may increase the risk of sudden death in clients with heart abnormalities.</li>
<li>Development of psychotic symptoms such as hallucinations, paranoia Withdrawal reaction.</li>
<li>Hypersensitivity skin reaction to transdermal methylphenidate (hives, papules)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Contraindications/Precautions</p>
<ul>
<li>These medications are contraindicated in clients who have a history of drug abuse, cardiovascular disorders, severe anxiety, and psychosis.</li>
</ul>
<p>Medication/Food Interactions:</p>
<p>Concurrent use of MAOI s may cause hypertensive crisis.</p>
<p>Concurrent use of caffeine may increase CNS stimulant effects.</p>
<p>Methylphenidate inhibits metabolism of phenytoin (Dilantin), warfarin (Coumadin), and phenobarbital, leading to increased serum levels.</p>
<p>OTC cold and decongestant medications with sympathomimetic action can increase CNS stimulant effects.</p>
<p>Nursing Administration</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Advise clients to swallow sustained-release tablets whole and to not chew or crush the tablets.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Teach clients the importance of administering the medication on a regular schedule.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Teach clients who use transdermal medication (Daytrana) to place the patch on one hip daily in the morning and leave it in place no longer than 9 hr. Alternate hips daily.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Instruct parents and clients that ADHD is not cured by medication and should be managed with an overall treatment plan that may include family therapy and cognitive therapy.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Instruct parents that these medications have special handling procedures controlled by federal law. Handwritten prescriptions are required for medication refills.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Instruct parents in safety and storage of medications.</p>
</li>
<li></li>
</ul>
<p>MUSCLE RELAXANT/NEUROMUSCULAR BLOCKING AGENTS</p>
<p>â€¢ Neuromuscular blocking agents have various uses including assisting with:</p>
<p>âœ“ sedation during general anesthesia,</p>
<p>âœ“ control of seizures during electroconvulsive therapy,</p>
<p>âœ“ suppression of gag reflex during endotracheal intubation.</p>
<p>â€¢ Medications include succinylcholine (Anectine) and vecuronium (Norcuron)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="anti-parkinson-s-drugs">Anti -Parkinson's drugs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#anti-parkinson-s-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Neuromuscular agents cont.'</p>
<p>Muscle relaxants and antispasmodic agents can affect both the central and peripheral nervous systems.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>These agents are used with spasticity related to muscle injury, cerebral palsy, spinal cord injury, and multiple sclerosis.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Agents include diazepam (Valium), baclofen (Lioresal), and dantrolene (Dantrium).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Bethanechol (Urecholine), a muscarinic agonist, is used for urinary retention.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Oxybutynin (Ditropan), a muscarinic antagonist, is used for neurogenic bladder</p>
</li>
<li></li>
</ul>
<p>Muscle relaxant/ Neuromuscular Blocking Agents cont.â€™</p>
<p>Depolarizing neuromuscular blocker: succinylcholine (Anectine)</p>
<p>Nondepolarizing neuromuscular blockers: pancuronium (Pavulon)</p>
<p>Other Medications:</p>
<p>Nondepolarizing neuromuscular blockers: atracurium (Tracrium), Vecuronium (Norcuron)</p>
<p>Expected Pharmacological Action</p>
<p>Neuromuscular blocking agents block acetylcholine (ACh) at the neuromuscular junction, resulting in muscle relaxation and hypotension. They do not cross the blood-brain barrier, so complete paralysis can be achieved without loss of consciousness or decreased pain sensation.</p>
<p>Neuromuscular agents cont.'</p>
<p>Therapeutic Uses</p>
<p>â€¢ Neuromuscular blocking agents are used as adjuncts to general anesthesia to promote muscle relaxation.</p>
<p>â€¢ These agents are used to control spontaneous respiratory movements in clients receiving mechanical ventilation.</p>
<p>â€¢ These agents are used as seizure control during electroconvulsive therapy.</p>
<p>â€¢ Neuromuscular blocking agents are used during endotracheal intubation and endoscopy</p>
<p>Side effect</p>
<ul>
<li>Respiratory arrest from paralyzed respiratory muscles</li>
<li>Hypotension</li>
<li>Low pseudo cholinesterase activity can lead to prolonged apnea</li>
<li>Signs of malignant hyperthermia include muscle rigidity accompanied by increased temperature, reaching levels as high as 43Â° C (109.4Â° F).</li>
<li>After 12 to 24 hr. postoperative, clients may experience muscle pain in the upper body and back.</li>
<li>Hyperkalemia</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Drug interaction</p>
<p>General anesthetics are often used concurrently in surgery.</p>
<p>â€¢ Dosage of tubocurarine should be reduced to prevent extreme neuromuscular blockade.</p>
<p>Aminoglycosides and tetracyclines can increase the effects of neuromuscular blockade.</p>
<p>â€¢ Take complete medication history of clients who are to receive neuromuscular blockade.</p>
<p>Neostigmine and other cholinesterase inhibitors increase the effects of depolarizing neuromuscular blockers, such as succinylcholine.</p>
<p>â€¢ Monitor clients during neuromuscular blockade reversal after surgery</p>
<p>Nursing Administration</p>
<ul>
<li>Clients must receive continuous cardiac and respiratory monitoring during therapy.</li>
<li>Monitor clients for respiratory depression and have life support equipment available.</li>
<li>Carefully monitor clients for return of respiratory function.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="local-anaesthetics">LOCAL ANAESTHETICS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#local-anaesthetics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>local anesthetic bind reversibly to a specific receptor site within the pore of the sodium channels in nerves and block ion movement when applied locally to nerve tissues in appropriate concentration.</li>
<li>Local anesthetic can act on any part of the nervous system, on every type of nerve fibers, reversibly blocking the action potentials responsible for nerve conduction.</li>
<li>Thus a local anesthetic in contact with a nerve trunk can cause both sensory and motor paralysis in the area innervated.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mechanism-of-action">Mechanism of action<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mechanism-of-action" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Local anesthetic block conduction by decreasing or preventing the large transient increase in the permeability of excitable membranes.</li>
<li>This action is due to direct interaction with voltage gated sodium channels.</li>
<li>As the anesthetic action progressively develops in the nerve ,the threshold for electrical excitability increase. The rate of rise of the action potential also declines, impulse conduction slows, and nerve conduction eventually fails</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="local-anesthetics">Local anesthetics<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#local-anesthetics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
